test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_000.jpg	While the threats that trigger this response in prehistory were physical, like
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_001.jpg	something that could eat us, these days the triggers are psychological—an angry
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_002.jpg	spouse, a snarky tweet. Yet the body’s reactions are the same, including emotional
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_003.jpg	upset. Human skin has an unusually large number of nerve endings (about five
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_004.jpg	hundred per square inch), each a pathway for the brain to send signals for what’s
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_005.jpg	called “neurogenic,” or brain-caused, inflammation. Skin specialists have long
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_006.jpg	observed that life’s stress can cause neurogenic flare-ups of inflammatory
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_007.jpg	disorders like psoriasis and eczema.
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_008.jpg	This makes the skin an appealing lab for studying how upsets impact our health.
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_009.jpg	Turns out the nerve pathways that let the brain signal the skin to inflame are
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_010.jpg	sensitive to capsaicin, the chemical that makes chilies “hot.” Richie’s lab used this
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_011.jpg	novel fact to create carefully controlled patches of inflammation, to see how stress
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_012.jpg	would increase, or meditation muffle, this reaction. Meanwhile, Melissa Rosenkranz,
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_013.jpg	a scientist in the lab, invented a clever way to assay the chemicals that induce
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_014.jpg	inflammation, by creating artificial (and painless) blisters in the inflamed area that
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_015.jpg	would fill with fluid.
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_016.jpg	The blisters were created in a contraption Melissa built that uses a vacuum system
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_017.jpg	to raise the first layer of skin in small circular areas over the course of forty-five
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_018.jpg	minutes. When done slowly the method is quite painless, hardly noticed by the
test/images/synth_doc_00004_line_019.jpg	participants.
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_000.jpg	More generally, if the generator is rendering artificially designed images, such as a
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_001.jpg	cartoon, or music played from a written composition, the accuracy is the closeness
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_002.jpg	of the rendered images to the intended ones. By ‘closeness’ we meancloseness as
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_003.jpg	perceived by the user. If the rendering is so close as to be indistinguishable by the
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_004.jpg	user from what is intended, then we can call it perfectly accurate. (So a rendering
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_005.jpg	that is perfectly accurate for one user may contain inaccuracies that are
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_006.jpg	perceptible to a user with sharper senses, or with additional senses.
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_007.jpg	A universal image generator does not of course contain recordings of all possible
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_008.jpg	images. What makes it universal is that, given a recording of any possible image, it
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_009.jpg	can evoke the corresponding sensation in the user. With a universal auditory
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_010.jpg	sensation generator — the ultimate hi-fi system — the recording might be given in
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_011.jpg	the form of a compact disc. To accommodate auditory sensations that last longer
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_012.jpg	than the disc’s storage capacity allows, we must incorporate a mechanism that can
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_013.jpg	feed any number of discs consecutively into the machine.
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_014.jpg	The same proviso holds for all other universal image generators, for strictly
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_015.jpg	speaking an image generator is not universal unless it includes a mechanism for
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_016.jpg	playing recordings of unlimited duration. Furthermore, when the machine has been
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_017.jpg	playing for a long time it will require maintenance, otherwise the images it
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_018.jpg	generates will become degraded or may cease altogether.
test/images/synth_doc_00003_line_019.jpg	These and similar considerations are all connected with the fact that considering a
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_000.jpg	On your last morning, we’ll compare notes and try to integrate and make sense of
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_001.jpg	your experience. Then I’ll cook you a big breakfast to get you ready to face the
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_002.jpg	interstate!” We scheduled a time for me to come back. • • •THE FIRST THING I
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_003.jpg	learned about myself that first afternoon, working with Fritz in the yurt, is that I am
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_004.jpg	“easy to put under”—susceptible to trance, a mental space completely new to me
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_005.jpg	and accessible by nothing more than a shift in the pattern of one’s breathing. It was
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_006.jpg	the damnedest thing. Fritz’s instructions were straightforward: Breathe deeply and
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_007.jpg	rapidly while exhaling as strongly as you can. “At first it will feel unnatural and you’ll
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_008.jpg	have to concentrate to maintain the rhythm, but after a few minutes your body will
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_009.jpg	take over and do it automatically.” I stretched out on the mattress and donned a
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_010.jpg	pair of eyeshades while he put on some music, something generically tribal and
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_011.jpg	rhythmic, dominated by the pounding of a drum.
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_012.jpg	He placed a plastic bucket at my side, explaining that occasionally people throw
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_013.jpg	up. It was hard work at first, to breathe in such an exaggerated and unnatural way,
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_014.jpg	even with Fritz’s enthusiastic coaching, but then all at once my body took over, and
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_015.jpg	I found that no thought was required to maintain the driving pace and rhythm. It was
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_016.jpg	as if I had broken free from gravity and settled into an orbit: the big deep breaths
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_017.jpg	just came, automatically.
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_018.jpg	Now I felt an uncontrollable urge to move my legs and arms in sync with the
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_019.jpg	pounding of the drums, which resonated in my rib cage like a powerful new
test/images/synth_doc_00007_line_020.jpg	heartbeat. I felt possessed, both my body and my mind. I can’t remember many
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_000.jpg	Then there are the many Tibetan yogis who traveled far to be studied in Richie’s
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_001.jpg	lab, as well as the Western retreatants from their center in Dordogne, France. We
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_002.jpg	are deeply indebted to Matthieu Ricard, who bridged the worlds of science and
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_003.jpg	contemplation, making this line of research possible. The scientists who have
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_004.jpg	contributed their studies to the ever-building mass of contemplative research are
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_005.jpg	too numerous to name, but we are grateful for their scientific work. Special thanks
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_006.jpg	to those at Richie’s lab, notably Antoine Lutz, Cortland Dahl, John Dunne, Melissa
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_007.jpg	Rosenkranz, Heleen Slagter, Helen Weng, and many others too numerous to list
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_008.jpg	who together contributed enormously to this work. The work in Richie’s center
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_009.jpg	would not be possible without the tireless contributions of the extraordinary
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_010.jpg	administrative staff and leadership, especially Isa Dolski, Susan Jensen, and Barb
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_011.jpg	Mathison.
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_012.jpg	Among the many friends and colleagues who have made insightful suggestions
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_013.jpg	along the way, we thank Jack Kornfield, Joseph Goldstein, Dawa Tarchin Phillips,
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_014.jpg	Tania Singer, Avideh Shashaani, Sharon Salzberg, Mirabhai Bush, and Larry
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_015.jpg	Brilliant, to mention a few. And of course we could not have written this book
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_016.jpg	without the loving support and encouragement of our wives, Susan and Tara. Our
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_017.jpg	biggest debt of gratitude goes to His Holiness the Dalai Lama, who both inspired
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_018.jpg	us by his very being and also pointedly suggested how meditation research could
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_019.jpg	bring the value of these practices to the widest number of people.Notes CHAPTER
test/images/synth_doc_00002_line_020.jpg	ONE. THE DEEP PATH AND THE WIDE 1.
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_000.jpg	Richie’s dissertation study, like Dan’s, was slightly suggestive of the effect he was
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_001.jpg	seeking to find. Fast-forward several decades to far more sophisticated measures
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_002.jpg	of the well-targeted sensory awareness Richie had tried to demonstrate.
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_003.jpg	A group at MIT deployed MEG—a magnetic EEG measure with a much more
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_004.jpg	precise targeting of brain areas than Richie’s old-time EEG had allowed—with
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_005.jpg	volunteers who had been randomly assigned to either get an eight-week program
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_006.jpg	in MBSR, or who waited to get the training until after the experiment was done.6
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_007.jpg	MBSR, remember, includes mindfulness of breath, practicing a systematic scan of
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_008.jpg	sensations throughout your body, attentive yoga, and moment-to- moment
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_009.jpg	awareness of thoughts and feelings—with the invitation to practice these attention
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_010.jpg	training methods daily. After eight weeks those who had gone through the MBSR
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_011.jpg	program showed a far better ability to focus on sensations— in this case a carefully
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_012.jpg	calibrated tapping on their hand or foot—than they had done before starting the
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_013.jpg	MBSR training, as well as better than those who were still waiting for MBSR.
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_014.jpg	Conclusion: mindfulness (at least in this form) strengthens the brain’s ability to
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_015.jpg	focus on one thing and ignore distractions. The neural circuitry for selective
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_016.jpg	attention, the study concluded, can be trained—contrary to the standard wisdom
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_017.jpg	where attention was assumed to be hardwired and so, beyond the reach of any
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_018.jpg	training attempt.A similar strengthening of selective attention was found in
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_019.jpg	vipassana meditators at the Insight Meditation Society who were tested before and
test/images/synth_doc_00008_line_020.jpg	after a three-month retreat.7 The retreat offered what amounts to explicit
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_000.jpg	Many but not all Psilocybes sport a “pellicle”—a condom-like layer of gelatinous
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_001.jpg	material covering the cap that can be peeled off. My fungal vocabulary might be
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_002.jpg	expanding, but my confidence was rapidly collapsing, much like the mushroom
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_003.jpg	that, in the course of a single day, decomposes into an inky puddle. By the time I
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_004.jpg	got to chapter four, “The Dangers of Mistaken Identification,” I was ready to throw in
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_005.jpg	the towel. “Mistakes in mushroom identification can be lethal,” Stamets begins,
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_006.jpg	before displaying a photograph in which a Psilocybe stuntzii is seen growing cheek
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_007.jpg	by jowl with a trio of indistinguishable Galerina autumnalis, an unremarkable little
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_008.jpg	mushroom that, when eaten, “can result in an agonizing death.”But while Stamets
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_009.jpg	urges extreme circumspection in amateurs hoping to identify Psilocybes, he also
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_010.jpg	equips the mushroom hunter who hasn’t been completely discouraged with
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_011.jpg	something he calls “The Stametsian Rule”: a three-pronged test that, he (sort of)
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_012.jpg	assures us, can head off death and disaster. “How do I know if a mushroom is a
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_013.jpg	psilocybin producing species or not?” “If a gilled mushroom has purplish brown to
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_014.jpg	black spores, and the flesh bruises bluish, the mushroom in question is very likely a
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_015.jpg	psilocybin- producing species.” This is definitely a big help, though I wouldn’t mind
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_016.jpg	something more categorical than “very likely.” He then offers a sobering caveat. “I
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_017.jpg	know of no exceptions to this rule,” he adds, “but that does not mean there are
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_018.jpg	none!” After committing to memory the Stametsian Rule, I began picking
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_019.jpg	promising-looking gilled LBMs—in my neighbors’ yards, on my walk to work, in the
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_020.jpg	parking lot of the bank—and then roughing them up a bit to see if they would turn
test/images/synth_doc_00006_line_021.jpg	black and blue.
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_000.jpg	Admission by consent of the instructor. “Experimental Expansion of
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_001.jpg	Consciousness” proved to be extremely popular. • • • IN ITS THREE YEARS of
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_002.jpg	existence, the Harvard Psilocybin Project accomplished surprisingly little, at least in
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_003.jpg	terms of science. In their first experiments, Leary and Alpert administered
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_004.jpg	psilocybin to hundreds of people of all sorts, including housewives, musicians,
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_005.jpg	artists, academics, writers, fellow psychologists, and graduate students, who then
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_006.jpg	completed questionnaires about their experiences.
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_007.jpg	According to “Americans and Mushrooms in a Naturalistic Environment: A
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_008.jpg	Preliminary Report,” most subjects had generally very positive and occasionally
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_009.jpg	life-changing experiences. “Naturalistic” was apt: these sessions took place not in
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_010.jpg	university buildings but in comfortable living rooms, accompanied by music and
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_011.jpg	candlelight, and to a casual observer they would have looked more like parties than
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_012.jpg	experiments, especially because the researchers themselves usually joined in.
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_013.jpg	(Leary and Alpert took a heroic amount of psilocybin and, later, LSD. At least in the
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_014.jpg	beginning, Leary, Alpert, and their graduate students endeavored to write up
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_015.jpg	accounts of their own and their subjects’ psilocybin journeys, as if they were
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_016.jpg	pioneers exploring an unmapped frontier of consciousness and the previous
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_017.jpg	decade of work surveying the psychedelic landscape had never happened. “We
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_018.jpg	were on our own,” Leary wrote, somewhat disingenuously. “Western literature had
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_019.jpg	almost no guides, no maps, no texts that even recognized the existence of altered
test/images/synth_doc_00001_line_020.jpg	states.” Drawing on their extensive fieldwork, however, Leary did do some original
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_000.jpg	One of the great appeals of high-risk sports like rock climbing seems to be just
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_001.jpg	that— the danger of the sport demands a full focus on where to put your hand or
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_002.jpg	foot next. More mundane worries take backstage in the mind. The same applies to
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_003.jpg	“flow,” the state where people perform at their best.
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_004.jpg	Paying full attention to what’s at hand, flow research tells us, rates high on the list of
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_005.jpg	what puts us into—and sustains—a joyous state. The self, in its form as
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_006.jpg	mind-wandering, becomes a distraction, suppressed for the time being. Managing
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_007.jpg	attention, as we saw in the previous chapter, is an essential ingredient of every
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_008.jpg	variety of meditation.
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_009.jpg	When we become lost in thoughts during meditation, we’ve fallen into the default
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_010.jpg	mode and its wandering mind. A basic instruction in almost all forms of meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_011.jpg	urges us to notice when our mind has wandered and then return our focus to the
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_012.jpg	chosen target, say, a mantra or our breathing. This moment has universal familiarity
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_013.jpg	on contemplative paths.
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_014.jpg	This simple mental move has a neural correlate: activating the connection between
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_015.jpg	the dorsolateral PFC and the default mode—a connection found to be stronger in
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_016.jpg	long-term meditators than in beginners.3 The stronger this connection, the more
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_017.jpg	likely regulatory circuits in the prefrontal cortex inhibit thedefault areas, quieting the
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_018.jpg	monkey mind—the incessant self-focused chatter that so often fills our minds when
test/images/synth_doc_00005_line_019.jpg	nothing else is pressing. A Sufi poem hints at this shift, speaking of the shift from “a
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_000.jpg	Beginning in the 1990s, well out of view of most of us, a small group of scientists,
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_001.jpg	psychotherapists, and so-called psychonauts, believing that something precious
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_002.jpg	had been lost from both science and culture, resolved to recover it. Today, after
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_003.jpg	several decades of suppression and neglect, psychedelics are having a
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_004.jpg	renaissance. A new generation of scientists, many of them inspired by their own
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_005.jpg	personal experience of the compounds, are testing their potential to heal mental
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_006.jpg	illnesses such as depression, anxiety, trauma, and addiction. Other scientists are
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_007.jpg	using psychedelics in conjunction with new brain-imaging tools to explore the links
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_008.jpg	between brain and mind, hoping to unravel some of the mysteries of
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_009.jpg	consciousness.
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_010.jpg	One good way to understand a complex system is to disturb it and then see what
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_011.jpg	happens. By smashing atoms, a particle accelerator forces them to yield their
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_012.jpg	secrets. By administering psychedelics in carefully calibrated doses,
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_013.jpg	neuroscientists can profoundly disturb the normal waking consciousness of
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_014.jpg	volunteers, dissolving the structures of the self and occasioning what can be
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_015.jpg	described as a mystical experience.
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_016.jpg	While this is happening, imaging tools can observe the changes in the brain’s
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_017.jpg	activity and patterns of connection. Already this work is yielding surprising insights
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_018.jpg	into the “neural correlates” of the sense of self and spiritual experience.
test/images/synth_doc_00009_line_019.jpg	The hoary 1960s platitude that psychedelics offered a key to understanding—and
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_000.jpg	DAVID: I neither know nor care. The reverence that philosophers show for the
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_001.jpg	historical sources of ideas is very perverse, you know. In science we do not
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_002.jpg	consider the discoverer of a theory to have any special insight into it.
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_003.jpg	On the contrary, we hardly ever consult original sources. They invariably become
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_004.jpg	obsolete, as the problem-situations that prompted them are transformed by the
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_005.jpg	discoveries themselves.
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_006.jpg	For example, most relativity theorists today understand Einstein’s theory better than
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_007.jpg	he did. The founders of quantum theory made a complete mess of understanding
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_008.jpg	their own theory.
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_009.jpg	Such shaky beginnings are to be expected; and when we stand upon the shoulders
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_010.jpg	of giants, it may not be all that hard to see further than they did. But in any case,
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_011.jpg	surely it is more interesting to argue about what the truth is, than about what some
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_012.jpg	particular thinker, however great, did or did not think. CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: All
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_013.jpg	right, I agree. But wait a moment, I think I spoke too soon when I said that you were
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_014.jpg	not postulating any sort of principle of induction. Look: you have justified a theory
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_015.jpg	about the future (the prevailing theory of gravity) as being more reliable than
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_016.jpg	another theory (the one I proposed), even though they are both consistent with all
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_017.jpg	currently known observations.
test/images/synth_doc_00014_line_018.jpg	Since the prevailing theory applies both to the future and to the past, you have
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_000.jpg	The retreat was a high for Richie. He came away with a deep conviction that there
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_001.jpg	were methods that could transform our minds to produce a profound well- being.
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_002.jpg	We did not have to be controlled by the mind, with its random associations, sudden
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_003.jpg	fears and angers, and all the rest—we could take back the helm.
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_004.jpg	For days after the retreat ended, Richie still felt he was on a high. Richie’s mind
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_005.jpg	kept soaring while he and Susan stayed on in Dalhousie. The high rode with him on
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_006.jpg	the bus down the mountains via roads wending through fields and villages with
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_007.jpg	mud-walled, thatch-roofed houses, on to the busier cities of the plains, and finally
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_008.jpg	through the throbbing, packed roads of Delhi.plains, and finally through the
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_009.jpg	throbbing, packed roads of Delhi. There Richie felt that high begin to wane as he
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_010.jpg	and Susan spent a few days in the bare-bones guesthouse they could afford on
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_011.jpg	their grad student budget, venturing out to Delhi’s cacophonous and crowded
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_012.jpg	streets to have a tailor make some clothes and buy souvenirs.
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_013.jpg	Perhaps the biggest force in the decline of that meditation state was the traveler’s
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_014.jpg	stomach they both had come down with. That malady plagued them through a
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_015.jpg	change of planes in Frankfurt on the cheap flight from Delhi to Kennedy Airport.
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_016.jpg	After a full day spent in travel they landed in New York, where they were greeted by
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_017.jpg	both sets of parents, eager to see them after this summer away in Asia. As Susan
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_018.jpg	and Richie exited Customs—sick, tired, and dressed in the Indian style of the
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_019.jpg	day—their families greeted them with looks of horrified shock. Instead of
test/images/synth_doc_00011_line_020.jpg	enveloping them in love, they yelled in alarm, “What have you done to yourselves?
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_000.jpg	But Dr Johnson’s idea is more than a refutation of solipsism. It also illustrates the
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_001.jpg	criterion for reality that is used in science, namely, if something can kick back, it
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_002.jpg	exists. ‘Kicking back’ here does not necessarily mean that the alleged object is
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_003.jpg	responding to being kicked — to being physically affected as Dr Johnson’s rock
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_005.jpg	It is enough that when we ‘kick’ something, the object affects us in ways that
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_006.jpg	require independent explanation. For example, Galileo had no means of affecting
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_007.jpg	planets, but he could affect the light that came from them. His equivalent of kicking
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_008.jpg	the rock was refracting that light through the lenses of his telescopes and eyes.
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_009.jpg	That light responded by ‘kicking’ his retina back. The way it kicked back allowed
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_010.jpg	him to conclude not only that the light was real, but that the heliocentric planetary
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_011.jpg	motions required to explain the patterns in which the light arrivedwere also real. By
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_012.jpg	the way, Dr Johnson did not directly kick the rock either.
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_013.jpg	A person is a mind, not a body. The Dr Johnson who performed the experiment was
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_014.jpg	a mind, and that mind directly ‘kicked’ only some nerves, which transmitted signals
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_015.jpg	to muscles, which propelled his foot towards the rock.
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_016.jpg	Shortly afterwards, Dr Johnson perceived being ‘kicked back’ by the rock, but
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_017.jpg	again only indirectly, after the impact had set up a pressure pattern in his shoe, and
test/images/synth_doc_00012_line_018.jpg	then in his skin, and had then led to electrical impulses in his nerves, and so forth.
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_000.jpg	I was curious to find out how Stamets came by his mycocentric worldview and what
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_001.jpg	role psilocybin mushrooms, in particular, might have contributed to it. Stamets grew
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_002.jpg	up in an Ohio town outside Youngstown called Columbiana, the youngest of five
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_003.jpg	children. His father’s engineering company went belly-up when Paul was a boy, the
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_004.jpg	family “going from riches to rags pretty quickly.” Dad began to drink heavily, and
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_005.jpg	Paul began looking up to his older brother John as a role model.Five years his
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_006.jpg	senior, John was an aspiring scientist—he would receive a scholarship to study
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_007.jpg	neurophysiology—who kept “an exquisite laboratory in the basement,” a realm that
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_008.jpg	was Paul’s idea of heaven, but to which John seldom granted his little brother
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_009.jpg	admittance. “I thought all houses had laboratories, so whenever I went over to a
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_010.jpg	friend’s house, I would ask where the laboratory was.
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_011.jpg	I didn’t understand why they would always point me to the bathroom instead—the
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_012.jpg	lavatory.” Winning John’s approval became a motive force in Paul’s life, which
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_013.jpg	perhaps explains the value Stamets places on mainstream scientific recognition of
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_014.jpg	work. John had died, of a heart attack, six months before my visit and, as it
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_015.jpg	happened, on the same day Paul received word of his AAAS honor.
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_016.jpg	His death was a loss from which Paul hadn’t yet recovered. When Paul was
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_017.jpg	fourteen, John told him about magic mushrooms, and when he went off to Yale,
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_018.jpg	John left behind a book, Altered States of Consciousness, that made a tremendous
test/images/synth_doc_00010_line_019.jpg	impression on Paul.
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_000.jpg	Nothing can move along the line. Time cannot flow. The idea of the flow of time
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_001.jpg	really presupposes the existence of a second sort of time, outside the
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_002.jpg	common-sense sequence-of-moments time.
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_003.jpg	If ‘now’ really moved from one of the moments to another, it would have to be with
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_004.jpg	respect to this exterior time. But taking that seriously leads to an infinite regress, for
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_005.jpg	we should then have to imagine the exterior time itself as a succession of moments,
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_006.jpg	with its own ‘present moment’ that was moving with respect to a still more exterior
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_007.jpg	time — and so on. At each stage, the flow of time would not make sense unless we
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_008.jpg	attributed it to the flow of an exterior time, ad infinitum. At each stage, we would
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_009.jpg	have a concept that made no sense; and the whole infinite hierarchy would make
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_010.jpg	no sense either.The origin of this sort of mistake is that we are accustomed to time
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_011.jpg	being a framework exterior to any physical entity we may be considering.
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_012.jpg	We are used to imagining any physical object as potentially changing, and so
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_013.jpg	existing as a sequence of versions of itself at different moments. But the sequence
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_014.jpg	of moments itself, in pictures like Figures 11.1—11.3, is an exceptional entity. It
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_015.jpg	does not exist within the framework of time — it is the framework of time. Since
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_016.jpg	there is no time outside it, it is incoherent to imagine it changing or existing in more
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_017.jpg	than one consecutive version. This makes such pictures hard to grasp.
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_018.jpg	The picture itself, like any other physical object, does exist over a period of time
test/images/synth_doc_00013_line_019.jpg	and does consist of multiple versions of itself. But what the picture depicts —
test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_000.jpg	At one time or another, he also worked for the Canadian Special Services, the U.S.
test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_001.jpg	Department of Justice, and the Food and Drug Administration.
test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_002.jpg	His FBI file suggests he had links to the CIA during the 1950s, but the redactions
test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_003.jpg	are too heavy for it to reveal much about his role, if any. We know the government
test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_004.jpg	kept close tabs on the psychedelic research community all through the 1950s,

test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_016.jpg	coming soon, and that he could play a role in it if he wanted to. But he hadn’t the

test/images/synth_doc_00016_line_019.jpg	newly discovered compound called LSD.
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_000.jpg	We can only speculate, but quite possibly we would see the same quieting of the
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_001.jpg	default mode network Brewer and Carhart-Harris have found. This quieting might
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_002.jpg	be accomplished by restricting blood flow to the network, or by stimulating the

test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_007.jpg	having a physical cause. • • • IF THE DEFAULT MODE network is the conductor of
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_008.jpg	the symphony of brain activity, you would expect its temporary absence from the
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_009.jpg	stage to lead to an increase in dissonance and mental disorder—as indeed
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_010.jpg	appears to happen during the psychedelic journey. In a series of subsequent
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_011.jpg	experiments using a variety of brain-imaging techniques, Carhart-Harris and his
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_012.jpg	colleagues began to study what happens elsewhere in the neural orchestra when
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_013.jpg	the default mode network puts down its baton. Taken as a whole, the default mode
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_014.jpg	network exerts an inhibitory influence on other parts of the brain, notably including
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_015.jpg	the limbic regions involved in emotion and memory, in much the same way Freud
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_016.jpg	conceived of the ego keeping the anarchic forces of the unconscious id in
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_017.jpg	check.(David Nutt puts the matter bluntly, claiming that in the DMN “we’ve found
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_018.jpg	the neural correlate for repression.”) Carhart-Harris hypothesizes that these and
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_019.jpg	other centers of mental activity are “let off the leash” when the default mode leaves
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_020.jpg	the stage, and in fact brain scans show an increase in activity (as reflected by
test/images/synth_doc_00015_line_021.jpg	increases in blood flow and oxygen consumption) in several other brain regions,
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_000.jpg	The laws of biology, say, are high-level, emergent consequences of the laws of
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_001.jpg	physics. But logically, some of the laws of physics are then ‘emergent’
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_002.jpg	consequences of the laws of biology. It could even be that, between them, the laws
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_003.jpg	governing biological and other emergent phenomena would entirely determine the
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_004.jpg	laws of fundamental physics. But in any case, when two theories are logically
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_005.jpg	related, logic does not dictate which of them we ought to regard as determining,
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_006.jpg	wholly or partly, the other. That depends on the explanatory relationships between
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_007.jpg	the theories.
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_008.jpg	The truly privileged theories are not the ones referring to any particular scale of size
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_009.jpg	or complexity, nor the ones situated at any particular level of the predictive
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_010.jpg	hierarchy — but the ones that contain the deepest explanations. The fabric of
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_011.jpg	reality does not consist only of reductionist ingredients like space, time and
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_012.jpg	subatomic particles, but also of life, thought, computation and the other things to
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_013.jpg	which those explanations refer. What makes a theory more fundamental, and less
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_014.jpg	derivative, is not its closeness to the supposed predictive base of physics, but its
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_015.jpg	closeness to our deepest explanatory theories. Quantum theory is, as I have said,
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_016.jpg	one such theory. But the other three main strands of explanation through which we
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_017.jpg	seek to understand the fabric of reality are all ‘high level’ from the point of view of
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_018.jpg	quantum physics.
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_019.jpg	They are the theory of evolution (primarily the evolution of living organisms),
test/images/synth_doc_00017_line_020.jpg	epistemology (the theory of knowledge) and the theory of computation (about
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_000.jpg	She started to meditate, and began to do research on how the method might
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_001.jpg	impact attention. But she got pushback from her colleagues, who cautioned her
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_002.jpg	that it was too risky and might not be of broad scientific interest within the field of
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_003.jpg	psychology.
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_004.jpg	The next year she attended the second meeting of the Mind and Life Summer
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_005.jpg	Research Institute, which proved transformative. The faculty, graduate students,
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_006.jpg	and postdocs she met there were a supportive community, who encouraged

test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_008.jpg	meeting about how meditation was part of her root culture.
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_009.jpg	While she had felt constrained in pursuing such research in the academy, she felt
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_010.jpg	she finally found her home with like-minded scientists doing research in this area.
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_011.jpg	Amishi has become a leader of a new generation of scientists committed to
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_012.jpg	contemplative neuroscience and its benefits for society. She and her colleagues
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_013.jpg	conducted one of the first rigorous studies of how meditation impacts attention.5
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_014.jpg	Her lab, now based at the University of Miami, found that novices trained in MBSR
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_015.jpg	significantly improved in orienting, a component of selective attention that directs
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_016.jpg	the mind to target one among the virtually infinite array of sensory inputs. Let’s say
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_017.jpg	you are at a party listening to the music, and tuning out a conversation going on
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_018.jpg	right next to you. If someone were to ask you what they had just said, you’d have no
test/images/synth_doc_00018_line_019.jpg	idea.
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_000.jpg	This all seems fine at first glance. Such a measure of mindfulness should and does
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_001.jpg	correlate with people’s progress in training programs like MBSR, and the test
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_002.jpg	scores correlated with the amount and quality of mindfulness practice itself.19
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_003.jpg	From a technical viewpoint that’s very good— it’s called “construct validity” in the
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_004.jpg	testing trade. But when Richie’s group put that measure to another technical test,
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_005.jpg	they found problems in “discriminant validity,” the ability of a measure not just to
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_006.jpg	correlate with what it should—like MBSR—but also not to correlate when it should
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_007.jpg	not. In this case, that test should not reflect the changes among those in the HEP
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_008.jpg	active control group, which was intentionally designed not to enhance mindfulness
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_009.jpg	in any way.
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_010.jpg	But the results from the HEP folks were pretty much like those from MBSR —an
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_011.jpg	uptick in mindfulness as assessed on the self-report test. More formally, there was
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_012.jpg	zero evidence that this measure had discriminant validity. Oops. Another widely
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_013.jpg	used self-report measure of mindfulness, in one study, showed a positive
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_014.jpg	correlation between binge drinking and mindfulness—the more drinking, the
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_015.jpg	greater the mindfulness.
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_016.jpg	Seems like something is off-base here!20 And a small study with twelve seasoned
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_017.jpg	(average of 5,800 hours of practice) and twelve more expert meditators (average of
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_018.jpg	11,000 hours of practice) found they did not differ from a nonmeditating group on
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_019.jpg	two very commonly used questionnaire measures of mindfulness, perhaps because
test/images/synth_doc_00019_line_020.jpg	they are more aware of the wanderings of their mind than most people.21 Any

test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_000.jpg	There are two theories in physics which are considerably deeper than all others.
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_001.jpg	The first is the general theory of relativity, which as I have said is our best theory of
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_002.jpg	space, time and gravity. The second, quantum theory, is even deeper.
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_003.jpg	Between them, these two theories (and not any existing or currently envisaged
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_004.jpg	theory of subatomic particles) provide the detailed explanatory and formal
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_005.jpg	framework within which all other theories in modern physics are expressed, and
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_006.jpg	they contain overarching physical principles to which all other theories conform. A
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_007.jpg	unification of general relativity and quantum theory — to give a quantum theory of
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_008.jpg	gravity — has been a major quest of theoretical physicists for several decades, and
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_009.jpg	would have to form part of any theory of everything in either the narrow or the broad
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_010.jpg	sense of the term. As we shall see in the next chapter, quantum theory, like
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_011.jpg	relativity, provides a revolutionary new mode of explanation of physical reality. The
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_012.jpg	reason why quantum theory is the deeper of the two lies more outside physics than
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_013.jpg	within it, for its ramifications are very wide, extending far beyond physics — and
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_014.jpg	even beyond science itself as it is normally conceived.
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_015.jpg	Quantum theory is one of what I shall call the four main strands of which our current
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_016.jpg	understanding of the fabric of reality is composed. Before I say what the other three
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_017.jpg	strands are, I must mention another way in which reductionism misrepresents the
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_018.jpg	structure of scientific knowledge. Not only does it assume that explanation always
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_019.jpg	consists of analysing a system into smaller, simpler systems, it also assumes that
test/images/synth_doc_00021_line_020.jpg	all explanation is of later events in terms of earlier events; in other words, that the
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_000.jpg	In a few applications, for instance weather forecasting, we may be almost as
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_001.jpg	satisfied with a purely predictive oracle as with an explanatory theory. But even
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_002.jpg	then, that would be strictly so only if the oracle’s weather forecast were complete
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_003.jpg	and perfect. In practice, weather forecasts are incomplete and imperfect, and to
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_004.jpg	make up for that they include explanations of how the forecasters arrived at their
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_005.jpg	predictions.
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_006.jpg	The explanations allow us to judge the reliability of a forecast and to deduce further
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_007.jpg	predictions relevant to our own location and needs. For instance, it makes a
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_008.jpg	difference to me whether today’s forecast that it will be windy tomorrow is based on
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_009.jpg	an expectation of a nearby high-pressure area, or of a more distant hurricane. I
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_010.jpg	would take more precautions in the latter case. Meteorologists themselves also
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_011.jpg	need explanatory theories about weather so that they can guess what
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_012.jpg	approximations it is safe to incorporate in their computer simulations of the weather,
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_013.jpg	what additional observations would allow the forecast to be more accurate and
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_014.jpg	more timely, and so on.
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_015.jpg	Thus the instrumentalist ideal epitomized by our imaginary oracle, namely a
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_016.jpg	scientific theory stripped of its explanatory content, would be of strictly limited
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_017.jpg	utility. Let us be thankful that real scientific theories do not resemble that ideal, and
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_018.jpg	that scientists in reality do not work towards that ideal.
test/images/synth_doc_00020_line_019.jpg	An extreme form of instrumentalism, called positivism (or logical positivism), holds
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_000.jpg	Shift how one thought about mortality? Actually change one’s mind in enduring
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_001.jpg	ways?
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_002.jpg	The idea took hold of me. It was a little like being shown a door in a familiar
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_003.jpg	room—the room of your own mind—that you had somehow never noticed before
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_004.jpg	and being told by people you trusted (scientists!) that a whole other way of
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_005.jpg	thinking—of being!—lay waiting on the other side.
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_006.jpg	All you had to do was turn the knob and enter. Who wouldn’t be curious? I might not
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_007.jpg	have been looking to change my life, but the idea of learning something new about
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_008.jpg	it, and of shining a fresh light on this old world, began to occupy my thoughts.
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_009.jpg	Maybe there was something missing from my life, something I just hadn’t named.
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_010.jpg	Now, I already knew something about such doors, having written about
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_011.jpg	psychoactive plants earlier in my career.
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_012.jpg	In The Botany of Desire, I explored at some length what I had been surprised to
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_013.jpg	discover is a universal human desire to change consciousness. There is not a
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_014.jpg	culture on earth (well, one*) that doesn’t make use of certain plants to change the
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_015.jpg	contents of the mind, whether as a matter of healing, habit, or spiritual practice.
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_016.jpg	That such a curious and seemingly maladaptive desire should exist alongside our
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_017.jpg	desires for nourishment and beauty and sex—all of which make much more
test/images/synth_doc_00023_line_018.jpg	obvious evolutionary sense—cried out for an explanation. The simplest was that
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_000.jpg	My lecture and the arguments it contains were not intended to persuade these
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_001.jpg	dream- people, but to persuade myself — to help me to clarify my ideas.’ However,
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_002.jpg	if there are sources of ideas that behave as if they were independent of oneself,
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_003.jpg	then they necessarily are independent of oneself. For if I define ‘myself as the
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_004.jpg	conscious entity that has the thoughts and feelings I am aware of having, then the
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_005.jpg	‘dream-people’ I seem to interact with are by definition something other than that
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_006.jpg	narrowly defined self, and so I must concede that something other than myself
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_007.jpg	exists. My only other option, if I were a committed solipsist, would be to regard the
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_008.jpg	dream-peopleas creations of my unconscious mind, and therefore as part of ‘myself
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_009.jpg	in a looser sense.
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_010.jpg	But then I should be forced to concede that ‘myself had a very rich structure, most
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_011.jpg	of which is independent of my conscious self. Within that structure are entities —
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_012.jpg	dream-people — who, despite being mere constituents of the mind of a supposed
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_013.jpg	solipsist, behave exactly as if they were committed anti-solipsists. So I could not
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_014.jpg	call myself wholly a solipsist, for only my narrowly defined self would take that view.
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_015.jpg	Many, apparently most, of the opinions held within my mind as a whole would
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_016.jpg	oppose solipsism.
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_017.jpg	I could study the ‘outer’ region of myself and find that it seems to obey certain laws,
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_018.jpg	the same laws as the dream-textbooks say apply to what they call the physical
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_019.jpg	universe. I would find that there is far more of the outer region than the inner region.
test/images/synth_doc_00022_line_020.jpg	Aside from containing more ideas, it is also more complex, more varied, and has
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_000.jpg	To generate the auditory image (i.e. the sound) of Mozart’s 20th piano concerto,
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_001.jpg	one plays the corresponding compact disc on the hi-fi system. Any image
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_002.jpg	generator is a rudimentary sort of virtual-reality generator, but the term ‘virtual
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_003.jpg	reality’ is usually reserved for cases where there is both a wide coverage of the
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_004.jpg	user’s sensory range, and a substantial element of interaction (‘kicking back’)
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_005.jpg	between the user and the simulated entities. Present-day video games do allow
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_006.jpg	interaction between the player and the game objects, but usually only a small
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_007.jpg	fraction of the user’s sensory range is covered. The rendered ‘environment’
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_008.jpg	consists of images on a small screen, and a proportion of the sounds that the user
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_009.jpg	hears.
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_010.jpg	But virtual-reality video games more worthy of the term do already exist. Typically,

test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_012.jpg	for each eye, and perhaps special gloves and other clothing lined with electrically
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_013.jpg	controlled effectors (pressure-generating devices). There are also sensors that
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_014.jpg	detect the motion of parts of the user’s body, especially the head.
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_015.jpg	The information about what the user is doing is passed to a computer, which
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_016.jpg	calculates what the user should be seeing, hearing and feeling, and responds by
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_017.jpg	sending appropriate signals to the image generators (Figure 5.1). When the user
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_018.jpg	looks to the left or right, the pictures on the two television screens pan, just as a real
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_019.jpg	field of view would, to show whatever is on the user’s left or right in the simulated
test/images/synth_doc_00025_line_020.jpg	world. The user can reach out and pick up a simulated object, and it feels real
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_000.jpg	One comparatively simple and comprehensible theory can cover an infinity of
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_001.jpg	indigestible facts. Our best theory of planetary motions is Einstein’s general theory
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_002.jpg	of relativity, which early in the twentieth century superseded Newton’s theories of
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_003.jpg	gravity and motion. It correctly predicts, in principle, not only all planetary motions
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_004.jpg	but also all other effects of gravity to the limits of accuracy of our best
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_005.jpg	measurements.
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_006.jpg	For a theory to predict something ‘in principle’ means that the predictions follow
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_007.jpg	logically from the theory, even if in practice the amount of computation that would
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_008.jpg	be needed to generate some of the predictions is too large to be technologically
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_009.jpg	feasible, or even too large for it to be physically possible for us to carry it out in the
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_010.jpg	universe as we find it. Being able to predict things or to describe them, however
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_011.jpg	accurately, is not at all the same thing as understanding them. Predictions and
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_012.jpg	descriptions in physics are often expressed as mathematical formulae. Suppose
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_013.jpg	that I memorize the formula from which I could, if I had the time and the inclination,
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_014.jpg	calculate any planetary position that has been recorded in the astronomical
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_015.jpg	archives.
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_016.jpg	What exactly have I gained, compared with memorizing those archives directly?
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_017.jpg	The formula is easier to remember — but then, looking a number up in the archives
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_018.jpg	may be even easier than calculating it from the formula.
test/images/synth_doc_00026_line_019.jpg	The real advantage of the formula is that it can be used in an infinity of cases

test/images/synth_doc_00028_line_000.jpg	DAVID: So it does. But not all languages are equal. Languages are theories. In their
test/images/synth_doc_00028_line_001.jpg	vocabulary and grammar, they embody substantial assertions about the world.
test/images/synth_doc_00028_line_002.jpg	Whenever we state a theory, only a small part of its content is explicit: the rest is
test/images/synth_doc_00028_line_003.jpg	carried by the language. Like all theories, languages are invented and selected for
test/images/synth_doc_00028_line_004.jpg	their ability to solve certain problems. In this case the problems are those of
test/images/synth_doc_00028_line_005.jpg	expressing other theories in forms in which it is convenient to apply them, and to

test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_010.jpg	CHAPTER SIX. PRIMED FOR LOVE 1. The Desert Fathers were early Christian
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_011.jpg	hermits who lived in communities located in remote areas of Egypt’s desert in the
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_012.jpg	early centuries AD.
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_013.jpg	There they could better focus on their religious practices, mainly the recitation of
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_014.jpg	Kyrie Eleison (a Greek phrase meaning “Lord, have mercy”), a Christian “mantra.”
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_015.jpg	These hermit communities were the historic predecessors of Christian orders for
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_016.jpg	monks and nuns; repetition of Kyrie Eleison remains a primary practice among
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_017.jpg	Eastern Orthodox monks, e.g., those on Mount Athos. Historical records suggest
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_018.jpg	that Christian monks from Egypt settled on Mount Athos in the seventh century,
test/images/synth_doc_00032_line_019.jpg	fleeing Islamic conquest. Helen Waddell, The Desert Fathers (Ann Arbor: University
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_000.jpg	But that high had disappeared into the mists of memory. Sic transeunt altered
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_001.jpg	states. In India they tell of a yogi who spent years and years alone in a cave,
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_002.jpg	achieving rarefied states of samadhi. One day, satisfied that he had reached the
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_003.jpg	end of his inner journey, the yogi came down from his mountain perch into a village.
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_004.jpg	That day the bazaar was crowded.
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_005.jpg	As he made his way through the crowd, the yogi was caught up in a rush to make
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_006.jpg	way for a local lord riding through on an elephant. A young boy standing in front of
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_007.jpg	the yogi stepped back suddenly in fright—stomping right on the yogi’s bare foot.
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_008.jpg	The yogi, angered and in pain, raised his walking staff to strike the youngster. But
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_009.jpg	suddenly seeing what he was about to do—and the anger that propelled his
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_010.jpg	arm—the yogi turned around and went right back up to his cave for more practice.
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_011.jpg	The tale speaks to the difference between meditation highs and enduring change.
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_012.jpg	Beyond transitory states like samadhi (or their equivalent, the absorptive jhanas),
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_013.jpg	there can be lasting changes in our very being. The Vissudhimagga holds this
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_014.jpg	transformation to be the true fruit of reaching the highest levels of the path of
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_015.jpg	insight.
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_016.jpg	For example, as the text says, strong negative feelings like greed and selfishness,
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_017.jpg	anger and ill will, fade away. In their place comes the predominance of positive
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_018.jpg	qualities like equanimity, kindness, compassion, and joy. That list resonates with
test/images/synth_doc_00034_line_019.jpg	similar claims from other meditative traditions.
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_000.jpg	Richie’s lab group initially compared expert meditators to controls in the magnitude
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_001.jpg	of prefrontal activation during focused attention on a small light. The long-term
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_002.jpg	meditators showed a modest increase in prefrontal activation compared with the
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_003.jpg	controls, though the difference was, strangely, not very impressive. One afternoon
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_004.jpg	as Richie and his lab team sat around a long conference table pondering these
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_005.jpg	somewhat disappointing data, they began to reflect on the large span of expertise
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_006.jpg	even within the so-called expert meditator group. This expert group actually ranged
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_007.jpg	in practice hours from 10,000 to 50,000—a very large spread.
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_008.jpg	Richie wondered what they would find if they compared those with the most versus
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_009.jpg	least amount of practice. He had already found that with higher levels of expertise,
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_010.jpg	there’s an effortlessness that actually would be reflected in less rather than more
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_011.jpg	prefrontal activation.When the team compared those with the most versus those
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_012.jpg	with the least amount of practice, they found something truly striking: all of the
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_013.jpg	increase in prefrontal activation was accounted for by those with the least amount
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_014.jpg	of practice.
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_015.jpg	For those with the most lifetime hours of practice, there was very little prefrontal
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_016.jpg	activation. Curiously, the activation tended to occur only at the very beginning of a
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_017.jpg	practice period, while the mind was focusing on the object of concentration, that
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_018.jpg	little light. Once the light was in focus, the prefrontal activation dropped away.
test/images/synth_doc_00030_line_019.jpg	This sequence may represent the neural echoes of effortless concentration.
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_000.jpg	But that distinction is not rooted in any significant difference. The role of the bear’s
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_001.jpg	nose is fundamentally no different from that of its den. Neither is a replicator,
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_002.jpg	though new instances of them are continually being made. Both the nose and the
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_003.jpg	den are merely parts of the environment which the bear’s genes manipulate in the
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_004.jpg	course of getting themselves replicated.
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_005.jpg	This gene-based understanding of life — regarding organisms as part of the
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_006.jpg	environment of genes — has implicitly been the basis of biology since Darwin, but it
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_007.jpg	was overlooked until at least the 1960s, and not fully understood until Richard
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_008.jpg	Dawkins published The Selfish Gene (1976) and The Extended Phenotype (1982).I
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_009.jpg	now return to the question whether life is a fundamental phenomenon of nature. I
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_010.jpg	have warned against the reductionist assumption that emergent phenomena, such
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_011.jpg	as life, are necessarily less fundamental than microscopic physical ones.
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_012.jpg	Nevertheless, everything I have just been saying about what life is seems to point to
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_013.jpg	its being a mere side-effect at the end of a long chain of side-effects. For it is not
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_014.jpg	merely the predictions of biology that reduce, in principle, to those of physics: it is,
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_015.jpg	on the face of it, also the explanations. As I have said, the great explanatory
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_016.jpg	theories of Darwin (in modern versions such as that propounded by Dawkins), and
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_017.jpg	of modern biochemistry, are reductive.
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_018.jpg	Living molecules genes — are merely molecules, obeying the same laws of physics
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_019.jpg	and chemistry as non-living ones. They contain no special substance, nor do they
test/images/synth_doc_00029_line_020.jpg	have any special physical attributes. They just happen, in certain environments, to
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_000.jpg	The same assumption occurs in inductivism, which supposes that we can be
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_001.jpg	absolutely certain of the conclusions of mathematical arguments because they are
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_002.jpg	deductive, reasonably sure of scientific arguments because they are ‘inductive’,
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_003.jpg	and forever undecided about philosophical arguments, which it sees as little more
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_004.jpg	than matters of taste. But none of that is true. Explanations are not justified by the
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_005.jpg	means by which they were derived; they are justified by their superior ability,
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_006.jpg	relative to rival explanations, to solve the problems they address. That is why the
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_007.jpg	argument that a theory is indefensible can be so compelling.
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_008.jpg	A prediction, or any assertion, that cannot be defended might still be true, but an
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_009.jpg	explanation that cannot be defended is not an explanation. The rejection of ‘mere’
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_010.jpg	explanations on the grounds that they are not justified by any ultimate explanation
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_011.jpg	inevitably propels one into futile searches for an ultimate source of justification.
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_012.jpg	There is no such source. Nor is there that hierarchy of reliability from mathematical
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_013.jpg	to scientific to philosophical arguments. Some philosophical arguments, including
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_014.jpg	the argument against solipsism, are far more compelling than any scientific
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_015.jpg	argument.
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_016.jpg	Indeed, every scientific argument assumes the falsity not only of solipsism, but also
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_017.jpg	of other philosophical theories including any number of variants of solipsism that
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_018.jpg	might contradict specific parts of the scientific argument. I shall also show (in
test/images/synth_doc_00033_line_019.jpg	Chapter 10) that even purely mathematical arguments derive their reliability from

test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_001.jpg	theory’? I could easily think of one right now. DAVID: I very much doubt that you
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_003.jpg	CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: Of course I can. Here it is. ‘Whenever you, David, jump
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_004.jpg	from high places in ways that would, according to the prevailing theory, kill you, you
