test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_006.jpg	that every past test of your theory was also necessarily a test of mine, since all the
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_007.jpg	predictions of your theory and mine regarding past experiments are identical.
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_008.jpg	Therefore your theory’s refuted rivals were also my theory’s refuted rivals. And
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_009.jpg	therefore my new theory is exactly as corroborated as your prevailing theory.
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_010.jpg	How, then, can my theory be ‘untenable’? What faults could it possibly have that are
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_011.jpg	not shared by your theory?
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_012.jpg	DAVID: Just about every fault in the Popperian book! Your theory is constructed
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_013.jpg	from the prevailing one by appending an unexplained qualification about me
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_014.jpg	floating. That qualification is, in effect, a new theory, but you have given no
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_015.jpg	argument either against the prevailing theory of my gravitational properties, or in
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_016.jpg	favour of the new one. You have subjected your new theory to no criticism (other
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_017.jpg	than what I am giving it now) and no experimental testing. It does not solve — or
test/images/synth_doc_00031_line_018.jpg	even purport to solve — any current problem, nor have you suggested a new,
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_000.jpg	Judson Brewer et al., “Mindfulness Training for Smoking Cessation: Results from a
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_001.jpg	Randomized Controlled Trial,” Drug and Alcohol Dependence 119 (2011b): 72–80.
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_002.jpg	13. A. P. Weible et al., “Rhythmic Brain Stimulation Reduces Anxiety-Related
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_003.jpg	Behavior in a Mouse Model of Meditation Training,” Proceedings of the National
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_004.jpg	Academy of Sciences, in press, 2017.
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_005.jpg	The photic driving impact of strobe lights can create a danger in humans for those
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_006.jpg	with epilepsy, because the rhythms can sometimes trigger a seizure. 14. H. F.
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_007.jpg	Iaccarino et al., “Gamma Frequency Entrainment Attenuates Amyloid Load and
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_008.jpg	Modifies Microglia,” Nature 540:7632 (2016): 230–35; doi:10.1038/nature20587.
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_009.jpg	15. The mouse’s basic mammalian biology maps somewhat along human lines, but
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_010.jpg	not entirely, and when it comes to the brain, the differences are far greater. 16.
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_011.jpg	For more details, see Daniel Goleman, A Force for Good: The Dalai Lama’s Vision
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_012.jpg	for Our World (New York: Bantam, 2015); www.joinaforce4good.org. 17. Some
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_013.jpg	evidence for this strategy: C. Lund et al., “Poverty and Mental Disorders: Breaking
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_014.jpg	the Cycle in Low-Income and Middle-Income Countries,” Lancet 378:9801 (2011):
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_015.jpg	1502–14; doi:10.1016/S0140- 6736(11)60754-X.Index The page numbers in this
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_016.jpg	index refer to the printed version of this book. The link provided will take you to the
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_017.jpg	beginning of that print page.
test/images/synth_doc_00035_line_018.jpg	You may need to scroll forward from that location to find the corresponding
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_000.jpg	A few long-term vipassana meditators had accumulated more than 20,000 lifetime
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_001.jpg	hours and one or two up to 30,000, though none had done a three-year retreat,
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_002.jpg	which became a de facto distinguishing feature of the yogi group. Despite the rare
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_003.jpg	overlaps in lifetime hours, the vast majority of the three groups fall into these rough
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_004.jpg	categories. There are no hard-and-fast lifetime hour cutoffs for the three levels, but
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_005.jpg	research on them has clustered in particular ranges. We’ve organizedresearch on
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_006.jpg	them has clustered in particular ranges. We’ve organized meditation’s benefits into
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_007.jpg	three dose-response levels, roughly mapping on the novice to amateur to
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_008.jpg	professional rankings found in expertise of all kinds, from ballerinas to chess
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_009.jpg	champions.
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_010.jpg	The vast majority of meditators in the West fall into the first level: people who
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_011.jpg	meditate for a short period—a few minutes to half an hour or so on most days. A
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_012.jpg	smaller group continues on to the long-term meditator level. And a mere handful
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_013.jpg	attain the expertise of the yogis.
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_014.jpg	Let’s look at the impacts in those who have just begun a meditation practice. When
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_015.jpg	it comes to stress recovery, the evidence for some benefits in the first few months
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_016.jpg	of daily practice are more subjective than objective—and shaky. On the other hand
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_017.jpg	the amygdala, a key node in the brain’s stress circuitry, shows lessened reactivity
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_018.jpg	after thirty or so hours over eight weeks of MBSR practice. Compassion meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_019.jpg	shows stronger benefits from the get-go; as few as seven total hours over the
test/images/synth_doc_00036_line_020.jpg	course of two weeks leads to increased connectivity in circuits important for
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_000.jpg	The rest of physics forms the first few storeys. Astrophysics and chemistry are at a
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_001.jpg	higher level, geology even higher, and so on. The edifice branches into many
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_002.jpg	towers of increasingly high-level subjects like biochemistry, biology and genetics.
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_003.jpg	Perched at the tottering, stratospheric tops are subjects like the theory of evolution,
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_004.jpg	economics, psychology and computer science, which in this picture are almost
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_005.jpg	inconceivably derivative. At present, we have only approximations to a reductive
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_006.jpg	‘theory of everything’.
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_007.jpg	These can already predict quite accurate laws of motion for individual subatomic
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_008.jpg	particles. From these laws, present- day computers can calculate the motion of any
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_009.jpg	isolated group of a few interacting particles in some detail, given their initial state.
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_010.jpg	But even the smallest speck of matter visible to the naked eye contains trillions of
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_011.jpg	atoms, each composed of many subatomic particles, and is continually interacting
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_012.jpg	with the outside world; so it is quite infeasible to predict its behaviour particle by
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_013.jpg	particle. By supplementing the exact laws of motion with various approximation
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_014.jpg	schemes, we can predict some aspects of the gross behaviour of quite large
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_015.jpg	objects — for instance, the temperature at which a given chemical compound will
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_016.jpg	melt or boil.
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_017.jpg	Much of basic chemistry has been reduced to physics in this way. But for
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_018.jpg	higher-level sciences the reductionist programme is a matter of principle only.
test/images/synth_doc_00038_line_019.jpg	No one expects actually to deduce many principles of biology, psychology or
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_000.jpg	I am grateful to my friends and colleagues Ruth Chang, Artur Ekert, David
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_001.jpg	Johnson-Davies, Michael Lockwood, Enrico Rodrigo and Kolya Wolf, to my mother
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_002.jpg	Tikvah Deutsch, and to my editors Caroline Knight and Ravi Mirchandani (of
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_003.jpg	Penguin Books) and John Woodruff, and especially to Sarah Lawrence, for their
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_004.jpg	thorough, critical reading of earlier drafts of this book, and for suggesting many
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_005.jpg	corrections and improvements. I am also grateful to those who have read and
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_006.jpg	commented on parts of the manuscript, including Harvey Brown, Steve Graham,
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_007.jpg	Rossella Lupaccini, Svein Olav Nyberg, Oliver and Harriet Strimpel, and especially
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_008.jpg	Richard Dawkins and Frank Tipler.1 The Theory of Everything I remember being
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_009.jpg	told, when I was a small child, that in ancient times it was still possible for a very
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_010.jpg	learned person to know everything that was known. I was also told that nowadays
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_011.jpg	so much is known that no one could conceivably learn more than a tiny fraction of
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_012.jpg	it, even in a long lifetime. The latter proposition surprised and disappointed me. In
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_013.jpg	fact, I refused to believe it.
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_014.jpg	I did not know how to justify my disbelief. But I knew that I did not want things to be
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_015.jpg	like that, and I envied the ancient scholars. It was not that I wanted to memorize all
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_016.jpg	the facts that were listed in the world’s encyclopaedias: on the contrary, I hated
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_017.jpg	memorizing facts. That is not the sense in which I expected it to be possible to
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_018.jpg	know everything that was known.
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_019.jpg	It would not have disappointed me to be told that more publications appear every
test/images/synth_doc_00037_line_020.jpg	day than anyone could read in a lifetime, or that there are 600,000 known species
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_000.jpg	So it went through the entire hermit community until the grapes came around again
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_001.jpg	to Macarius. Those early Christian hermits, known as Desert Fathers, lauded the
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_002.jpg	same wholesome modes of being as do yogis in the Himalayas today, who follow
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_003.jpg	surprisingly similar discipline, customs, and meditative practices.
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_004.jpg	They share an ethic of selflessness and generosity and live in isolation, the better to
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_005.jpg	immerse themselves in meditation. What propelled those juicy grapes’ journey
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_006.jpg	through that desert commune? The drivers were compassion and loving-kindness,
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_007.jpg	the attitude of putting the needs of others ahead of our own. Technically,
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_008.jpg	“loving-kindness” refers to wishing that other people be happy; its near cousin
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_009.jpg	“compassion” entails the wish that people be relieved of suffering.
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_010.jpg	Both outlooks (which we’ll just refer to as “compassion”) can be strengthened
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_011.jpg	through mind training—and if successful, the result will be acting to help others, as
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_012.jpg	demonstrated by the Desert Fathers and that bunch of grapes. But consider a
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_013.jpg	modern update. Divinity students at a theological seminary were told they would be
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_014.jpg	evaluated on a practice sermon. Half were given a random selection of Bible topics
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_015.jpg	for their sermon. The other half were assigned the parable of the Good Samaritan,
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_016.jpg	the man who stopped to help a stranger inthe parable of the Good Samaritan, the
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_017.jpg	man who stopped to help a stranger in need who was lying by the side of the road,
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_018.jpg	even as others walked by, indifferent.
test/images/synth_doc_00040_line_019.jpg	After a time to prepare their thoughts, they went one by one to another building,
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_000.jpg	These tasks are purposely devilish, designed and calibrated to ensure that whoever takes it will make a
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_001.jpg	certain percentage of mistakes, and, what’s more, that their confidence in their responses will vary.
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_002.jpg	Imagine, for instance, having 160 words whiz by in succession for 1.5 seconds each. Then you see another
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_003.jpg	set of 320 words, half of which you’ve seen before in that zippy presentation. You have to press one of
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_004.jpg	two buttons to tell if you think the word you see in the second set was in the previous list, or not. Then
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_005.jpg	you rate your confidence in your accuracy for each word, a metric for meta-awareness to the degree you
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_006.jpg	both have confidence in and make the correct response.
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_007.jpg	Psychologists at UC–Santa Barbara used such a mental challenge with people learning mindfulness for the
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_008.jpg	first time, as well as a group who had a course in nutrition.21 Meta-awareness improved in the meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_009.jpg	group, but not a whit in those taking the nutrition class.WILL IT LAST? Amishi Jha’s lab tested the effect
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_010.jpg	of an intensive mindfulness retreat where people meditated for more than eight hours each day for a
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_011.jpg	month.22 The retreat boosted participants’ “alerting,” a vigilant state of readiness to respond to whatever
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_012.jpg	you encounter.
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_013.jpg	But although in a previous study she had found an improvement in orienting with beginners in a brief
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_014.jpg	course of mindfulness, surprisingly, these retreat participants showed no such boost. This nonfinding
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_015.jpg	represents important data if we are to get a full picture of how meditation does and does not matter.
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_016.jpg	It helps us get a portrait of how various aspects of attention change—or do not—with different types of
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_017.jpg	meditation, and at differing levels. Some changes might occur right away, while others take longer: while
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_018.jpg	orienting may budge initially and then stall, alerting seems to improve with practice. And, we suspect,
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_019.jpg	meditation sustained over time might be needed to maintain such shifts in attention, lest they fade. About
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_020.jpg	the time when Richie was doing his Harvard research on signal-to- noise shifts in meditators, cognitive
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_021.jpg	scientists such as Anne Treisman and Michael Posner pointed out that “attention” represents too gross a
test/images/synth_doc_00042_line_022.jpg	concept.
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_000.jpg	Grilling the FDA regulators about their plans to cancel many of the remaining
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_001.jpg	researchprojects, Kennedy demanded to know, “Why if [these projects] were
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_002.jpg	worthwhile six months ago, why aren’t they worthwhile now?” Kennedy said it would
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_003.jpg	be a “loss to the nation” if psychedelics were banned from medicine because of
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_004.jpg	illicit use. “Perhaps we have lost sight of the fact that [they] can be very, very
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_005.jpg	helpful in our society if used properly.” But Kennedy got nowhere. Leary, and
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_006.jpg	perhaps the drugs themselves, had made drawing such distinctions impossible. In
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_007.jpg	October, some sixty psychedelic researchers scattered across the United States
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_008.jpg	received a letter from the FDA ordering them to stop their work. James Fadiman,
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_009.jpg	the psychologist conducting experiments on creativity at the International
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_010.jpg	Foundation for Advanced Study in Menlo Park, remembers the day well. The letter
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_011.jpg	revoking FDA approval of the project arrived at the very moment he had finished
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_012.jpg	dosing four of his problem-solving creatives to begin their session.
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_013.jpg	As he read the letter, sprawled on the floor in the next room, “four men lay, their
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_014.jpg	minds literally expanding.” Fadiman said to his colleagues, “I think we need to
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_015.jpg	agree that we got this letter tomorrow.” And so it was not until the following day that
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_016.jpg	the research program of the International Foundation for Advanced Study, along
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_017.jpg	with virtually every other research program then under way in the United States,
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_018.jpg	closed down. One psychedelic research program survived the purge: the Maryland
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_019.jpg	Psychiatric Research Center at Spring Grove.
test/images/synth_doc_00039_line_020.jpg	Here, researchers such as Stanislav Grof, Bill Richards, Richard Yensen, and, until
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_000.jpg	Thus the outcome of a crucial experimental test to decide between two theories does depend on the
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_001.jpg	theories’ predictions, and not directly on their explanations. This is the source of the misconception that
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_002.jpg	there is nothing more to a scientific theory than its predictions. But experimental testing is by no means
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_003.jpg	the only process involved in the growth of scientific knowledge. The overwhelming majority of theories
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_004.jpg	are rejected because they contain bad explanations, not because they fail experimental tests.
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_005.jpg	We reject them without ever bothering to test them. For example, consider the theory that eating a
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_006.jpg	kilogram of grass is a cure for the common cold. That theory makes experimentally testable predictions: if
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_007.jpg	people tried the grass cure and found it ineffective, the theory would be proved false.
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_008.jpg	But it has never been tested and probably never will be, because it contains no explanation — either of
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_009.jpg	how the cure would work, or of anything else. We rightly presume it to be false. There are always infinitely
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_010.jpg	many possible theories of that sort, compatible with existing observations and making new predictions, so
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_011.jpg	we could never have the timeor resources to test them all. What we test are new theories that seem to
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_012.jpg	show promise of explaining things better than the prevailing ones do. To say that prediction is the
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_013.jpg	purpose of a scientific theory is to confuse means with ends.
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_014.jpg	It is like saying that the purpose of a spaceship is to burn fuel. In fact, burning fuel is only one of many
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_015.jpg	things a spaceship has to do to accomplish its real purpose, which is to transport its payload from one
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_016.jpg	point in space to another. Passing experimental tests is only one of many things a theory has to do to
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_017.jpg	achieve the real purpose of science, which is to explain the world. As I have said, explanations are
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_018.jpg	inevitably framed partly in terms of things we do not observe directly: atoms and forces; the interiors of
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_019.jpg	stars and the rotation of galaxies; the past and the future; the laws of nature.
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_020.jpg	The deeper an explanation is, the more remote from immediate experience are the entities to which it
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_021.jpg	must refer. But these entities are not fictional: on the contrary, they are part of the very fabric of reality.
test/images/synth_doc_00041_line_022.jpg	Explanations often yield predictions, at least in principle. Indeed, if something is, in principle, predictable,
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_000.jpg	Our theories of physics are, unlike common sense, coherent, and they first achieved this by dropping the
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_001.jpg	idea of the flow of time. Admittedly, physicists talk about the flow of time just as everyone else does. For
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_002.jpg	example, in his book Principia, in which he set out the principles of Newtonian mechanics and
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_003.jpg	gravitation, Newton wrote: Absolute, true, and mathematical time, of itself, and from its own nature, flows
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_004.jpg	equably without relation to anything external.
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_005.jpg	But Newton wisely makes no attempt to translate his assertion that time flows into mathematical form, or
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_006.jpg	to derive any conclusion from it. None of Newton’s physical theories refers to the flow of time, nor has
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_007.jpg	any subsequent physical theory referred to, or been compatible with, the flow of time.
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_008.jpg	So why did Newton think it necessary to say that time ‘flows equably’? There is nothing wrong with
test/images/synth_doc_00044_line_009.jpg	‘equably’: one can interpret that as meaning that measurements of time are the same for observers An

test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_000.jpg	I am not saying that when we understand a theory it necessarily follows that we understand everything it
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_001.jpg	can explain. With a very deep theory, the recognition that it explains a given phenomenon may itself be a
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_002.jpg	significant discovery requiring independent explanation. For example, quasars — extremely bright sources
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_003.jpg	of radiation at the centre of some galaxies — were for many years one of the mysteries of astrophysics. It
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_004.jpg	was once thought that new physics would be needed to explain them, but now we believe that they are
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_005.jpg	explained by the general theory of relativity and other theories that were already known before quasars
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_006.jpg	were discovered. We believe that quasars consist of hot matter in the process of falling into black holes
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_007.jpg	(collapsed stars whose gravitational field is so intense that nothing can escape from them).
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_008.jpg	Yet reaching that conclusion has required years of research, both observational and theoretical. Now that
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_009.jpg	we believe we have gained a measure of understanding of quasars, we do not think that this understanding
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_010.jpg	is something we already had before. Explaining quasars, albeit through existing theories, has given us
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_011.jpg	genuinely new understanding.
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_012.jpg	Just as it is hard to define what an explanation is, it is hard to define when a subsidiary explanation should
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_013.jpg	count as an independent component of what is understood, and when it should be considered as being
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_014.jpg	subsumed in the deeper theory. It is hard to define, but not so hard to recognize: as with explanations in
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_015.jpg	general, in practice we know a new explanation when we are given one. Again, the difference has
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_016.jpg	something to do with creativity. Explaining the motion of a particular planet, when one already
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_017.jpg	understands the general explanation of gravity, is a mechanical task, though it may be a very complex one.
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_018.jpg	But using existing theory to account for quasars requires creative thought. Thus, to understand everything
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_019.jpg	that is understood in astrophysics today, you would have to know the theory of quasars explicitly. But you
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_020.jpg	would not have to know the orbit of any specific planet.
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_021.jpg	So, even though our stock of known theories is indeed snowballing, just as our stock of recorded facts is,
test/images/synth_doc_00043_line_022.jpg	that still does not necessarily make the whole structure harder to understand than it used to be. For while
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_000.jpg	Pahnke suggested Richards try one more time, but in a room with soft lighting, plants, and music and
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_001.jpg	using a higher dose. Once again, Richards had “an incredibly profound experience.
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_002.jpg	I realized I had not exaggerated the first trip but in fact had forgotten 80 percent of it. “I have never
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_003.jpg	doubted the validity of these experiences,” Richards told me. “This was the realm of mystical
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_004.jpg	consciousness that Shankara was talking about, that Plotinus was writing about, that Saint John of the
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_005.jpg	Cross and Meister Eckhart were writing about. It’s also what AbrahamMaslow was talking about with his
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_006.jpg	‘peak experiences,’ though Abe could get there without the drugs.” Richards would go on to study
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_007.jpg	psychology under Maslow at Brandeis University. “Abe was a natural Jewish mystic.
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_008.jpg	He could just lie down in the backyard and have a mystical experience. Psychedelics are for those of us
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_009.jpg	who aren’t so innately gifted.” Richards emerged from those first psychedelic explorations in possession
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_010.jpg	of three unshakable convictions. The first is that the experience of the sacred reported both by the great
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_011.jpg	mystics and by people on high-dose psychedelic journeys is the same experience and is “real”— that is,
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_012.jpg	not just a figment of the imagination. “You go deep enough or far out enough in consciousness and you
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_013.jpg	will bump into the sacred.
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_014.jpg	It’s not something we generate; it’s something out there waiting to be discovered. And this reliably
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_015.jpg	happens to nonbelievers as well as believers.” Second, that, whether occasioned by drugs or other means,
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_016.jpg	these experiences of mystical consciousness are in all likelihood the primal basis of religion. (Partly for
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_017.jpg	this reason Richards believes that psychedelics should be part of a divinity student’s education. And third,
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_018.jpg	that consciousness is a property of the universe, not brains.
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_019.jpg	On this question, he holds with Henri Bergson, the French philosopher, who conceived of the human
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_020.jpg	mind as a kind of radio receiver, able to tune in to frequencies of energy and information that exist
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_021.jpg	outside it. “If you wanted to find the blonde who delivered the news last night,” Richards offered by way
test/images/synth_doc_00045_line_022.jpg	of an analogy, “you wouldn’t look for her in the TV set.” The television set is, like the human brain,
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_000.jpg	For the same reason, each shadow atom in the barrier can be interacting with only a small proportion of
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_001.jpg	the other shadow atoms in its vicinity, and the ones it does interact with form a barrier much like the
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_002.jpg	tangible one. And so on. All matter, and all physical processes, have this structure.
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_003.jpg	If the tangible barrier is the frog’s retina, then there must be many shadow retinas, each capable of
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_004.jpg	stopping only one of the shadow-counterparts of each photon. Each shadow retina only interacts strongly
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_005.jpg	with the corresponding shadow photons, and with the corresponding shadow frog, and so on. In other
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_006.jpg	words, particles are grouped into parallel universes. They are ‘parallel’ in the sense that within each
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_007.jpg	universe particles interact with each other just as they do in the tangible universe, but each universe affects
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_008.jpg	the others only weakly, through interference phenomena. Thus we have reached the conclusion of the
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_009.jpg	chain of reasoning that begins with strangely shaped shadows and ends with parallel universes.
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_010.jpg	Each step takes the form of noting that the behaviour of objects that we observe can beexplained only if
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_011.jpg	there are unobserved objects present, and if those unobserved objects have certain properties. The heart
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_012.jpg	of the argument is that single-particle interference phenomena unequivocally rule out the possibility that
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_013.jpg	the tangible universe around us is all that exists. There is no disputing the fact that such interference
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_014.jpg	phenomena occur.
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_015.jpg	Yet the existence of the multiverse is still a minority view among physicists. Why?
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_016.jpg	The answer, I regret to say, does not reflect well upon the majority. I shall have more to say about this in
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_017.jpg	Chapter 13, but for the moment let me point out that the arguments I have presented in this chapter are
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_018.jpg	compelling only to those who seek explanations.
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_019.jpg	Those who are satisfied with mere prediction, and who have no strong desire to understand how the
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_020.jpg	predicted outcomes of experiments come about, may if they wish simply deny the existence of anything
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_021.jpg	other than what I have been calling ‘tangible’ entities. Some people, such as instrumentalists and
test/images/synth_doc_00047_line_022.jpg	positivists, take this line as a matter of philosophical principle.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_000.jpg	One could not easily program them to do word processing or to factorize large numbers. On the other
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_001.jpg	hand, they exert exquisitely accurate, interactive control over the responses of a complex environment
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_002.jpg	(the organism) to everything that may happen to it. And this control is directed towards causing the
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_003.jpg	environment to act back upon the genes in a specific way (namely, to replicate them) such that the net
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_004.jpg	effect on the genes is as independent as possible of what may be happening outside. This is more than
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_005.jpg	just computing.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_006.jpg	It is virtual-reality rendering. The analogy with the human technology of virtual reality is no perfect. First,
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_007.jpg	although genes are enveloped, just as a user of virtual reality is, in an environment whose detailed
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_008.jpg	constitution and behaviour are specified by a program (which the genes themselves embody), the genes
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_009.jpg	do not experience that environment because they have neither senses nor experiences.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_010.jpg	So if an organism is an virtual-reality rendering specified by its genes, it is a rendering without an audience.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_011.jpg	Second, the organism is not only being rendered, it is being manufactured. It is not a matter of ‘fooling’
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_012.jpg	the gene into believing that there is an organism out there.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_013.jpg	The organism really is out there. However, these differences are unimportant.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_014.jpg	As I have said, all virtual-reality rendering physically manufactures the rendered environment. The inside
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_015.jpg	of any virtual-reality generator in the act of rendering is precisely a real, physical environment,
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_016.jpg	manufactured to have the properties specified in the program. It is just that we users sometimes choose to
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_017.jpg	interpret it as a different environment, which happens to feel the same. As for the absence of a user, let us
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_018.jpg	consider explicitly what the role of the user of virtual reality is.
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_019.jpg	First, it is to kick the rendered environment and to be kicked back in return — in other words, to interact
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_020.jpg	with the environment in an autonomous way. In the biological case, that role is performed by the external
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_021.jpg	habitat. Second, it is to provide the intention behind the rendering. That is to say, it makes little sense to
test/images/synth_doc_00049_line_022.jpg	speak of a particular situation as being a virtual-reality rendering if there is no concept of the rendering
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_000.jpg	While helping out with the dishes after a Friday night dinner at the Shulgins’, Jesse learned that a group of
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_001.jpg	therapists and scientists would be gathering in Big Sur to discuss the prospects for reviving psychedelic
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_002.jpg	research. There were signs that the door Washington, D.C., had slammed shut on research in the late
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_003.jpg	1960s might be opening, if only a crack: Curtis Wright, a new administrator at the FDA (and, as it
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_004.jpg	happens, a former student of Roland Griffiths’s at Hopkins), had signaled that research protocols for
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_005.jpg	psychedelics would be treated like any other—judged on their merits. Testing this new receptivity, a
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_006.jpg	psychiatrist at the University of New Mexico named Rick Strassman had sought and received approval to
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_007.jpg	study the physiological effects of DMT, a powerful psychedelic compound found in many plants. This
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_008.jpg	small trial marked the first federally sanctioned experiment with a psychedelic compound since the
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_009.jpg	1970s—in retrospect, a watershed event.
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_010.jpg	Around the same time, Rick Doblin and Charles Grob, a psychiatrist at UCLA, had succeeded in
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_011.jpg	persuading the government to approve the first human trial of MDMA. (Grob is one of the first
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_012.jpg	psychiatrists to advocate for the return of psychedelics to psychotherapy; he later conducted the first
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_013.jpg	modern trial of psilocybin for cancer patients. The year before the Esalen gathering (which Grob and
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_014.jpg	Doblin both attended), David Nichols, a Purdue University chemist and pharmacologist, launched the
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_015.jpg	Heffter Research Institute (named for the German chemist who first identified the mescaline compound
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_016.jpg	in 1897) with the then improbable ambition of funding serious psychedelic science. (Heffter has since
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_017.jpg	helped fund many of the modern trials of psilocybin.
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_018.jpg	So there were scattered hopeful signs in the early 1990s that conditions were ripening for a revival of
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_019.jpg	psychedelic research. The tiny community that had sustained such a dream through the dark ages began,
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_020.jpg	tentatively, quietly, to organize.
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_021.jpg	Even though Jesse was new to this community, and neither a scientist nor a therapist, he asked if he could
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_022.jpg	attend the Esalen meeting and offered to make himself useful, refilling water glasses if that’s what ittook.
test/images/synth_doc_00048_line_023.jpg	Most of the gathering was taken up with discussions of the potential medical applications of psychedelics,
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_000.jpg	If two programs respond in the same way to every possible action by the user, then they render the same
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_001.jpg	environment; if they would respond perceptibly differently to even one possible action, they render
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_002.jpg	different environments. That remains so even if the user never happens to perform the action that shows
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_003.jpg	up the difference.
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_004.jpg	The environment a program renders (for a given type of user, with a given connecting cable) is a logical
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_005.jpg	property of the program, independent of whether the program is ever executed. A rendered environment
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_006.jpg	is accurate in so far as it would respond in the intended way to every possible action of the user.
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_007.jpg	Thus its accuracy depends not only on experiences which users of it actually have, but also on experiences
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_008.jpg	they do not have, but would have had if they had chosen to behave differently during the rendering. This
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_009.jpg	may sound paradoxical, but as I have said, it is a straightforward consequence of the fact that virtual reality
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_010.jpg	is, like reality itself, interactive.
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_011.jpg	This gives rise to an important difference between image generation and virtual-reality generation. The
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_012.jpg	accuracy of an image generator’s rendering can in principle be experienced, measured and certified by the
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_013.jpg	user, but the accuracy of a virtual-reality rendering never can be. For example, if you are a music-lover and
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_014.jpg	know a particular piece well enough, you can listen to a performance of it and confirm that it is a perfectly
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_015.jpg	accurate rendering, in principle down to the last note, phrasing, dynamics and all. But if you are a tennis
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_016.jpg	fan who knows Wimbledon’s Centre Court perfectly, you can never confirm that a purported rendering of
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_017.jpg	it is accurate. Even if you are free to explore the rendered Centre Court for however long you like, and to
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_018.jpg	‘kick’ it in whatever way you like, and even if you have equal access to the real Centre Court for
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_019.jpg	comparison, you cannot ever certify that the program does indeed render the real location.
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_020.jpg	For you can never know what would have happened if only you had explored a little more, or looked over
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_021.jpg	your shoulder at the right moment. Perhaps if you had sat on the rendered umpire’s chair and shouted
test/images/synth_doc_00046_line_022.jpg	‘fault!’, a nuclear submarine would have surfaced through the grass and torpedoed the Scoreboard.
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_000.jpg	However, this line of criticism lets inductivism off far too lightly. It does illustrate the fact that repeated
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_001.jpg	observations cannot justify theories, but in doing so it entirely misses (or rather, accepts) a more basic
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_002.jpg	misconception: namely, that the inductive extrapolation of observations to form new theories is even
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_003.jpg	possible. In fact, it is impossible to extrapolate observations unless one has already placed them within an
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_004.jpg	explanatory framework. For example, in order to ‘induce’ its false prediction, Russell’s chicken must first
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_005.jpg	have had in mind a false explanation of the farmer’s behaviour. Perhaps it guessed that the farmer
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_006.jpg	harboured benevolent feelings towards chickens.
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_007.jpg	Had it guessed a different explanation — that the farmer was trying to fatten the chickens up for
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_008.jpg	slaughter, for instance — it would have ‘extrapolated’ the behaviour differently. Suppose that one day the
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_009.jpg	farmer starts bringing the chickens more food than usual. How one extrapolates this new set of
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_010.jpg	observations to predict the farmer’s future behaviour depends entirely on how one explains it. According
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_011.jpg	to the benevolent-farmer theory, it isevidence that the farmer’s benevolence towards chickens has
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_012.jpg	increased, and that therefore the chickens have even less to worry about than before.
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_013.jpg	But according to the fattening-up theory, the behaviour is ominous — it is evidence that slaughter is
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_014.jpg	imminent. The fact that the same observational evidence can be ‘extrapolated’ to give two diametrically
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_015.jpg	opposite predictions according to which explanation one adopts, and cannot justify either of them, is not
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_016.jpg	some accidental limitation of the farmyard environment: it is true of all observational evidence under all
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_017.jpg	circumstances.
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_018.jpg	Observations could not possibly play either of the roles assigned to them in the inductivist scheme, even
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_019.jpg	in respect of mere predictions, let alone genuine explanatory theories. Admittedly, inductivism is based on
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_020.jpg	the common-sense theory of the growth of knowledge — that we learn from experience — and
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_021.jpg	historically it was associated with the liberation of science from dogma and tyranny.
test/images/synth_doc_00050_line_022.jpg	But if we want to understand the true nature of knowledge, and its place in the fabric of reality, we must
