test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_000.jpg	You could die! What if you lose your lunch or, even worse, your shit?! And what if “the grandmother”
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_001.jpg	dredges up some childhood trauma? Do you really want to lose it among these strangers?
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_002.jpg	These women? (Part of the power of the ego flows from its command of one’s rational faculties. By the
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_003.jpg	time I arrived for the circle, I was a nervous wreck, assailed by second and third thoughts as to the
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_004.jpg	wisdom of what I was about to do.
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_005.jpg	But, as has happened every time, as soon as I swallowed the medicine and slipped past the point of no
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_006.jpg	return, the voice of doubt went quiet and I surrendered to whatever was in store. Which was not unlike
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_007.jpg	my other psychedelic experiences, with a couple of notable exceptions. Perhaps because the tea, which
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_008.jpg	was viscous and acrid and unexpectedly sweet, makes its alien presence felt in your stomach and
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_009.jpg	intestines, ayahuasca isa more bodily experience than some other psychedelics. I did not get sick, but I was
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_010.jpg	very much aware of the thick brew moving through me and, as the effect of the DMT (ayahuasca’s active
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_011.jpg	ingredient) came on, imagined it as a vine winding its way through the curls and convolutions of my
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_012.jpg	intestines, occupying my body before slowly working its snakelike way up to and into my head.
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_013.jpg	There followed a great many memories and images, some horrifying, others magnificent, but I want to
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_014.jpg	describe one in particular because, although I don’t completely understand it, it captures something that
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_015.jpg	psychedelics have taught me, something important. Because there was still some light in the room when
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_016.jpg	the ceremony began, we were all wearing eye masks, and mine felt a little tight around my head. Early in
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_017.jpg	the journey, I became aware of the black straps circling my skull, and these morphed into bars.
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_018.jpg	My head was caged in steel. The bars then began to multiply, moving down from my head to encircle my
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_019.jpg	torso and then my legs. I was now trapped head to toe in a black steel cage.
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_020.jpg	I pressed against the bars, but they were unyielding. There was no way out. Panic was building when I
test/images/synth_doc_00051_line_021.jpg	noticed the green tip of a vine at the base of the cage.
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_000.jpg	The yogi, angered and in pain, raised his walking staff to strike the youngster. But suddenly seeing what he
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_001.jpg	was about to do—and the anger that propelled his arm—the yogi turned around and went right back up
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_002.jpg	to his cave for more practice.
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_003.jpg	The tale speaks to the difference between meditation highs and enduring change. Beyond transitory states
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_004.jpg	like samadhi (or their equivalent, the absorptive jhanas), there can be lasting changes in our very being.
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_005.jpg	The Vissudhimagga holds this transformation to be the true fruit of reaching the highest levels of the path
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_006.jpg	of insight. For example, as the text says, strong negative feelings like greed and selfishness, anger and ill
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_007.jpg	will, fade away.
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_008.jpg	In their place comes the predominance of positive qualities like equanimity, kindness, compassion, and
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_009.jpg	joy. That list resonates with similar claims from other meditative traditions. Whether these traits are due to
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_010.jpg	some specific transformative experiences that accrue in attaining those levels, or from the sheer hours of
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_011.jpg	practice along the way, we can’t say. But Richie’s delicious meditation-induced high—possibly somewhere
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_012.jpg	in the vicinity of access concentration, if not first jhana—was not sufficient to bring on these trait
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_013.jpg	changes.The Buddha’s discovery—reaching enlightenment via the path of insight— was a challenge to the
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_014.jpg	yogic traditions of his day, which followed the path of concentration to various levels of samadhi, the
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_015.jpg	bliss-filled state of utter absorption. In those days, insight versus concentration was a burning issue in a
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_016.jpg	politics of consciousness that revolved around the best path to those altered traits.
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_017.jpg	Fast-forward to another politics of consciousness in the 1960s, during the heady days of the psychedelic
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_018.jpg	fad. The sudden revelations of drug-induced altered states led to assumptions like, as one acidhead put it,
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_019.jpg	“With LSD we experienced what it took Tibetan monks 20 years to obtain, yet we got there in 20
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_020.jpg	minutes.”20 Dead wrong.
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_021.jpg	The trouble with drug-induced states is that after the chemical clears your body, you remain the same
test/images/synth_doc_00053_line_022.jpg	person as always. And, as Richie discovered, the same fading away happens with highs in meditation.3
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_000.jpg	The human mind affects the body and the outside world by emitting nerve impulses. Therefore a
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_001.jpg	virtual-reality generator can in principle obtain all the information it needs about what the user is doing by
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_002.jpg	intercepting the nerve signals coming from the user’s brain. Those signals, which would have gone to the
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_003.jpg	user’s body, can instead be transmitted to a computer and decoded to determine exactly how the user’s
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_004.jpg	body would have moved. The signals sent back to the brain by the computer can be the same as those
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_005.jpg	that would have been sent by the body if it were in the specified environment. If thespecification called
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_006.jpg	for it, the simulated body could also react differently from the real one, for example to enable it to survive
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_007.jpg	in simulations of environments that would kill a real human body, or to simulate malfunctions of the
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_008.jpg	body.
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_009.jpg	I had better admit here that it is probably too great an idealization to say that the human mind interacts
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_010.jpg	with the outside world only by emitting and receiving nerve impulses. There are chemical messages
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_011.jpg	passing in both directions as well.
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_012.jpg	I am assuming that in principle those messages could also be intercepted and replaced at some point
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_013.jpg	between the brain and the rest of the body. Thus the user would lie motionless, connected to the
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_014.jpg	computer, but having the experience of interacting fully with a simulated world — in effect, living there.
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_015.jpg	Figure 5.2 illustrates what I am envisaging. Incidentally, though such technology lies well in the future, the
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_016.jpg	idea for it is much older than the theory of computation itself. In the early seventeenth century Descartes
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_017.jpg	was already considering the philosophical implications of a sense- manipulating ‘demon’ that was
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_018.jpg	essentially a virtual-reality generator of the type shown in Figure 5.2, with a supernatural mind replacing
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_019.jpg	the computer. From the foregoing discussion it seems that any virtual-reality generator must have at least
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_020.jpg	three principal components: a set of sensors (which may be nerve-impulse detectors) to detect what the
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_021.jpg	user is doing, a set of image generators (which may be nerve-stimulation devices), and a computer in
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_022.jpg	control. My account so far has concentrated on the first two of these, the sensors and the image
test/images/synth_doc_00055_line_023.jpg	generators.
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_000.jpg	A telegram from friends in India soon after revealed that the “swami” was actually the former manager of
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_001.jpg	a shoe factory who had abandoned his wife and two children and come to America to make his fortune.
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_002.jpg	No doubt Swami X was seeking a marketing edge to attract disciples. In his subsequent appearances he
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_003.jpg	made sure to mention that “scientists at Harvard” had studied his meditative prowess. This was an early
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_004.jpg	harbinger of what has become a bountiful harvest of data refried into sales hype. With such cautionary
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_005.jpg	incidents in mind, we bring open but skeptical minds —the scientist’s mind-set—to the current wave of
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_006.jpg	meditation research.
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_007.jpg	For the most part we view with satisfaction the rise of the mindfulness movement and its rapidly growing
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_008.jpg	reach in schools, business, and our private lives—the wide approach. But we bemoan how the data all too
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_009.jpg	often is distorted or exaggerated when science gets used as a sales hook. The mix of meditation and
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_010.jpg	monetizing has a sorry track record as a recipe for hucksterism, disappointment, even scandal. All too
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_011.jpg	often, gross misrepresentations, questionable claims, or distortions of scientific studies are used to sell
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_012.jpg	meditation. A business website, for instance, features a blog post called “How Mindfulness Fixes Your
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_013.jpg	Brain, Reduces Stress, and Boosts Performance.” Are these claims justified by solid scientific findings?
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_014.jpg	Yes and no —though the “no” too easily gets overlooked. Among the iffy findings gone viral with
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_015.jpg	enthusiastic claims: that meditation thickens the brain’s executive center, the prefrontal cortex, while
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_016.jpg	shrinking the amygdala, the trigger for our freeze-fight-or-flight response; that meditation shifts our
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_017.jpg	brain’s set point for emotions into a more positive range; thatshifts our brain’s set point for emotions into
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_018.jpg	a more positive range; that meditation slows aging; and that meditation can be used to treat diseases
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_019.jpg	ranging from diabetes to attention deficit hyperactivity disorder. On closer look, each of the studies on
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_020.jpg	which these claims are based has problems with the methods used; they need more testing and
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_021.jpg	corroboration to make firm claims.
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_022.jpg	Such findings may well stand up to further scrutiny—or maybe not. The research reporting amygdala
test/images/synth_doc_00056_line_023.jpg	shrinkage, for instance, used a method to estimate amygdala volume that may not be very accurate. And
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_000.jpg	It may therefore seem that we are inferring ever grander conclusions from ever scantier evidence. What
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_001.jpg	justifies these inferences? Can we be sure that just because a star appeared millimetrically displaced on
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_002.jpg	Eddington’s photographic plate, space and time must be curved; or that because a photodetector at a
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_003.jpg	certain position does not register a ‘hit’ in weak light, there must be parallel universes? Indeed, what I have
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_004.jpg	just said understates both the fragility and the indirectness of all experimental evidence.
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_005.jpg	For we do not directly perceive the stars, spots on photographic plates, or any other external objects or
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_006.jpg	events. We see things only when images of them appear on our retinas, and we do not perceive even
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_007.jpg	those images until they have given rise to electrical impulses in our nerves, and those impulses have been
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_008.jpg	received and interpreted by our brains. Thus the physical evidence that directly sways us, and causes us to
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_009.jpg	adopt one theory or world-view rather than another, is less than millimetric: it is measured in thousandths
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_010.jpg	of a millimetre (the separation of nerve fibres in the optic nerve), and in hundredths of a volt (the change
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_011.jpg	in electric potential in our nerves that makes the difference between our perceiving one thing and
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_012.jpg	perceiving another). However, we do not accord equal significance to all our sensory impressions.
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_013.jpg	In scientific experiments we go to great lengths to bring to our perceptions those aspects of external
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_014.jpg	reality that we think might help us to distinguish between rival theories we are considering. Before we
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_015.jpg	even make an observation, we decide carefully where and when we should look, and what we should look
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_016.jpg	for. Often we use complex, specially constructed instruments, such as telescopes and photomultipliers.
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_017.jpg	Yet however sophisticated the instruments we use, and however substantial the external causes to which
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_018.jpg	we attribute their readings, we perceive those readings exclusively through our own sense organs. There is
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_019.jpg	no getting away from the fact that we human beings are small creatures with only a few inaccurate,
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_020.jpg	incomplete channels through which we receive all information from outside ourselves.
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_021.jpg	We interpret this information as evidence of a large and complex external universe (or multiverse). But
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_022.jpg	when we are weighing up this evidence, we are literally contemplating nothing more than patterns of weak
test/images/synth_doc_00058_line_023.jpg	electric current trickling through our own brains. What justifies the inferences we draw from these
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_000.jpg	This might not come as news to people who take psychedelic drugs or to the researchers who first studied
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_001.jpg	them back in the 1950s and 1960s. But it wasn’t at all obvious to modern science, or to me, in 2006, when
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_002.jpg	the paper was published.What was most remarkable about the results reported in the article is that
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_003.jpg	participants ranked their psilocybin experience as one of the most meaningful in their lives, comparable
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_004.jpg	“to the birth of a first child or death of a parent.” Two-thirds of the participants rated the session among
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_005.jpg	the top five “most spiritually significant experiences” of their lives; one-third ranked it the most
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_006.jpg	significant such experience in their lives. Fourteen months later, these ratings had slipped only slightly.
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_007.jpg	The volunteers reported significant improvements in their “personal well-being, life satisfaction and
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_008.jpg	positive behavior change,” changes that were confirmed by their family members and friends. Though no
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_009.jpg	one knew it at the time, the renaissance of psychedelic research now under way began in earnest with the
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_010.jpg	publication of that paper.
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_011.jpg	It led directly to a series of trials—at Hopkins and several other universities—using psilocybin to treat a
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_012.jpg	variety of indications, including anxiety and depression in cancer patients, addiction to nicotine and
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_013.jpg	alcohol, obsessive-compulsive disorder, depression, and eating disorders. What is striking about this
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_014.jpg	whole line of clinical research is the premise that it is not the pharmacological effect of the drug itself but
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_015.jpg	the kind of mental experience it occasions—involving the temporary dissolution of one’s ego—that may
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_016.jpg	be the key to changing one’s mind. • • • AS SOMEONE not at all sure he has ever had a single
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_017.jpg	“spiritually significant” experience, much less enough of them to make a ranking, I found that the 2006
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_018.jpg	paper piqued my curiosity but also my skepticism. Many of the volunteers described being given access to
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_019.jpg	an alternative reality, a “beyond” where the usual physical laws don’t apply and various manifestations of
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_020.jpg	cosmic consciousness or divinity present themselves as unmistakably real. All this I found both a little
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_021.jpg	hard to take (couldn’t this be just a drug- induced hallucination?) and yet at the same time intriguing; part
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_022.jpg	of me wanted it to be true, whatever exactly “it” was.
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_023.jpg	This surprised me, because I have never thought of myself as a particularly spiritual, much less mystical,
test/images/synth_doc_00057_line_024.jpg	person. This is partly a function of worldview, I suppose, and partly of neglect: I’ve never devoted much
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_000.jpg	Yet on his return he somehow was invited to lecture on this notion at a meeting of the Massachusetts
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_001.jpg	Psychological Association. After his talk ended, a slim, bright-eyed young man wearing an ill-fitting sport
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_002.jpg	jacket approached him, saying he was a graduate student in psychology with similar interests.
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_003.jpg	He had spent several years as a monk in Thailand studying meditation, surviving there on the generosity
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_004.jpg	of the Thai people, a country where every household finds it an honor to feed monks. No such luck in
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_005.jpg	New England. This grad student thought that as a psychologist he could adapt meditative tools, in the
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_006.jpg	guise of psychotherapy, to alleviate people’s suffering.
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_007.jpg	He was gladtools, in the guise of psychotherapy, to alleviate people’s suffering. He was glad to hear
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_008.jpg	someone else was making the connection between meditation and therapeutic applications.
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_009.jpg	That grad student was Jack Kornfield, on whose dissertation committee Richie served. Jack became one
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_010.jpg	of the founders of, first, the Insight Meditation Society in Barre, Massachusetts, and then went on to
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_011.jpg	found Spirit Rock, a meditation center in the San Francisco Bay Area. Jack has been a pioneer in
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_012.jpg	translating Buddhist theories of the mind into language attuned to the modern sensibility.16 Jack, along
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_013.jpg	with a group including Joseph Goldstein, designed and ran the teacher training program that graduated
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_014.jpg	the very teachers who helped Steve Z recover from his PTSD all those years later. Jack’s own explanation
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_015.jpg	of Buddhist psychological theories, The Wise Heart, shows how this perspective on the mind and
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_016.jpg	working with meditation can be used in psychotherapy—or on your own.
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_017.jpg	This synthesis was the first of his by now many books integrating traditional Eastern and modern
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_018.jpg	approaches. Another main voice in this movement has been Mark Epstein, a psychiatrist.
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_019.jpg	Mark was a student in Dan’s psychology of consciousness course, and, as a Harvard senior, he asked Dan
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_020.jpg	to be his faculty adviser for an honors project on Buddhist psychology. Dan, at the time the only member
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_021.jpg	of the Harvard psychology department with interest and a bit of knowledge in the area, agreed; Mark and
test/images/synth_doc_00054_line_022.jpg	Dan later wrote an article together in a short-lived journal.17 In a series of books integrating
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_000.jpg	Many of the cancer patients I interviewed described an experience of either giving birth or being reborn,
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_001.jpg	though none quite as intense as Patrick’s. Many also described an encounter with their cancer (or their
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_002.jpg	fear of it) that had the effect of shrinking its power over them. I mentioned earlier the experience of
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_003.jpg	Dinah Bazer, a petite and mild New Yorker in her sixties, a figure-skating instructor, who was diagnosed
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_004.jpg	with ovarian cancer in2010.
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_005.jpg	When we met in the NYU treatment room, Dinah, who has auburn curls and wore large hoop earrings,
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_006.jpg	told me that even after a successful course of chemotherapy she was paralyzed by the fear of a recurrence
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_007.jpg	and wasted her days “waiting for the other shoe to drop.” She too worked with Tony Bossis and in the
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_008.jpg	difficult first moments of her session imagined herself trapped in the hold of a ship, rocking back and
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_009.jpg	forth, consumed by fear. “I stuck my hand out from under the blanket and said, ‘I am so scared.’ Tony
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_010.jpg	took my hand and told me to just go with it. His hand became my anchor. “I saw my fear. Almost as in a
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_011.jpg	dream, my fear was located under my rib cage on the left side; it was not my tumor, but it was this black
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_012.jpg	thing in my body. And it made me immensely angry; I was enraged by my fear.
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_013.jpg	I screamed, ‘Get the fuck out! I won’t be eaten alive.’ And you know what? It was gone! It went away. I
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_014.jpg	drove it away with my anger.” Dinah reports that years later it hasn’t returned. “The cancer is something
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_015.jpg	completely out of my control, but the fear, I realized, is not.” Dinah’s epiphany gave way to feelings of
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_016.jpg	“overwhelming love” as her thoughts turned from her fear to her children.
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_017.jpg	She told me she was and remains a “solid atheist,” and yet “the phrase that I used—which I hate to use
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_018.jpg	but it’s the only way to describe it—is that I felt ‘bathed in God’s love.’” Paradox is a hallmark of the
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_019.jpg	mystical experience, and the contradiction between the divine love Dinah felt and “not having a shred of
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_020.jpg	belief” didn’t seem to faze her. When I pointed this out, she shrugged and then smiled: “What other way
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_021.jpg	is there to express it?” Not surprisingly, visions of death loom large in the journeys taken by the cancer
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_022.jpg	patients I interviewed at NYU and Hopkins. A breast cancer survivor in her sixties (who asked to remain
test/images/synth_doc_00059_line_023.jpg	anonymous) described zipping merrily through space as if in a video game until she arrived smack at the
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_000.jpg	But none of that is true. Explanations are not justified by the means by which they were derived; they are
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_001.jpg	justified by their superior ability, relative to rival explanations, to solve the problems they address. That is
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_002.jpg	why the argument that a theory is indefensible can be so compelling. A prediction, or any assertion, that
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_003.jpg	cannot be defended might still be true, but an explanation that cannot be defended is not an explanation.
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_004.jpg	The rejection of ‘mere’ explanations on the grounds that they are not justified by any ultimate explanation
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_005.jpg	inevitably propels one into futile searches for an ultimate source of justification. There is no such source.
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_006.jpg	Nor is there that hierarchy of reliability from mathematical to scientific to philosophical arguments. Some
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_007.jpg	philosophical arguments, including the argument against solipsism, are far more compelling than any
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_008.jpg	scientific argument. Indeed, every scientific argument assumes the falsity not only of solipsism, but also of
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_009.jpg	other philosophical theories including any number of variants of solipsism that might contradict specific
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_010.jpg	parts of the scientific argument.
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_011.jpg	I shall also show (in Chapter 10) that even purely mathematical arguments derive their reliability from the
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_012.jpg	physical and philosophical theories that underpin them, and therefore that they cannot, after all, yield
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_013.jpg	absolute certainty. Having embraced realism, we are continually faced with decisions as to whether entities
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_014.jpg	referred to in competing explanations are real or not. Deciding that they are not real — as we did in the
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_015.jpg	case of the ‘angel’ theory of planetary motion — is equivalent to rejecting the corresponding explanation.
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_016.jpg	Thus, in searching for and judging explanations, we need more than just a refutation of solipsism.
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_017.jpg	We need to develop reasons for accepting or rejecting the existence of entities that may appear in
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_018.jpg	contending theories; in other words, we need a criterion for reality. We should not, of course, expect to
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_019.jpg	find a final or an infallible criterion. Our judgements of what is or isnot real always depend on the various
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_020.jpg	explanations that are available to us, and sometimes change as our explanations improve. In the
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_021.jpg	nineteenth century, few things would have been regarded more confidently as real than the force of
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_022.jpg	gravity. Not only did it figure in Newton’s then-unrivalled system of laws, but everyone could feel it, all
test/images/synth_doc_00060_line_023.jpg	the time, even with their eyes shut — or so they thought.
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_000.jpg	As each of them in turn passed through a courtyard on the way to give their sermon, they passed a man
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_001.jpg	who was bent over and moaning in pain. The question: Did they stop to help the stranger in need? Turns
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_002.jpg	out whether a divinity student helped or not depended on how late that student felt—the more
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_003.jpg	time-pressured, the less likely to stop.2 When we are rushing through a busy day, worried about getting to
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_004.jpg	the next place on time, we tend literally not to notice the people around us, let alone their needs. There’s a
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_005.jpg	spectrum that runs from self-centered preoccupations (I’m late!), to noticing the people around us, to
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_006.jpg	tuning in to them, empathizing, and finally, if they are in need, acting to help. Holding the attitude of
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_007.jpg	compassion means we merely espouse this virtue; embodying compassion means we act.
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_008.jpg	The students pondering the Good Samaritan likely were appreciating his compassion—but were not more
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_009.jpg	likely to act with compassion themselves. Several meditation methods aim to cultivate compassion.
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_010.jpg	The scientific (and ethical) question is, Does this matter—does it move people toward compassionate
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_011.jpg	action? MAY ALL BEINGS BE FREE FROM SUFFERING During Dan’s first stay in India, in
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_012.jpg	December 1970, he was asked to lecture at a conference on yoga and science in New Delhi. Among the
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_013.jpg	many Western travelers who came to hear Dan was Sharon Salzberg, then an eighteen-year-old doing an
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_014.jpg	independent study year from the State University of New York at Buffalo. Sharon had joined the
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_015.jpg	thousands of young Westerners who made the overland journey from Europe through the Near East to
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_016.jpg	India in the 1970s, travel that warfare and politics have made virtually impossible today.Dan mentioned
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_017.jpg	that he had just come from a vipassana course given by S. N.
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_018.jpg	Goenka in Bodh Gaya, and that a series of these ten-day retreats was continuing. Sharon was among the
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_019.jpg	handful of Westerners who headed straight from Delhi to the Burmese vihara in Bodh Gaya to take part.
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_020.jpg	She became an ardent student of the method and continued her meditation studies with teachers in India
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_021.jpg	and Burma, and after returning to the States became a teacher herself, cofounding the Insight Meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_022.jpg	Society in Massachusetts—along with Joseph Goldstein, whom she met at the vihara. Sharon has become
test/images/synth_doc_00061_line_023.jpg	the leading advocate of a method she first learned from Goenka, called metta in Pali and loosely translated
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_000.jpg	As I have said, the modern theories are fewer, more general and deeper. For each situation that the master
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_001.jpg	builder faced while building something in his repertoire — say, when deciding how thick to make a
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_002.jpg	load-bearing wall — he had a fairly specific intuition or rule of thumb, which, however, could give
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_003.jpg	hopelessly wrong answers if applied to novel situations. Today one deduces such things from a theory
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_004.jpg	that is general enough for it to be applied to walls made of any material, in all situations: on the Moon,
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_005.jpg	underwater, or wherever. The reason why it is so general is that it is based on quite deep explanations of
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_006.jpg	how materials and structures work. To find the proper thickness of a wall that is to be made from an
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_007.jpg	unfamiliar material, one uses the same theory as for any other wall, but starts the calculation by assuming
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_008.jpg	different facts — by using different numerical values for the various parameters.
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_009.jpg	One has to look up those facts, such as the tensile strength and elasticity of the material, but one needs no
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_010.jpg	additional understanding. That is why, despite understanding incomparably more than an ancient master
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_011.jpg	builder did, a modern architect does not require a longer or morearduous training. A typical theory in a
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_012.jpg	modern student’s syllabus may be harder to understand than any of the master builder’s rules of thumb;
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_013.jpg	but the modern theories are far fewer, and their explanatory power gives them other properties such as
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_014.jpg	beauty, inner logic and connections with other subjects which make them easier to learn. Some of the
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_015.jpg	ancient rules of thumb are now known to be erroneous, while others are known to be true, or to be good
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_016.jpg	approximations to the truth, and we know why that is so. A few are still in use.
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_017.jpg	But none of them is any longer the source of anyone’s understanding of what makes structures stand up. I
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_018.jpg	am not, of course, denying that specialization is occurring in many subjects in which knowledge is
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_019.jpg	growing, including architecture. This is not a one-way process, for specializations often disappear too:
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_020.jpg	wheels are no longer designed or made by wheelwrights, nor ploughs by ploughwrights, nor are letters
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_021.jpg	written by scribes. It is nevertheless quite evident that the deepening, unifying tendency I have been
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_022.jpg	describing is not the only one at work: a continual broadening is going on at the same time.
test/images/synth_doc_00062_line_023.jpg	That is, new ideas often do more than just supersede, simplify or unify existing ones. They also extend
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_000.jpg	Let us consider this environment. Clearly it is a physically possible environment.
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_001.jpg	Is it a renderable environment? Of course. In fact it isexceptionally easy to render: one simply uses a
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_002.jpg	second flight simulator of the same design, running the identical program. Under those circumstances the
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_003.jpg	second flight simulator can be thought of as rendering either the physically impossible aircraft, or a
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_004.jpg	physically possible environment, namely the first flight simulator.
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_005.jpg	Similarly, the first flight simulator could be regarded as rendering a physically possible environment,
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_006.jpg	namely the second flight simulator. If we assume that any virtual-reality generator that can in principle be
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_007.jpg	built, can in principle be built again, then it follows that every virtual-reality generator, running any
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_008.jpg	program in its repertoire, is rendering some physically possible environment.
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_009.jpg	It may be rendering other things as well, including physically impossible environments, but in particular
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_010.jpg	there is always some physically possible environment that it is rendering. So, which physically impossible
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_011.jpg	environments can be rendered in virtual reality?
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_012.jpg	Precisely those that are not perceptibly different from physically possible environments. Therefore the
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_013.jpg	connection between the physical world and the worlds that are renderable in virtual reality is far closer
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_014.jpg	than it looks. We think of some virtual-reality renderings as depicting fact, and others as depicting fiction,
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_015.jpg	but the fiction is always an interpretation in the mind of the beholder. There is no such thing as a
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_016.jpg	virtual-reality environment that the user would be compelled to interpret as physically impossible. We
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_017.jpg	might choose to render an environment as predicted by some ‘laws of physics’ that are different from the
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_018.jpg	true laws of physics.
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_019.jpg	We may do this as an exercise, or for fun, or as an approximation because the true rendering is too
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_020.jpg	difficult or expensive. If the laws we are using are as close as we can make them to real ones, given the
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_021.jpg	constraints under which we are operating, we may call these renderings ‘applied mathematics’ or
test/images/synth_doc_00063_line_022.jpg	‘computing’.
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_000.jpg	Or Transcendental Meditation (TM), which offers classic Sanskrit mantras to the modern world in a
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_001.jpg	user-friendly format. The even more widely accessible forms of meditation at Level 4 are, of necessity, the
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_002.jpg	most watered-down, all the better to render them handy for the largest number of people. The current
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_003.jpg	vogues of mindfulness-at-your-desk, orlargest number of people.
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_004.jpg	The current vogues of mindfulness-at-your-desk, or via minutes-long meditation apps, exemplify this
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_005.jpg	level. We foresee also a Level 5, one that exists now only in bits and pieces, but which may well increase
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_006.jpg	in number and reach with time. At Level 5, the lessons scientists have learned in studying all the other
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_007.jpg	levels will lead to innovations and adaptations that can be of widest benefit—a potential we explore in the
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_008.jpg	final chapter, “A Healthy Mind.” The deep transformations of Level 1 fascinated us when we originally
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_009.jpg	encountered meditation.
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_010.jpg	Dan studied ancient texts and practiced the methods they describe, particularly during the two years he
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_011.jpg	lived in India and Sri Lanka in his grad school days and just afterward. Richie (as everyone calls him)
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_012.jpg	followed Dan to Asia for a lengthy visit, likewise practicing on retreat there, meeting with meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_013.jpg	scholars—and more recently has scanned the brains of Olympic-level meditators in his lab at the
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_014.jpg	University of Wisconsin. Our own meditation practice has been mainly at Level 2. But from the start, the
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_015.jpg	wide path, Levels 3 and 4, has also been important to us.
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_016.jpg	Our Asian teachers said if any aspect of meditation could help alleviate suffering, it should be offered to
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_017.jpg	all, not just those on a spiritual search. Our doctoral dissertations applied that advice by studying ways
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_018.jpg	meditation could have cognitive and emotional payoffs.
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_019.jpg	The story we tell here mirrors our own personal and professional journey. We have been close friends and
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_020.jpg	collaborators on the science of meditation since the 1970s, when we met at Harvard during graduate
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_021.jpg	school, and we have both been practitioners of this inner art over all these years (although we are
test/images/synth_doc_00064_line_022.jpg	nowhere near mastery).
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_000.jpg	As the mask began to rotate, gradually bringing its back side into view, the whole thing dissolved into a
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_001.jpg	gray jelly that slid down the screen of my laptop before I could determine whether the melting mask I was
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_002.jpg	watching was convex or concave. So much for conducting psychological experiments while tripping. I put
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_003.jpg	on my eyeshades and sank back down into what now became a cracked and parched desert landscape
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_004.jpg	dense with artifacts and images of death.
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_005.jpg	Bleached skulls and bones and the faces of the familiar dead passed before me, aunts and uncles and
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_006.jpg	grandparents, friends and teachers and my father-in-law—with a voice telling me I had failed to properly
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_007.jpg	mourn all of them. It was true.
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_008.jpg	I had never really reckoned the death of anyone in my life; something had always gotten in the way. I
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_009.jpg	could do it here and now and did.
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_010.jpg	I looked hard at each of their faces, one after another, with a pity that seemed bottomless but with no fear
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_011.jpg	whatsoever. Except once, when Icame to my aunt Ruthellen and watched, horrified, as her face slowly
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_012.jpg	transformed into Judith’s. Ruthellen and Judith were both artists, and both had been diagnosed with
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_013.jpg	breast cancer around the same time.
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_014.jpg	The cancer had killed Ruthellen and spared Judith. So what was Judith doing down here among the
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_015.jpg	unmourned dead?
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_016.jpg	Had I been defending myself against that possibility all this time? Heart wide open, defenses melting, the
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_017.jpg	tears began to flow. • • • I’VE LEFT OUT one important part of my journey to the underworld: the
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_018.jpg	soundtrack.
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_019.jpg	Before going back under for this last passage, I had asked Mary to please stop playing spa music and put
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_020.jpg	on something classical. We settled on the second of Bach’s unaccompanied cello suites, performed by
test/images/synth_doc_00067_line_021.jpg	Yo-Yo Ma. The suite in D minor is a spare and mournful piece that I’d heard many times before, often at
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_000.jpg	But to everyone’s shock, instead of going into a remote hermitage with an attendant along to cook and
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_001.jpg	care for him as is traditional, he disappeared one night from his monastery in Bodh Gaya, India, taking
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_002.jpg	only his robes, a bit of cash, and an ID card. During his odyssey Mingyur lived as a wandering mendicant,
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_003.jpg	spending winters as a sadhu on the plains of India and during the warmer months inhabiting Himalayan
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_004.jpg	caves where fabled Tibetan masters had stayed.
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_005.jpg	Such a wandering retreat, not uncommon in old Tibet, has become rare, especially among Tibetans like
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_006.jpg	Mingyur whose diaspora has brought them into the modern world. During those wandering years there
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_007.jpg	was not a word from him, save once when he was recognized by a Taiwanese nun at a retreat cave.
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_008.jpg	He gave her awhen he was recognized by a Taiwanese nun at a retreat cave. He gave her a letter (telling
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_009.jpg	her to send it after he had moved on) that said not to worry, he was fine—and exhorting his students to
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_010.jpg	practice. A photo that surfaced when a monk, a longtime friend, managed to join Mingyur shows a radiant
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_011.jpg	face with a wispy beard and long hair, his expression one of ebullient rapture. Then, suddenly, in
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_012.jpg	November 2015, after almost four and a half years as a wanderer in radio silence, Mingyur reappeared at
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_013.jpg	his monastery in Bodh Gaya.
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_014.jpg	On hearing that news, Richie arranged to see him during a visit to India that December. Months later,
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_015.jpg	Mingyur stopped in Madison while on an American teaching tour, and stayed at Richie’s house. Within
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_016.jpg	minutes of his arrival at the house Mingyur agreed to go back into the scanner. Only a few months after
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_017.jpg	returning from his hardscrabble life he seemed right at home in this up-to-the-minute lab. As Mingyur
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_018.jpg	entered the MRI suite, the lab technician gave him a friendly welcome, saying, “I was the tech the last time
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_019.jpg	you were in the scanner.” Mingyur beamed his electric smile in return.
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_020.jpg	While he waited for the machine to be readied, Mingyur joked with another member of Richie’s team, an
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_021.jpg	Indian scientist from Hyderabad. Given the go-ahead, Mingyur left his sandals at the bottom of the
test/images/synth_doc_00068_line_022.jpg	two-step ladder that boosted him to the MRI table and lay down so the tech could strap his head into a

test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_000.jpg	At the Garrison Institute, an hour up the Hudson River from New York City, one hundred scientists,
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_001.jpg	graduate students, and postdocs had gathered for the first in what has become a yearly series of events, the
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_002.jpg	Summer Research Institute (SRI), a gathering devoted to furthering the rigorous study of meditation. The
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_003.jpg	meetings are organized by the Mind and Life Institute, itself formed in 1987 by the Dalai Lama, Francisco,
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_004.jpg	and Adam Engle, a lawyer turned businessman.
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_005.jpg	We were founding board members. The mission of Mind and Life is “to alleviate suffering and promote
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_006.jpg	flourishing by integrating science with contemplative practice.” Mind and Life’s summer institute, we felt,
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_007.jpg	could offer a more welcoming reality for those who, like us in our grad school days, wanted to do research
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_008.jpg	on meditation. While we had been isolated pioneers, we wanted to knit together a community of
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_009.jpg	like-minded scholars and scientists who shared this quest. They could be supportive of each other’s work
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_010.jpg	at a distance, even if they were alone in their interests at their own institution. Details of the SRI were
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_011.jpg	hatched over the kitchen table in Richie’s home in Madison, in a conversation with Adam Engle.
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_012.jpg	Richie and a handful of scientistsMadison, in a conversation with Adam Engle. Richie and a handful of
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_013.jpg	scientists and scholars then organized the first summer program and served as faculty for the week,
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_014.jpg	featuring topics like the cognitive neuroscience of attention and mental imagery.
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_015.jpg	As of this writing, thirteen more meetings have followed (with two so far in Europe, and possibly future
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_016.jpg	meetings in Asia and South America). Beginning with the very first SRI, the Mind and Life Institute began
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_017.jpg	a program of small grants named in honor of Francisco. These few dozen, very modest Varela research
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_018.jpg	awards (up to $25,000, though most research of this kind takes far more in funding) have leveraged more
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_019.jpg	than $60 million in follow-on funding from foundations and US federal granting agencies.
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_020.jpg	And the initiative has borne plentiful fruit: fifty or so graduates of the SRI have published several hundred
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_021.jpg	papers on meditation. As these young scientists entered academic posts, they swelled the numbers of
test/images/synth_doc_00069_line_022.jpg	researchers doing such studies. They have driven in no small part the ever- growing numbers of scientific
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_000.jpg	Worse, someone may reach a better understanding that explains not only all existing observations but also
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_001.jpg	why the previous explanations seemed to work but are nevertheless quite wrong. Galileo, for instance,
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_002.jpg	found new explanation of the age-old observation that the ground beneath our feet is at rest, an
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_003.jpg	explanation that involved the ground actually moving. Virtual reality — which can make one environment
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_004.jpg	seem to be another — underlines the fact that when observation is the ultimate arbiter between theories,
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_005.jpg	there can never be any certainty that an existing explanation, however obvious, is even remotely true. But
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_006.jpg	when proof is the arbiter, it is supposed, there can be certainty.
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_007.jpg	It is said that the rules of logic were first formulated in the hope that they would provide an impartial and
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_008.jpg	infallible method of resolving all disputes. This hope can never be fulfilled. The study of logic itself
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_009.jpg	revealed that the scope of logical deduction as a means of discovering the truth is severely limited.
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_010.jpg	Given substantive assumptions about the world, one can deduceconclusions; but the conclusions are no
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_011.jpg	more secure than the assumptions. The only repositions that logic can prove without recourse to
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_012.jpg	assumptions are tautologies — statements such as ‘all planets are planets’, which assert nothing.
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_013.jpg	In particular, all substantive questions of science lie outside the domain in which logic alone can settle
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_014.jpg	disputes. But mathematics, it is supposed, lies inside that domain. Thus mathematicians seek absolute but
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_015.jpg	abstract truth, while scientists console themselves with the thought that they can gain substantive and
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_016.jpg	useful knowledge of the physical world.
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_017.jpg	But they must accept that this knowledge comes without guarantees. It is forever tentative, forever fallible.
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_018.jpg	The idea that science is characterized by ‘induction’, a method of justification which is supposed to be a
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_019.jpg	slightly fallible analogue of logical deduction, is an attempt to make the best of this perceived second-class
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_020.jpg	status of scientific knowledge. Instead of deductively justified certainties, perhaps we can make do with
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_021.jpg	inductively justified near- certainties.
test/images/synth_doc_00066_line_022.jpg	As I have said, there is no such method of justification as ‘induction’. The idea of reasoning one’s way to
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_000.jpg	In most other nearby universes, the first of the two segments has the same sequence, TCGTCGTTTC, as
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_001.jpg	it does in our universe, but the second segment varies greatly between nearby universes. So from the
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_002.jpg	multiverse perspective the two segments are not even remotely alike (Figure 8.1). Again we were too
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_003.jpg	parochial, and were led to the false conclusion: that knowledge-bearing entities can be physically identical
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_004.jpg	to non knowledge- bearing ones; and this in turn cast doubt on the fundamental status of knowledge. But
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_005.jpg	now we have come almost full circle. We can see that the ancient idea that living matter has special
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_006.jpg	physical properties was almost true: it is not living matter but knowledge-bearing matter that is physically
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_007.jpg	special.
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_008.jpg	Within one universe it looks irregular; across universes it has a regular structure, like a crystal in the
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_009.jpg	multiverse. So knowledge is a fundamental physical quantity after all, and the phenomenon of life is only
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_010.jpg	slightly less so. Imagine looking through an electron microscope at a DNA molecule from a bear’s cell,
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_011.jpg	and trying to distinguish the genes from the non-gene sequences and to estimate the degree of adaptation
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_012.jpg	of each gene. In any one universe, this task is impossible. The property of being a gene — that is, of being
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_013.jpg	highly adapted — is, in so far as it can be detected within one universe, overwhelmingly complicated.
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_014.jpg	It is an emergent property. You would have to make many copies of the DNA, with variations, use
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_015.jpg	genetic engineering tocreate many bear embryos for each variant of the DNA, allow the bears to grow up
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_016.jpg	and live in a variety of environments representative of the bear’s niche, and see which bears succeed in
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_017.jpg	having offspring. FIGURE 8.1 Multiverse view of two DNA segments which happen to be identical in
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_018.jpg	our universe, one random and one from within a gene. But with a magic microscope that could see into
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_019.jpg	other universes (which, I stress, is not possible: we are using theory to imagine — or render — what we
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_020.jpg	know must be there) the task would be easy. As in Figure 8.1, the genes would stand out from the
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_021.jpg	non-genes just as cultivated fields stand out from a jungle in an aerial photograph, or like crystals that
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_022.jpg	have precipitated from solution.
test/images/synth_doc_00070_line_023.jpg	They are regular across many nearby universes, while all the non- gene, junk-DNA segments are irregular.
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_000.jpg	In fact, the ‘theory of everything’ is expected to inherit virtually its entire explanatory structure — its
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_001.jpg	physical concepts, its language, its mathematical formalism and the form of its explanations — from the
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_002.jpg	existing theories of electromagnetism, nuclear forces and gravity. Therefore we may look to this
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_003.jpg	underlying structure, which we already know from existing theories, for the contribution of fundamental
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_004.jpg	physics to our overall understanding.
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_005.jpg	There are two theories in physics which are considerably deeper than all others. The first is the general
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_006.jpg	theory of relativity, which as I have said is our best theory of space, time and gravity. The second,
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_007.jpg	quantum theory, is even deeper. Between them, these two theories (and not any existing or currently
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_008.jpg	envisaged theory of subatomic particles) provide the detailed explanatory and formal framework within
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_009.jpg	which all other theories in modern physics are expressed, and they contain overarching physical principles
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_010.jpg	to which all other theories conform. A unification of general relativity and quantum theory — to give a
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_011.jpg	quantum theory of gravity — has been a major quest of theoretical physicists for several decades, and
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_012.jpg	would have to form part of any theory of everything in either the narrow or the broad sense of the term.
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_013.jpg	As we shall see in the next chapter, quantum theory, like relativity, provides a revolutionary new mode of
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_014.jpg	explanation of physical reality. The reason why quantum theory is the deeper of the two lies more outside
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_015.jpg	physics than within it, for its ramifications are very wide, extending far beyond physics — and even
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_016.jpg	beyond science itself as it is normally conceived. Quantum theory is one of what I shall call the four main
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_017.jpg	strands of which our current understanding of the fabric of reality is composed.
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_018.jpg	Before I say what the other three strands are, I must mention another way in which reductionism
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_019.jpg	misrepresents the structure of scientific knowledge. Not only does it assume that explanation always
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_020.jpg	consists of analysing a system into smaller, simpler systems, it also assumes that all explanation is of later
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_021.jpg	events in terms of earlier events; in other words, that the only way of explaining something is to state its
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_022.jpg	causes. And this implies that the earlier the events in terms of which we explain something, the better
test/images/synth_doc_00071_line_023.jpg	theexplanation, so that ultimately the best explanations of all are in terms of the initial state of the
