test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_000.jpg	The story became national news, introducing millions of Americans to the controversy surrounding these
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_001.jpg	exotic new drugs. It also earned Andrew Weil a plum assignment from Look magazine to write about the
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_002.jpg	controversy, which spread the story still further.
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_003.jpg	Describing the psychedelic scene at Harvard in the third person, Weil alluded to “an undergraduate group
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_004.jpg	. . . conducting covert research with mescaline,” neglecting to mention he was a founding member of that
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_005.jpg	group. This was not, suffice it to say, Andrew Weil’s proudest moment, and when I spoke to him about it
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_006.jpg	recently, he confessed that he’s felt badly about the episode ever since and had sought to make amends to
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_007.jpg	both Leary and Ram Dass. (Two years after his departure from Harvard, Alpert embarked on a spiritual
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_008.jpg	journey to India and returned as Ram Dass.)Leary readily accepted Weil’s apology—the man was
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_009.jpg	apparently incapable of holding a grudge—but Ram Dass refused to talk to Weil for years, which pained
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_010.jpg	him. But after Ram Dass suffered a stroke in 1997, Weil traveled to Hawaii to seek his forgiveness. Ram
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_011.jpg	Dass finally relented, telling Weil that he had come to regard being fired from Harvard as a blessing. “If
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_012.jpg	you hadn’t done what you did,” he told Weil, “I would never have become Ram Dass.” • • • HERE,
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_013.jpg	UPON THEIR EXIT from Harvard, we should probably take our leave of Timothy Leary and Richard
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_014.jpg	Alpert, even though their long, strange trip through American culture still had a long, strange way to go.
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_015.jpg	The two would now take their show (with its numerous ex-students and hangers- on) on the road, moving
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_016.jpg	the International Federation for Internal Freedom (which would later morph into the League for Spiritual
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_017.jpg	Discovery) from Cambridge to Zihuatanejo, until the Mexican government (under pressure from U.S.
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_018.jpg	authorities) kicked them out, then briefly to the Caribbean island of Dominica, until that government
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_019.jpg	kicked them out, before finally settling for several raucous years in a sixty-four- room mansion in
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_020.jpg	Millbrook, New York, owned by a wealthy patron named Billy Hitchcock. Embraced by the rising
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_021.jpg	counterculture, Leary was invited (along with Allen Ginsberg) to speak at the first Human Be-In in San
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_022.jpg	Francisco, an event that drew some twenty-five thousand young people to Golden Gate Park in January
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_023.jpg	1967, to trip on freely distributed LSD while listening to speakers proclaim a new age. The ex-professor,
test/images/synth_doc_00072_line_024.jpg	who for the occasion had traded in his Brooks Brothers for white robes and love beads (and flowers in
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_000.jpg	They observe this by the same means, and according to the same definition, as we apply when we say that
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_001.jpg	the universe we observe is ‘tangible’. Tangibility is relative to a given observer. So objectively there are not
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_002.jpg	two kinds of photon, tangible and shadow, nor two kinds of frog, nor two kinds of universe, one tangible
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_003.jpg	and the rest shadow.
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_004.jpg	There is nothing in the description I have given of the formation of shadows, or any of the related
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_005.jpg	phenomena, that distinguishes between the ‘tangible’ and the ‘shadow’ objects, apart from the mere
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_006.jpg	assertion that one of the copies is ‘tangible’. When I introduced tangible and shadow photons I apparently
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_007.jpg	distinguished them by saying that we can see the former, but not the latter. But who are ‘we’? While I was
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_008.jpg	writing that, hosts of shadow Davids were writing it too. They too drew a distinction between tangible
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_009.jpg	and shadow photons; but the photons they called ‘shadow’ include the ones I called ‘tangible’, and the
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_010.jpg	photons they called ‘tangible’ are among those I called ‘shadow’.
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_011.jpg	Not only do none of the copies of an object have any privileged position in the explanation of shadows
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_012.jpg	that I have just outlined, neither do they have a privileged position in the full mathematical explanation
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_013.jpg	provided by quantum theory. I may feel subjectively that I am distinguished among the copies as the
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_014.jpg	‘tangible’ one, because I can directly perceive myself and not the others, but I must come to terms with
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_015.jpg	the fact that all the others feel the same about themselves.
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_016.jpg	Many of those Davids are at this moment writing these very words. Some are putting it better. Others
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_017.jpg	have gone for a cup of tea. TERMINOLOGY photon A particle of light. tangible/shadow For the
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_018.jpg	purposes of exposition in this chapter only, I called particles in this universe tangible, and particles in
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_019.jpg	other universes shadow particles. multiverse The whole of physical reality.
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_020.jpg	It contains many parallel universes. parallel universes They are ‘parallel’ in the sense that within each
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_021.jpg	universe particles interact with each other just as they do in the tangible universe, but each universe affects
test/images/synth_doc_00074_line_022.jpg	the others only weakly, through interference phenomena. quantum theory The theory of the physics of
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_000.jpg	Immediately after my session with Andrei, I had a meetingwith a second prospective guide, a brilliant
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_001.jpg	psychologist in his eighties who had been a student of Timothy Leary’s at Harvard. His knowledge of
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_002.jpg	psychedelics was deep; his credentials impressive; he had been highly recommended by people I
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_003.jpg	respected. Yet when over lunch at a Tibetan restaurant near his office he removed his bolo tie and
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_004.jpg	suspended it over the menu, I began to lose confidence that this was my man.
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_005.jpg	He explained that he relied on the energies released by the pendulum swing of the silver clasp to choose
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_006.jpg	the entrée most likely to agree with his temperamental digestion. I forget what his tie ordered for lunch,
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_007.jpg	but even before he began dilating on the evidence that 9/11 was an inside job, I knew my search for a
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_008.jpg	guide was not over quite yet. • • • ONE NOTABLE DIFFERENCE about doing psychedelics at sixty, as
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_009.jpg	opposed to when you’re eighteen or twenty, is that at sixty you’re more likely to have a cardiologist you
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_010.jpg	might want to consult in advance of your trip. That was me. A year before I had decided to embark on
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_011.jpg	this adventure, my heart, the reliable operations of which I had taken completely for granted to that point,
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_012.jpg	had suddenly made its presence felt and, for the first time in my life, demanded my attention. While sitting
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_013.jpg	at my computer one afternoon, I was suddenly made aware of a pronounced and crazily syncopated new
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_014.jpg	rhythm in my chest. “Atrial fibrillation” was the name the doctor gave the abnormal squiggles that
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_015.jpg	appeared on my EKG.
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_016.jpg	The danger of AFib is not a heart attack, he said to my (short-lived) relief, but a heightened risk of stroke.
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_017.jpg	“My cardiologist”—the unfortunate phrase had suddenly joined my vocabulary, probably for the
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_018.jpg	duration—put me on a couple of meds to calm the heart rhythms and lower the blood pressure, plus a
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_019.jpg	daily baby aspirin to thin my blood. And then he told me not to worry about it. I followed all of his advice
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_020.jpg	except the last bit.
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_021.jpg	Now I couldn’t help but think about my heart constantly. All of its operations that had previously taken
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_022.jpg	place completely outside my conscious awareness suddenly became salient: something I could hear and
test/images/synth_doc_00077_line_023.jpg	feel whenever I thought to check in, which now was incessantly. Months later, the AFib had not recurred,
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_000.jpg	A few years ago, Stamets won a patent for a “mycopesticide”—a mutant mycelium from a species of
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_001.jpg	Cordyceps that, after being eaten by carpenter ants, colonizes their bodies and kills them, but not before
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_002.jpg	chemically inducing the ant to climb to the highest point in its environment and then bursting a
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_003.jpg	mushroom from the top of its head that releases its spores to the wind. The second or third time I
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_004.jpg	watched Stamets show a video of a Cordyceps doing its diabolical thing to an ant—commandeering its
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_005.jpg	body, making it do its bidding, and then exploding a mushroom from its brain in order to disseminate its
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_006.jpg	genes—it occurred to me that Stamets and that poor ant had rather a lot in common. Fungi haven’t killed
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_007.jpg	him, it’s true,and he probably knows enough about their wiles to head off that fate. But it’s also true that
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_008.jpg	this man’s life—his brain!—has been utterly taken over by fungi; he has dedicated himself to their cause,
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_009.jpg	speaking for the mushrooms in the same way that Dr. Seuss’s Lorax speaks for the trees.
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_010.jpg	He disseminates fungal spores far and wide, helping them, whether by mail order or sheer dint of his
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_011.jpg	enthusiasm, to vastly expand their range and spread their message. • • • I DON’T THINK I’m saying
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_012.jpg	anything about Paul Stamets to which he would object. He writes in his book that mycelia—the vast,
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_013.jpg	cobwebby whitish net of single-celled filaments, called hyphae, with which fungi weave their way through
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_014.jpg	the soil—are intelligent, forming “a sentient membrane” and “the neurological network of nature.” The
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_015.jpg	title of his book Mycelium Running can be read in two ways. The mycelium is indeed always running
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_016.jpg	through the ground, where it plays a critical role in forming soils, keeping plants and animals in good
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_017.jpg	health, and knitting together the forest. But the mycelium are also, in Stamets’s view, running the show—
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_018.jpg	that of nature in general and, like a neural software program, the minds of certain creatures, including, he
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_019.jpg	would be the first to tell you, Paul Stamets himself. “Mushrooms are bringing us a message from nature,”
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_020.jpg	he likes to say. “This is a call I’m hearing.” Yet even some of Stamets’s airier notions turn out to have a
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_021.jpg	scientific foundation beneath them.
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_022.jpg	For years now, Stamets has been talking about the vast web of mycelia in the soil as “Earth’s natural
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_023.jpg	Internet”—a redundant, complexly branched, self-repairing, and scalable communications network linking
test/images/synth_doc_00078_line_024.jpg	many species over tremendous distances. (The biggest organism on earth is not a whale or a tree but a
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_000.jpg	Like gold, a small amount of light can be evenly spread over a very large area, but eventually if one tries to
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_001.jpg	spread it out further it gets lumpy. Even if gold atoms could somehow be prevented from clumping
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_002.jpg	together, there is a point beyond which they cannot be subdivided without ceasing to be gold.
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_003.jpg	So the only way in which one can make a one-atom-thick gold sheet even thinner is to space the atoms
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_004.jpg	farther apart, with empty space between them. When they are sufficiently far apart it becomes misleading
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_005.jpg	to think of them as forming a continuous sheet. For example, if each gold atom were on average several
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_006.jpg	centimetres from its nearest neighbour, one might pass one’s hand through the ‘sheet’ without touching
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_007.jpg	any gold at all. Similarly, there is an ultimate lump or ‘atom’ of light, a photon. Each flicker seen by the
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_008.jpg	frog is caused by a photon striking the retina of its eye.
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_009.jpg	What happens when a beam of light gets fainter is not that the photons themselves get fainter, but that
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_010.jpg	they get farther apart, with empty space between them (Figure 2.2). When the beam is very faint it can be
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_011.jpg	misleading to call it a ‘beam’, for it is not continuous. During periods when the frog sees nothing it is not
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_012.jpg	because the light entering its eye is too weak to affect the retina, but because no light has entered its eye at
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_014.jpg	This property of appearing only in lumps of discrete sizes is called quantization. An individual lump, such
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_015.jpg	as a photon, is called a quantum (plural quanta). Quantum theory gets its name from this property, which
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_016.jpg	it attributes to all measurable physical quantities — not just to things like the amount of light, or the mass
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_017.jpg	of gold, which are quantized because the entities concerned, though apparently continuous, are really
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_018.jpg	made of particles.
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_019.jpg	Even for quantities like distance (between two atoms, say), the notion of a continuous range of possible
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_020.jpg	values turns out to be an idealization. There are no measurable continuous quantities in physics. There are
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_021.jpg	many new effects in quantum physics, and on the face of it quantization is one of the tamest, as we shall
test/images/synth_doc_00076_line_022.jpg	see. Yet in a sense it remains the key to all the others, for if everything is quantized, how does any quantity
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_000.jpg	Tellingly, their brains seemed to disconnect the usual link between executive center circuits where we
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_001.jpg	evaluate (This hurts!) and circuitry for sensing physical pain (This burns).In short, the Zen meditators
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_002.jpg	seemed to respond to pain as though it was a more neutral sensation. In more technical language, their
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_003.jpg	brains showed a “functional decoupling” of the higher and lower brain regions that register pain —while
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_004.jpg	their sensory circuitry felt the pain, their thoughts and emotions did not react to it.
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_005.jpg	This offers a new twist on a strategy sometimes used in cognitive therapy: reappraisal of severe
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_006.jpg	stress—thinking about it in a less threatening way —which can lessen its subjective severity as well as the
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_007.jpg	brain’s response. Here, though, the Zen meditators seemed to apply a no-appraisal neural strategy—in
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_008.jpg	keeping with the mind-set of zazen itself. A close reading of this article reveals a mention only in passing
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_009.jpg	of a significant trait effect, in a difference found between Zen meditators and the comparison group.
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_010.jpg	During the initial baseline reading the temperature is increased in a staircase-like series of finely graduated
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_011.jpg	rises to calibrate the precise maximum pain threshold for each person. The Zen practitioners’ pain
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_012.jpg	threshold was 2 degrees Centigrade (5.6 degrees Fahrenheit) higher than for nonmeditators.
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_013.jpg	This may not sound like much, but the way we experience pain from heat means that slight increases in
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_014.jpg	temperature can have dramatic impact both subjectively and in how our brain responds. Though that
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_015.jpg	difference of 2 degrees Centigrade may seem trivial, in the world of pain experience, it is huge.
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_016.jpg	Researchers are, appropriately, skeptical about such traitlike findings because self-selection in who
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_017.jpg	chooses to stick with meditation and who drops out along the way might also account for such data;
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_018.jpg	perhaps people who choose to meditate for years and years are already different in ways that look like trait
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_019.jpg	effects.
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_020.jpg	The maxim “Correlation does not mean causation” applies here. But if a trait can be understood as a
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_021.jpg	lasting effect of the practice, that poses an alternative explanation.
test/images/synth_doc_00075_line_022.jpg	And when different research groups come up with similar trait findings, these converging results make us
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_000.jpg	At each stage, we would have a concept that made no sense; and the whole infinite hierarchy would make
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_001.jpg	no sense either.The origin of this sort of mistake is that we are accustomed to time being a framework
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_002.jpg	exterior to any physical entity we may be considering. We are used to imagining any physical object as
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_003.jpg	potentially changing, and so existing as a sequence of versions of itself at different moments. But the
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_004.jpg	sequence of moments itself, in pictures like Figures 11.1—11.3, is an exceptional entity. It does not exist
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_005.jpg	within the framework of time — it is the framework of time.
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_006.jpg	Since there is no time outside it, it is incoherent to imagine it changing or existing in more than one
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_007.jpg	consecutive version. This makes such pictures hard to grasp.
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_008.jpg	The picture itself, like any other physical object, does exist over a period of time and does consist of
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_009.jpg	multiple versions of itself. But what the picture depicts — namely, the sequence of versions of something
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_010.jpg	— exists in only one version.
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_011.jpg	No accurate picture of the framework of time can be a moving or changing picture. It must be static. But
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_012.jpg	there is an inherent psychological difficulty in taking this on board. Although the picture is static, we
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_013.jpg	cannot understand it statically. It shows a sequence of moments simultaneously on the page, and in order
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_014.jpg	to relate that to our experience the focus of our attention must move along the sequence.
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_015.jpg	For example, we might look at one snapshot, and take it to represent ‘now’, and a moment later look at a
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_016.jpg	snapshot to the right of it and think of that as representing the new ‘now’. Then we tend to confuse the
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_017.jpg	genuine motion of our focus of attention across the mere picture, with the impossible motion of
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_018.jpg	something through real moments. It is easily done. But there is more to this problem than the difficulty of
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_019.jpg	illustrating the common-sense theory of time.
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_020.jpg	The theory itself contains a substantive and deep equivocation: it cannot make up its mind whether the
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_021.jpg	present is, objectively, a single moment or many — and hence, for example, whether Figure 11.1 depicts
test/images/synth_doc_00079_line_022.jpg	one moment or many. Common sense wants the present to be a single moment so as to allow the flow of
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_000.jpg	But in the classical theory of proof or computation this makes no fundamental difference, for the
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_001.jpg	following reason. If we can go through the process of a proof, we can, with only a moderate amount
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_002.jpg	of extra effort, keep a record of everything relevant that happens during that process. That record, a
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_003.jpg	physical object, will constitute a proof in the sequence-of-statements sense.
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_004.jpg	And conversely, if we have such a record we can read through it, checking that it satisfies the rules of
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_005.jpg	inference, and in the process of doing so we shall have proved the conclusion. In other words, in the
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_006.jpg	classical case, converting between proof processes and proof objects is always a tractable task. Now
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_007.jpg	consider some mathematical calculation that is intractable on all classical computers, but suppose
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_008.jpg	that a quantum computer can easily perform it using interference between, say, 10 500 universes.
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_009.jpg	To make the point more clearly, let the calculation be such that the answer (unlike the result of a
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_010.jpg	factorization) cannot be tractably verified once we have it. The process of programming a quantum
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_011.jpg	computer to perform such a computation, running the program and obtaining a result, constitutes a
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_012.jpg	proof that the mathematical calculation has that particular result. But now there is no way of keeping
test/images/synth_doc_00081_line_013.jpg	a record of everything that happened during the proof process, because most of it happened in other
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_000.jpg	But refer to it they do. A rose by any other name would smell as sweet.
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_001.jpg	Suppose that you — indeed suppose that everyone — were a native speaker of your language, and
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_002.jpg	believed your theory of gravity to be true. Suppose that we all took it entirely for granted, and thought
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_003.jpg	it so natural that we used the same word ‘x-fall’ to describe what you or I would do if we jumped over
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_004.jpg	the railing.
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_005.jpg	None of that alters in the slightest degree the obvious difference there would be between my response
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_006.jpg	to gravity and everything else’s. If you fell over the railing, you might well envy me on the way down.
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_007.jpg	You might well think, ‘if only I could respond to gravity as David does, rather than in this entirely
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_008.jpg	different way that I do!’ CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: That’s true. Just because the same word ‘x-falling’
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_009.jpg	describes your response to gravity and mine, I wouldn’t think that the actual response is the same. On
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_010.jpg	the contrary, being a fluent speaker of this supposed language, I’d know very well that ‘x-falling’ was
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_011.jpg	physically different for you and for me, just as a native English speaker knows that the words ‘being
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_012.jpg	drunk’ mean something physically different for a person and for a glass of water. I wouldn’t think, ‘if
test/images/synth_doc_00082_line_013.jpg	this had happened to David, he’d be x- falling just as I am’.
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_000.jpg	If the measurements were irrelevant to what they were doing, or if their brain failed to meet some
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_001.jpg	scientific expectation, it might look to some as though their methods were of no use. That, they said,
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_002.jpg	might discourage those on the same path.
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_003.jpg	Whatever the reasons, the net result of this scientific expedition was a resounding nothing. Despite the
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_004.jpg	failure to get cooperation, let alone data, and though futile in the short term, the exercise proved
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_005.jpg	instructive, beginning a steep learning curve. For starters, better to bring the meditators to the
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_006.jpg	equipment, especially in a well- fortified brain lab—if they would come. For another, research on such
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_007.jpg	adepts confronts unique challenges beyond their rarity, their intentional remoteness, and their
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_008.jpg	unfamiliarity with or disinterest in scientific endeavors.
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_009.jpg	While their mastery at this inner expertise seems akin to world-class rankings in sports, in this “sport,”
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_010.jpg	the better you get the less you care about your ranking—let alone social status, riches, or fame. That
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_011.jpg	list of indifferences includes any personal pride you might take in what scientific measures show
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_012.jpg	about your inner accomplishments. What mattered to them was how the results might influence
test/images/synth_doc_00085_line_013.jpg	others for better or worse. Prospects for scientific studies were dim. A SCIENTIST AND A MONKEnter
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_000.jpg	There were signs that the door Washington, D.C., had slammed shut on research in the late 1960s
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_001.jpg	might be opening, if only a crack: Curtis Wright, a new administrator at the FDA (and, as it happens, a
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_002.jpg	former student of Roland Griffiths’s at Hopkins), had signaled that research protocols for psychedelics
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_003.jpg	would be treated like any other—judged on their merits. Testing this new receptivity, a psychiatrist at
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_004.jpg	the University of New Mexico named Rick Strassman had sought and received approval to study the
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_005.jpg	physiological effects of DMT, a powerful psychedelic compound found in many plants. This small trial
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_006.jpg	marked the first federally sanctioned experiment with a psychedelic compound since the 1970s—in
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_007.jpg	retrospect, a watershed event. Around the same time, Rick Doblin and Charles Grob, a psychiatrist at
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_008.jpg	UCLA, had succeeded in persuading the government to approve the first human trial of MDMA. (Grob
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_009.jpg	is one of the first psychiatrists to advocate for the return of psychedelics to psychotherapy; he later
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_010.jpg	conducted the first modern trial of psilocybin for cancer patients.
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_011.jpg	The year before the Esalen gathering (which Grob and Doblin both attended), David Nichols, a Purdue
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_012.jpg	University chemist and pharmacologist, launched the Heffter Research Institute (named for the
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_013.jpg	German chemist who first identified the mescaline compound in 1897) with the then improbable
test/images/synth_doc_00083_line_014.jpg	ambition of funding serious psychedelic science. (Heffter has since helped fund many of the modern
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_000.jpg	So objectively there are not two kinds of photon, tangible and shadow, nor two kinds of frog, nor two
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_001.jpg	kinds of universe, one tangible and the rest shadow. There is nothing in the description I have given of
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_002.jpg	the formation of shadows, or any of the related phenomena, that distinguishes between the ‘tangible’
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_003.jpg	and the ‘shadow’ objects, apart from the mere assertion that one of the copies is ‘tangible’. When I
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_004.jpg	introduced tangible and shadow photons I apparently distinguished them by saying that we can see
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_005.jpg	the former, but not the latter. But who are ‘we’? While I was writing that, hosts of shadow Davids were
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_006.jpg	writing it too.
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_007.jpg	They too drew a distinction between tangible and shadow photons; but the photons they called
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_008.jpg	‘shadow’ include the ones I called ‘tangible’, and the photons they called ‘tangible’ are among those I
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_009.jpg	called ‘shadow’. Not only do none of the copies of an object have any privileged position in the
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_010.jpg	explanation of shadows that I have just outlined, neither do they have a privileged position in the full
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_011.jpg	mathematical explanation provided by quantum theory. I may feel subjectively that I am
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_012.jpg	distinguished among the copies as the ‘tangible’ one, because I can directly perceive myself and not
test/images/synth_doc_00086_line_013.jpg	the others, but I must come to terms with the fact that all the others feel the same about themselves.
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_000.jpg	Tony Bossis and Krystallia Kalliontzi, his guides, greeted him, reviewed the day’s plans, and then at 9:00
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_001.jpg	a.m. presented Patrick with a chalice containing the pill; whether it contained psilocybin or the placebo,
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_002.jpg	none of them would know for at least thirty minutes. Patrick was asked to state his intention, which he

test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_006.jpg	and eyeshades, and fell quiet.
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_007.jpg	In his account, Patrick likened the start of the journey to the launch of a space shuttle: “a physically
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_008.jpg	violent and rather clunky liftoff which eventually gave way to the blissful serenity of weightlessness.”Many
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_009.jpg	of the volunteers I interviewed reported initial episodes of intense fear and anxiety before giving
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_010.jpg	themselves up to the experience, as the guides encourage them to do. This is where the flight instructions
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_011.jpg	come in. Their promise is that if you surrender to whatever happens (“trust, let go, and be open” or “relax
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_012.jpg	and float downstream”), whatever at first might seem terrifying will soon morph into something else, and
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_013.jpg	likely something pleasant, even blissful. Early in his journey, Patrick encountered his brother’s wife, who
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_014.jpg	died of cancer more than twenty years earlier, at forty-three. “Ruth acted as my tour guide,” he wrote, and
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_015.jpg	“didn’t seem surprised to see me. She ‘wore’ her translucent body so I would know her . . .

test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_018.jpg	her shortcomings . . . could never NOT love her offspring. This was very powerful.
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_019.jpg	I knew I was crying . . . it was here that I felt as if I was coming out of the womb . . . being birthed again.
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_020.jpg	My rebirth was smooth . . . comforting.” Outwardly, however, what was happening to Patrick appeared to
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_021.jpg	be anything but smooth. He was crying, Bossis noted, and breathing heavily. This is when he first said,
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_022.jpg	“Birth and death is a lot of work,” and seemed to be convulsing. Then Patrick reached out and clutched
test/images/synth_doc_00080_line_023.jpg	Kalliontzi’s hand while pulling up his knees and pushing, as if he were delivering a baby.
test/images/synth_doc_00087_line_000.jpg	He was also said to have traveled to Mecca in the 1930s with a MuslimHe was also said to have

test/images/synth_doc_00087_line_010.jpg	In that view contemplative paths are more or less the same, a doorway beyond ordinary experience.
test/images/synth_doc_00087_line_011.jpg	At a practical level, all forms of meditation share a common core of mind training—e.g., learning to

test/images/synth_doc_00088_line_000.jpg	Dark nights are not unique to vipassana; most every meditative tradition warns about them. In

test/images/synth_doc_00088_line_007.jpg	The proportion of dark nights among all those who do prolonged retreats are, by all accounts, very

test/images/synth_doc_00088_line_011.jpg	million, were found by the National Institute of Mental Health to suffer from a mental illness in any

test/images/synth_doc_00084_line_000.jpg	In one experiment, she presented children with a toy box that lights up and plays music when a

test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_000.jpg	But if we take the view that science is about explanations, we see that this rule is really a special case
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_001.jpg	of something that applies naturally to all problem-solving: theories that are capable of giving more
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_002.jpg	detailed explanations are automatically preferred. They are preferred for two reasons. One is that a
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_003.jpg	theory that ‘sticks its neck out’ by being more specific about more phenomena opens up itself and its
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_004.jpg	rivals to more forms of criticism, and therefore has more chance of taking the problem-solving
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_005.jpg	process forward. The second is simply that, if such a theory survives the criticism, it leaves less
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_006.jpg	unexplained — which is the object of the exercise. FIGURE 3.3 The course of scientific discovery.
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_007.jpg	I have already remarked that even in science most criticism does not consist of experimental testing.
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_008.jpg	That is because most scientific criticism is directed not at a theory’s predictions but directly at the
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_009.jpg	underlying explanations. Testing the predictions is just an indirect way (albeit an exceptionally
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_010.jpg	powerful one, when available) of testing the explanations. In Chapter 1, I gave the example of the
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_011.jpg	‘grass cure’ — the theory that eating a kilogram of grass is a cure for the common cold.
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_012.jpg	That theory and an infinity of others of the same ilk are readily testable. But we can criticize and reject
test/images/synth_doc_00089_line_013.jpg	them without bothering to do any experiments, purely on the grounds that they explain no more than
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_000.jpg	DAVID: So your additional postulate is not just superfluous, it is positively bad. In general, perverse
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_001.jpg	but unrefuted theories which one can propose off the cuff fall roughly into two categories. There are
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_002.jpg	theories that postulate unobservable entities, such as particles that do not interact with any other
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_003.jpg	matter. They can be rejected for solving nothing (‘Occam’s razor’, if you like).
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_004.jpg	And there are theories, like yours, that predict unexplained observable anomalies. They can be
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_005.jpg	rejected for solving nothing and spoiling existing solutions.
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_006.jpg	It is not, I hasten to add, that they conflict with existing observations. It is that they remove the
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_007.jpg	explanatory power from existing theories by asserting that the predictions of those theories have
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_008.jpg	exceptions, but not explaining how. You can’t just say ‘spacetime geometry brings unsupported
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_009.jpg	objects together, unless one of them is David, in which case it leaves them alone’. Either the
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_010.jpg	explanation of gravity is spacetime curvature or it isn’t. Just compare your theory with the perfectly
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_011.jpg	legitimate assertion that a feather would float down slowly because there would indeed be a sufficient
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_012.jpg	upward force on it from the air.
test/images/synth_doc_00090_line_013.jpg	That assertion is a consequence of our existing explanatory theory of what air is, so it raises no new
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_000.jpg	Andrei, the first guide I interviewed, was a gruff Romanian-born psychologist in his late sixties with
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_001.jpg	decades of experience; he had worked with a friend of a friend of a friend. We met at his office in a
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_002.jpg	modest neighborhood of small bungalows and neat lawns in a city in the Pacific Northwest. A
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_003.jpg	hand-lettered sign on the door instructed visitors to remove their shoes and come upstairs to the
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_004.jpg	dimly lit waiting room.
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_005.jpg	A kilim rug had been pinned to the wall. Instead of a table piled with old copies of People or
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_006.jpg	Consumer Reports, I found a small shrine populated with spiritual artifacts from a bewildering variety
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_007.jpg	of traditions: a Buddha, a crystal, a crow’s wing, a brass bowl for burning incense, a branch of sage.
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_008.jpg	At the back of the shrine stood two framed photographs, one of a Hindu guru I didn’t recognize and
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_009.jpg	the other of a Mexican curandera I did: María Sabina. This was not the last time I would encounter
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_010.jpg	such a confusing tableau. In fact every guide I met maintained some such shrine in the room where
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_011.jpg	he or she worked, and clients were often asked to contribute an item of personal significance before
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_012.jpg	embarking on their journeys.
test/images/synth_doc_00092_line_013.jpg	What I was tempted to dismiss as a smorgasbord of equal-opportunity New Age tchotchkes, I would
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_000.jpg	I had been looking forward to trying an azzie, but before the evening was over, Stamets had
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_001.jpg	dampened my enthusiasm. “I find azurescens almost too strong,” he told me when we were standing
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_002.jpg	around the fire pit outside our yurt, having a beer. After nightfall, we had driven out onto the beach to
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_003.jpg	hunt for razor clams by headlight; now we were sautéing them with onions over the fire. “And azzies
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_004.jpg	have one potential side effect that some people find troubling.” Yes?“Temporary paralysis,” he said
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_005.jpg	matter-of-factly. He explained that some people on azzies find they can’t move their muscles for a
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_006.jpg	period of time. That might be tolerable if you’re in a safe place, he suggested, “but what if you’re
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_007.jpg	outdoors and the weather turns cold and wet? You could die of hypothermia.” Not much of an
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_008.jpg	advertisement for azurescens, especially coming from the man who discovered the species and
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_009.jpg	named it.
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_010.jpg	I was suddenly in much less of a hurry to try one. • • • THE QUESTION I KEPT returning to that weekend
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_011.jpg	is this: Why in the world would a fungus go to the trouble of producing a chemical compound that
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_012.jpg	has such a radical effect on the minds of the animals that eat it? What, if anything, did this peculiar
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_013.jpg	chemical do for the mushroom? One could construct a quasi-mystical explanation for this
test/images/synth_doc_00091_line_014.jpg	phenomenon, as Stamets and McKenna have done: both suggest that neurochemistry is the language
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_000.jpg	In chapter thirteen, “Altering Traits,” we lay out the benefits of meditation at three levels: beginner,
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_001.jpg	long-term, and “Olympic.” In our final chapter we speculate on what the future might bring, and how
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_002.jpg	these findings might be of greater benefit not just to each of us individually but to society. THE
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_003.jpg	ACCELERATION As early as the 1830s, Thoreau and Emerson, along with their fellow American
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_004.jpg	Transcendentalists, flirted with these Eastern inner arts.
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_005.jpg	They were spurred bythe first English-language translations of ancient spiritual texts from Asia—but
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_006.jpg	had no instruction in the practices that supported those texts. Almost a century later, Sigmund Freud
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_007.jpg	advised psychoanalysts to adopt an “even-hovering attention” while listening to their clients—but
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_008.jpg	again, offered no method.
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_009.jpg	The West’s more serious engagement took hold mere decades ago, as teachers from the East arrived,
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_010.jpg	and as a generation of Westerners traveled to study meditation in Asia, some returning as teachers.
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_011.jpg	These forays paved the way for the current acceleration of the wide path, along with fresh possibilities
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_012.jpg	for those few who choose to pursue the deep way. Publication Count for Scientific Studies on
test/images/synth_doc_00094_line_013.jpg	Meditation or Mindfulness, 1970–2016 In the 1970s, when we began publishing our research on
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_000.jpg	Known physics provides no way other than free fall, even in principle, of removing an object’s weight.
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_001.jpg	The only way of putting a flight simulator into free fall while it remained stationary on the surface of
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_002.jpg	the Earth would be somehow to suspend a massive body, such as another planet of similar mass, or a
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_003.jpg	black hole, above it. Even if this were possible (remember, we are concerned here not with immediate
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_004.jpg	practicality, but with what the laws of physics do or do not permit), a real aircraft could also produce
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_005.jpg	frequent, complex changes in the magnitude and direction of the occupants’ weight by manoeuvring
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_006.jpg	or by switching its engines on and off.
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_007.jpg	To simulate these changes, the massive body would have to be moved around just as frequently, and
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_008.jpg	it seems likely that the speed of light (if nothing else) would impose an absolute limit on how fast this
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_009.jpg	could be done. However, to simulate free fall a flight simulator would not have to provide real
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_010.jpg	weightlessness, only the experience of weightlessness, and various techniques which do not involve
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_011.jpg	free fall have been used to approximate that. For example, astronauts train under water in spacesuits
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_012.jpg	that are weighted so as to have zero buoyancy. Another technique is to use a harness that carries the
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_013.jpg	astronaut through the air under computer control to mimic weightlessness. But these methods are
test/images/synth_doc_00093_line_014.jpg	crude, and the sensations they produce could hardly be mistaken for the real thing, let alone be
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_000.jpg	So what makes them compelling? This is the ‘problem of induction’. According to inductivism, scientific
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_001.jpg	theories are discovered by extrapolating the results of observations, and justified when corroborating
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_002.jpg	observations are obtained. In fact, inductive reasoning is invalid, and it is impossible to extrapolate
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_003.jpg	observations unless one already has an explanatory framework for them. But the refutation of
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_004.jpg	inductivism, and also the real solution of the problem of induction, depends on recognizing that
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_005.jpg	science is a process not of deriving predictions from observations, but of finding explanations.
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_006.jpg	We seek explanations when we encounter a problem with existing ones. We then embark on a
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_007.jpg	problem-solving process.
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_008.jpg	New explanatory theories begin as unjustified conjectures, which are criticized and compared
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_009.jpg	according to the criteria inherent in the problem. Those that fail to survive this criticism are
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_010.jpg	abandoned. The survivors become the new prevailing theories, some of which are themselves
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_011.jpg	problematic and so lead us to seek even better explanations. The whole process resembles biological
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_012.jpg	evolution. Thus we acquire ever more knowledge of reality by solving problems and finding better
test/images/synth_doc_00097_line_013.jpg	explanations.
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_000.jpg	So in the spring of 1953, Humphry Osmond traveled to Los Angeles to administer mescaline to Aldous
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_001.jpg	Huxley, though not without some trepidation. In advance of the session, he confided to a colleague
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_002.jpg	that he did not “relish the possibility, however remote, of finding a small but discreditable niche in
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_003.jpg	literary history as the man who drove Aldous Huxley mad.” He need not have worried. Huxley had a
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_004.jpg	splendid trip, one that would change forever the culture’s understanding of these drugs when, the
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_005.jpg	following year, he published his account of his experience in The Doors of Perception.“It was without
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_006.jpg	question the most extraordinary and significant experience this side of the Beatific Vision,” Huxley
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_007.jpg	wrote in a letter to his editor shortly after it happened. For Huxley, there was no question but that the
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_008.jpg	drugs gave him access not to the mind of the madman but to a spiritual realm of ineffable beauty.
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_009.jpg	The most mundane objects glowed with the light of a divinity he called “the Mind at Large.” Even “the
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_010.jpg	folds of my gray flannel trousers were charged with ‘is-ness,’” he tells us, before dilating on the beauty
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_011.jpg	of the draperies in Botticelli’s paintings and the “Allness and Infinity of folded cloth.” When he gazed
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_012.jpg	upon a small vase of flowers, he saw “what Adam had seen on the morning of his creation—the
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_013.jpg	miracle, moment by moment, of naked existence . . . flowers shining with their own inner light and all
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_014.jpg	but quivering under the pressure of the significance with which they were charged.” “Words like ‘grace’
test/images/synth_doc_00095_line_015.jpg	and ‘transfiguration’ came to my mind.” For Huxley, the drug gave him unmediated access to realms
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_000.jpg	I realize there are just some domains that science will not penetrate. Science can bring you to the big
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_001.jpg	bang, but it can’t take you beyond it.
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_002.jpg	You need a different kind of apparatus to peer into that.” These anecdotal reports of personal
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_003.jpg	transformation found strong support in a follow-up study done on the first groups of healthy normals
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_004.jpg	studied at Hopkins. Katherine MacLean, a psychologist on the Hopkins team, crunched the survey
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_005.jpg	data produced by fifty-two volunteers, including follow-up interviews with friends and family members
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_006.jpg	they had designated, and discovered that in many cases the psilocybin experience had led to lasting
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_007.jpg	changes in their personalities. Specifically, those volunteers who had “complete mystical experiences”
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_008.jpg	(as determined by their scores on the Pahnke-Richards Mystical Experience Questionnaire) showed, in
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_009.jpg	addition to lasting improvements in well-being, long-term increases in the personality trait of
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_010.jpg	“openness to experience.” One of the five traits psychologists use to assess personality (the other four
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_011.jpg	are conscientiousness, extroversion, agreeableness, and neuroticism), openness encompasses
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_012.jpg	aesthetic appreciation and sensitivity, fantasy and imagination, as well as tolerance of others’
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_013.jpg	viewpoints and values; it also predicts creativity in both the arts and the sciences, as well as,
test/images/synth_doc_00096_line_014.jpg	presumably, a willingness to entertain ideas at odds with those of current science. Such pronounced
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_000.jpg	As mentioned, when we are watching a movie and are lost in its story, but then notice that we are in a
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_001.jpg	movie theater watching a film, we have stepped outof the movie’s world into a large frame that
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_002.jpg	includes the movie but goes beyond. Having such meta-awareness allows us to monitor our thoughts,
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_003.jpg	feelings, and actions; to manage them as we like; and to inquire into their dynamics.
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_004.jpg	Our sense of self gets woven in an ongoing personal narrative that threads together disparate parts
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_005.jpg	of our life into a coherent story line. This narrator resides mainly in the default mode but brings
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_006.jpg	together inputs from a broad range of brain areas that in themselves have nothing to do with the
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_007.jpg	sense of self.
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_008.jpg	The seasoned meditators in the Brewer study had the same strong connection between the control
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_009.jpg	circuit and the default mode seen in beginners, but in addition had less activation within the default
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_010.jpg	mode areas themselves. This was particularly true when they practiced loving-kindness meditation—a
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_011.jpg	corroboration of the maxim that the more we think of the well-being of others, the less we focus on
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_012.jpg	ourselves.8 Intriguingly, the long-term meditators seemed to have roughly the same lessened
test/images/synth_doc_00098_line_013.jpg	connectivity in the default mode circuitry while they just rested before the test as they displayed
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_000.jpg	They do intensive sessions under the watchful eye of a coach, who suggests to them what to work on
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_001.jpg	next toget even better. This leads to a continuous learning curve with steady improvements. These
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_002.jpg	findings point to the need for a teacher, someone more advanced than you are, who can give you
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_003.jpg	coaching on how to improve.
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_004.jpg	Both of us have continued to seek guidance from meditation teachers over the years, but the
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_005.jpg	opportunity occurs sporadically in our lives. The Visuddhimagga advises practitioners to find as a
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_006.jpg	guide someone more experienced than they are. This ancient list of potential teachers starts at the top
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_007.jpg	with, ideally, direction from an arhant (the Pali word for a fully accomplished meditator, someone at
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_008.jpg	the Olympic level).
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_009.jpg	If none is available, it advises, just find someone more seasoned than you—at the very least, they
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_010.jpg	should have read a sutra, a passage from a holy text—if you have read none. In today’s world, that
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_011.jpg	might be the equivalent of getting instruction from someone who had tried out a meditation app—it’s
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_012.jpg	better than nothing. BRAIN MATCHING “Your program,” Dan wrote to Jon Kabat-Zinn, “could spread
test/images/synth_doc_00100_line_013.jpg	throughout the healthcare system.” Little did he know. The year was 1983, and Jon was still working
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_000.jpg	DAVID: It is not perfectly secure. Nor should we expect it to be, for logical reasoning is no less a
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_001.jpg	physical process than scientific reasoning is, and it is inherently fallible. The laws of logic are not
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_002.jpg	self-evident. There are people, the mathematical ‘intuitionists’, who disagree with the conventional
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_003.jpg	laws of deduction (the logical ‘rules of inference’). I discuss their strange world-view in Chapter 10 of
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_004.jpg	The Fabric of Reality.
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_005.jpg	They cannot be proved wrong, but I shall argue that they are wrong, and I am sure you will agree that
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_006.jpg	my argument justifies this conclusion. CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: So you don’t think that there is a
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_007.jpg	‘problem of deduction’, then? DAVID: No.
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_008.jpg	I don’t think that there is a problem with any of the usual ways of justifying conclusions in science,
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_009.jpg	philosophy or mathematics. However, it is an interesting fact that the physical universe admits
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_010.jpg	processes that create knowledge about itself, and about other things too. We may reasonably try to
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_011.jpg	explain this fact in the same way as we explain other physical facts, namely through explanatory
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_012.jpg	theories. You will see in Chapter 6 of The Fabric of Reality that I think that the Turing principle is the
test/images/synth_doc_00102_line_013.jpg	appropriate theory in this case.
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_000.jpg	It was in the family room of a pub called the Fighting Cocks in St. Albans.
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_001.jpg	I was ten.” Antidepressants helped for a while, but “putting the plaster over the wound doesn’t heal
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_002.jpg	anything.” On psilocybin, he was able for the first time to confront his lifelong pain—and his father.
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_003.jpg	“Normally, when Dad comes up in my head, I just push the thought away. But this time I went the
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_004.jpg	other way.” His guide had told him he should “go in and through” any frightening material that arose
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_005.jpg	during his journey. “So this time I looked him in the eye. That was a really big thing for me, to literally
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_006.jpg	face the demon. And there he was. But he was a horse!
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_007.jpg	A military horse standing on its hind legs, dressed in a military outfit with a helmet, and holding a
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_008.jpg	gun. It was terrifying, and I wanted to push theimage aside, but I didn’t. In and through: Instead, I
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_009.jpg	looked the horse in the eyes—and promptly started to laugh, it was so ridiculous. “That’s when what
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_010.jpg	had been a bad trip really turned.
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_011.jpg	Now I had every sort of emotion, positive, negative, it didn’t matter. I thought about the [Syrian]
test/images/synth_doc_00099_line_012.jpg	refugees in Calais and started crying for them, and I saw that every emotion is as valid as any other.
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_000.jpg	Galileo believed that the planets move in circles, while in fact their orbits are very nearly ellipses. So
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_001.jpg	the data did not fit the particular heliocentric theory that Galileo was defending either.
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_002.jpg	(So much, then, for his having been convinced by accumulated observations! But for all that, the
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_003.jpg	Church took no position in this controversy.
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_004.jpg	The Inquisition did not care where the planets appeared to be; what they cared about was reality.
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_005.jpg	They cared where the planets really were, and they wanted to understand the planets through
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_006.jpg	explanations, just as Galileo did. Instrumentalists and positivists would say that since the Church was
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_007.jpg	perfectly willing to accept Galileo’s observational predictions, further argument between them was
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_008.jpg	pointless, and that his muttering ‘eppur si muove’ was strictly meaningless. But Galileo knew better,
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_009.jpg	and so did the Inquisition. When they denied the reliability of scientific knowledge, it was precisely the
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_010.jpg	explanatory part of that knowledge that they had in mind.
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_011.jpg	Their world-view was false, but it was not illogical. Admittedly they believed in revelation and
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_012.jpg	traditional authority as sources of reliable knowledge. But they also had an independent reason for
test/images/synth_doc_00101_line_013.jpg	criticizing the reliability of knowledge obtained by Galileo’s methods. They could simply point out that
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_000.jpg	It is virtually impossible to die from an overdose of LSD or psilocybin, for example, and neither drug is
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_001.jpg	addictive. After trying them once, animals will not seek a second dose, and repeated use by people
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_002.jpg	robs the drugs of their effect.* It is true that the terrifying experiences some people have on
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_003.jpg	psychedelics can risk flipping those at risk into psychosis, so no one with a family history or
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_004.jpg	predisposition to mental illness should ever take them. But emergency room admissions involving
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_005.jpg	psychedelics are exceedingly rare, and many of the cases doctors diagnose as psychotic breaks turn
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_006.jpg	out to be merely short-lived panic attacks.
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_007.jpg	It is also the case that people on psychedelics are liable to do stupid and dangerous things: walk out
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_008.jpg	into traffic, fall from high places, and, on rare occasions, kill themselves. “Bad trips” are very real and
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_009.jpg	can be one of “the most challenging experiences of [a] lifetime,” according to a large survey of
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_010.jpg	psychedelic users asked about their experiences.* But it’s important to distinguish what can happen
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_011.jpg	when these drugs are used in uncontrolled situations, without attention to set and setting, from what
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_012.jpg	happens under clinical conditions, after careful screening and under supervision. Since the revival of
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_013.jpg	sanctioned psychedelic researchbeginning in the 1990s, nearly a thousand volunteers have been
test/images/synth_doc_00103_line_014.jpg	dosed, and not a single serious adverse event has been reported. • • • IT WAS AT THIS POINT that the
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_000.jpg	You can all punch out now. Our work is done.” But it wasn’t done, not yet. Now “I took a tour of my
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_001.jpg	lungs . . . I remember breathing deeply to help facilitate the ‘seeing.’” Bossis notedthat at 2:30 Patrick
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_002.jpg	had said, “I went into my lungs and saw two spots. They were no big deal. “I was being told (without
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_003.jpg	words) not to worry about the cancer . . . it’s minor in the scheme of things . . . simply an imperfection
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_004.jpg	of your humanity and that the more important matter . . . the real work to be done is before you.
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_005.jpg	Again, love.” Now Patrick experienced what he called “a brief death.” “I approached what appeared to
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_006.jpg	be a very sharp, pointed piece of stainless steel. It had a razor blade quality to it. I continued up to the
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_007.jpg	apex of this shiny metal object and as I arrived, I had a choice, to look or not look, over the edge and
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_008.jpg	into the infinite abyss . . . the vastness of the universe . . . the eye of everything . . .
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_009.jpg	[and] of nothing. I was hesitant but not frightened. I wanted to go all in but felt that if I did, I would
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_010.jpg	possibly leave my body permanently . . . death from this life. But it was not a difficult decision . . .
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_011.jpg	I knew there was much more for me here.” Telling his guides about his choice, Patrick explained that
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_012.jpg	he “was not ready to jump off and leave Lisa.” Then, rather suddenly around 3:00 p.m., it was over.
test/images/synth_doc_00104_line_013.jpg	“The transition from a state where I had no sense of time or space to the relative dullness of now,
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_000.jpg	CODACODA “What if, by transforming our minds, we could improve not only our own health and
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_001.jpg	well-being but also those of our communities and the wider world?” That rhetorical question, too,
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_002.jpg	comes from the internal notice at the National Institutes of Health about Richie’s talk there. So, what
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_003.jpg	if? We envision a world where widespread mental fitness deeply alters society for the better. We hope
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_004.jpg	the scientific case we make here shows the enormous potential for enduring well-being from caring
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_005.jpg	for our minds and brains, and convinces you that a little daily mental exercise can go a long way
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_006.jpg	toward the cultivation of that well-being. Signs of such flourishing include increasing generosity,
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_007.jpg	kindness and focus, and a less rigid division between “us” and “them.” In light of increases in empathy
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_008.jpg	and perspective taking from various kinds of meditation, we think it likely that these practices will
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_009.jpg	produce a greater sense of our interdependence on one another and with the planet.
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_010.jpg	When nurtured on a grand scale, these qualities—particularly kindness and compassion—would
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_011.jpg	inevitably lead to changes for the better in our communities, our nations, and our societies. These
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_012.jpg	positive altered traits have the potential for transforming our world in ways that will enhance not only
test/images/synth_doc_00105_line_013.jpg	our individual thriving but also the odds for our species’ survival.
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_000.jpg	And the most important thing of all is the breath. When that stops, you’re dead.” She emerged from
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_001.jpg	her journey with the conviction “that you should cherish your breath.” She has not had a cigarette
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_002.jpg	since her psilocybin journey.
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_003.jpg	Whenever she feels a craving, she goes back in memory to her session “and thinks of all the wonderful
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_004.jpg	things I experienced, and how it felt to be on that much higher plane.” Charles Bessant had his
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_005.jpg	epiphany while on a similarly “higher plane.” Bessant, a museum exhibit designer in his sixties, found
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_006.jpg	himself standing on a mountaintop in the Alps, “the German states stretching out before me all the
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_007.jpg	way to the Baltic.” (Wagner was playing in his headphones.) “My ego had dissolved, yet I’m telling you
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_008.jpg	this. It was terrifying.” He sounded like a nineteenth-century Romantic describing an encounter with
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_009.jpg	the sublime, at once terrible and awe inspiring. “People use words like ‘oneness,’ ‘connectivity,’
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_010.jpg	‘unity’—I get it! I was part of something so much larger than anything I had ever imagined.” We were
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_011.jpg	speaking by phone on a Saturday morning, and at one point Bessant paused in his account to
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_012.jpg	describe the scene before him. “Right now, I’m standing here in my garden, and the light is coming
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_013.jpg	through the canopy of leaves. For me to be able to stand here in the beauty of this light, talking to
test/images/synth_doc_00106_line_014.jpg	you, it’s only because my eyes are open tosee it. If you don’t stop to look, you’ll never see it.
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_000.jpg	More right-side activity than left correlated with negative moods like depression and anxiety; relatively
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_001.jpg	more left-side activity was associated with buoyant moods like energy and enthusiasm. That ratio
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_002.jpg	appeared to predict a person’s day-to-day mood range.
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_003.jpg	For the general population this ratio seemed to fit a bell curve, with most of us in the middle—we
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_004.jpg	have good days and bad days. A very few people are at the extremes of the curve; if toward the left,
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_005.jpg	they bounce back from feeling down, if toward the right they might be clinically anxious or depressed.
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_006.jpg	The study at the biotech start-up seemed to show a remarkable shift in brain function after the
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_007.jpg	meditation training—from tilting toward the right to a leftward pitch, and reporting a switch into a
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_008.jpg	more relaxed state.
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_009.jpg	There were no such changes in a comparison group of workers assigned to a wait list, who were told
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_010.jpg	they would receive the meditation training later. But here’s one major hitch. This research was never
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_011.jpg	replicated, and was designed only as a pilot.
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_012.jpg	We don’t know, for instance, if an active control like HEP would result in similar benefits. While that
test/images/synth_doc_00107_line_013.jpg	study was never replicated, others seem to support the finding on the brain ratio and its shift.
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_000.jpg	It tells us that a single physical object, buildable once and for all (apart from maintenance and a
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_001.jpg	supply of additional memory when needed), can perform with unlimited accuracy the task of
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_002.jpg	describing or mimicking any other part of the multiverse. The set of all behaviours and responses of
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_003.jpg	that one object exactly mirrors the set of all behaviours and responses of all other physically possible
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_004.jpg	objects and processes. This is just the sort of self-similarity that is necessary if, according to the hope I
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_005.jpg	expressed in Chapter 1, the fabric of reality is to be truly unified and comprehensible. If the laws of
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_006.jpg	physics as they apply to any physical object or process are to be comprehensible, they must be
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_007.jpg	capable of being embodied in another physical object — the knower. It is also necessary that
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_008.jpg	processes capable of creating such knowledge be physically possible.
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_009.jpg	Such processes are called science. Science depends on experimental testing, which means physically
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_010.jpg	rendering a law’s predictions and comparing it with (a rendering of) reality. It also depends on
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_011.jpg	explanation, and that requires the abstractlaws themselves, not merely their predictive content, to be
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_012.jpg	capable of being rendered in virtual reality.
test/images/synth_doc_00110_line_013.jpg	This is a tall order, but reality does meet it. That is to say, the laws of physics meet it. The laws of
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_000.jpg	A stream of findings from the deep path markedly boosts science’s models of the upper limits of our
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_001.jpg	positive potential. The further reaches of the deep path cultivate enduring qualities like selflessness,
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_002.jpg	equanimity, a loving presence, and impartial compassion—highly positive altered traits.
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_003.jpg	When we began, this seemed big news for modern psychology—if it would listen. Admittedly, at first
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_004.jpg	the concept of altered traits had scant backing save for the gut feelings we had from meeting highly
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_005.jpg	seasoned practitioners in Asia, the claims of ancient meditation texts, and our own fledgling tries at
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_006.jpg	this inner art.
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_007.jpg	Now, after decades of silence and disregard, the last few years have seen ample findings that bear out
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_008.jpg	our early hunch. Only of late have the scientific data reached critical mass, confirming what our
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_009.jpg	intuition and the texts told us: these deep changes are external signs of strikingly different brain
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_010.jpg	function.Much of that data comes from Richie’s lab, the only scientific center that has gathered
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_011.jpg	findings on dozens of contemplative masters, mainly Tibetan yogis— the largest pool of deep
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_012.jpg	practitioners studied anywhere. These unlikely research partners have been crucial in building a
test/images/synth_doc_00109_line_013.jpg	scientific case for the existence of a way of being that has eluded modern thought, though it was
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_000.jpg	The sounder studies, we found, focus on lessening our psychological distress rather than on curing
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_001.jpg	medical syndromes or looking for underlying biological mechanisms. So, when it comes to a better
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_002.jpg	quality of life for those with chronic diseases, yes to meditation.
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_003.jpg	Such palliative care gets ignored too often in medicine, but it matters enormously to patients. Still,
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_004.jpg	might meditation offer biological relief? Consider the Dalai Lama, now in his eighties, who goes to bed
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_005.jpg	at 7:00 p.m. and gets a full night’s sleep before he awakens around 3:30 for a four-hour stint of
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_006.jpg	spiritual practice, including meditation.
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_007.jpg	Add another hour of practice before he goes to bed and that gives him five hours a day of
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_008.jpg	contemplative time. But painful arthritis in his knees makes going up or down stairs an ordeal— not
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_009.jpg	uncommon for someone in the ninth decade of life. When he was asked if meditation helps medical
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_010.jpg	conditions, he retorted, “If meditation was good for all health problems, I’d be free of pain in my
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_011.jpg	knees.” When it comes to whether meditation does more than offer palliative help, we’re not sure
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_012.jpg	yet—and if so, in what medical conditions? A few years after Richie got that stinging rejection of his
test/images/synth_doc_00108_line_013.jpg	plan to measure genetic changes from one day of meditation, he was invited to give the prestigious
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_000.jpg	The enzyme telomerase, which slows cellular aging, increases after three months of intensive practice
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_001.jpg	of mindfulness and loving-kindness. Finally, long-term meditation may lead to beneficial structural
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_002.jpg	changes in the brain, though current evidence is inconclusive about whether such effects emerge with
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_003.jpg	relatively short-term practice like MBSR, or only become apparent with longer-termpractice.
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_004.jpg	All in all, the hints of neural rewiring that undergird altered traits seem scientifically credible, though
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_005.jpg	we await further studies for specifics.10 Meditation as Psychotherapy D r. Aaron Beck, the founder of
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_006.jpg	cognitive therapy, had a question: “What is mindfulness?” It was the mid-1980s, and Dr. Beck was
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_007.jpg	asking Tara Bennett-Goleman, Dan’s wife. She had come to his home in Ardmore, Pennsylvania, at Dr.
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_008.jpg	Beck’s request, because Judge Judith Beck, his wife, was about to undergo some elective surgery. Dr.
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_009.jpg	Beck had a hunch meditation might help better prepare her mentally and, perhaps, even physically.
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_010.jpg	Tara instructed the couple on the spot. Following her guidance the Becks sat quietly and observed the
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_011.jpg	sensations of their breathing in and out, then tried a walking meditation in their living room.
test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_012.jpg	That was a hint of what has since become a strong movement in “mindfulness-based cognitive
