test/images/synth_doc_00111_line_013.jpg	therapy,” or MBCT. Tara’s book Emotional Alchemy: How the Mind Can Heal the Heart was the first to
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_000.jpg	As Keltner has written, the overwhelming force and the mystery of awe are such that the experience
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_001.jpg	can’t readily be interpreted according to our accustomed frames of thought. By rocking those
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_002.jpg	conceptual frameworks, awe has the power to change our minds.
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_003.jpg	Three: Depression Something unexpected happened when, early in 2017, Roland Griffiths and Stephen
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_004.jpg	Ross brought the results of their clinical trials to the FDA, hoping to win approval for a larger, phase 3
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_005.jpg	trial of psilocybin for cancer patients. Impressed by their data—and seemingly undeterred by the
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_006.jpg	unique challenges posed by psychedelic research, such as the problem of blinding, the combining of
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_007.jpg	therapy and medicine, and the fact that the drug in question is still illegal—the FDA staff surprised the
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_008.jpg	researchers by asking them to expand their focus and ambition: to test whether psilocybin could be
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_009.jpg	used to treat the much larger and more pressing problem of depression in the general population. As
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_010.jpg	the regulators saw it, the data contained a strong enough “signal” that psilocybin could relieve
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_011.jpg	depression; it would be a shame not to test the proposition, given the enormity of the need and the
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_012.jpg	limitations of the therapies now available. Ross and Griffiths had focused on cancer patients because
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_013.jpg	they thought it would be easier to win approval to study a controlled substance in people who were
test/images/synth_doc_00112_line_014.jpg	already seriously ill or dying. Now the government was telling them to raise their sights. “It was
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_000.jpg	And the answer is, usually, that we cannot. The difference between the real trajectory and the
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_001.jpg	predicted trajectory, calculated from slightly inaccurate data, tends to grow exponentially and
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_002.jpg	irregularly (‘chaotically’) with time, so that after a while the original, slightly imperfectly known state is
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_003.jpg	no guide at all to what the system is doing.
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_004.jpg	The implication for computer prediction is that planetary motions, the epitome of classical
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_005.jpg	predictability, are untypical classical systems. In order to predict what a typical classical system will
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_006.jpg	do after only a moderate period, one would have to determine its initial state to an impossibly high
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_007.jpg	precision. Thus it is said that in principle, the flap of a butterfly’s wing in one hemisphere of the planet
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_008.jpg	could cause a hurricane in the other hemisphere.
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_009.jpg	The infeasibility of weather forecasting and the like is then attributed to the impossibility of
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_010.jpg	accounting for every butterfly on the planet.However, real hurricanes and real butterflies obey
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_011.jpg	quantum theory, not classical mechanics. The instability that would rapidly amplify slight mis-
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_012.jpg	specifications of an initial classical state is simply not a feature of quantum- mechanical systems. In
test/images/synth_doc_00113_line_013.jpg	quantum mechanics, small deviations from a specified initial state tend to cause only small deviations
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_000.jpg	Even poor Mr. Katz’s twelve hours as a madman included passages of indescribable pleasure and
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_001.jpg	insight that could not be overlooked. As it happened, the psychotomimetic paradigm was replaced
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_002.jpg	not by one but by two distinct new theoretical models: the psycholytic and, later, the psychedelic
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_003.jpg	model. Each was based on a different conception of how the compounds worked on the mind and
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_004.jpg	therefore how they might best be deployed in the treatment of mental illness.
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_005.jpg	The two models weren’t at odds with each other, exactly, and some researchers explored both
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_006.jpg	atvarious times, but they did represent profoundly different approaches to understanding the psyche,
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_007.jpg	as well as to psychotherapy and, ultimately, science itself. The so-called psycholytic paradigm was
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_008.jpg	developed first and proved especially popular in Europe and with the Los Angeles group identified
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_009.jpg	with Sidney Cohen, Betty Eisner, and Oscar Janiger.
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_010.jpg	Coined by an English psychiatrist named Ronald Sandison, “psycholytic” means “mind loosening,”
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_011.jpg	which is what LSD and psilocybin seem to do—at least at low doses. Therapists who administered
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_012.jpg	doses of LSD as low as 25 micrograms (and seldom higher than 150 micrograms) reported that their
test/images/synth_doc_00117_line_013.jpg	patients’ ego defenses relaxed, allowing them to bring up and discuss difficult or repressed material
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_000.jpg	What would it feel like to be in a Cantgotu environment? Although the laws of physics do not permit us
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_001.jpg	to be in one, it is still logically possible and so it is legitimate to ask what it would feel like. Certainly, it
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_002.jpg	could give us no new sensations, because a universal image generator is possible and is assumed to
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_003.jpg	be part of our high-technology virtual-reality generator. So a Cantgotu environment would seem
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_004.jpg	mysterious to us only after we had experienced it and reflected on the results. It would go something
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_005.jpg	like this.
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_006.jpg	Suppose you are a virtual-reality buff in the distant, ultra-high-techhnology future. You have become
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_007.jpg	jaded, for it seems to you that you have already tried everything interesting.
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_008.jpg	But then one day a genie appears and claims to be able to transport you to a Cantgotu environment.
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_009.jpg	You are sceptical, but agree to put its claim to the test.
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_010.jpg	You are whisked away to the environment. After a few expedients you seem to recognize it — it
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_011.jpg	responds just like one of your favourite environments, which on your home virtual-reality system has
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_012.jpg	program number X. However, you keep experimenting, and eventually, during the Xth subjective
test/images/synth_doc_00119_line_013.jpg	minute of the experience, the environment responds in a way that is markedly different from anything
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_000.jpg	Of course, meditation has its limits. Dan’s original interest in meditation during his college days was
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_001.jpg	because he felt anxious. Meditation seemed to calm those feelings somewhat, but they still came and
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_002.jpg	went. Many people go to psychotherapists for just such problems.
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_003.jpg	Dan did not. But years later he was diagnosed with that adrenal disorder, the cause of his long-
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_004.jpg	standing high blood pressure. One of those adrenal symptoms: elevated levels of cortisol, the stress
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_005.jpg	hormone that triggers feelings of anxiety. Along with his years of meditation, a drug that adjusts that
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_006.jpg	adrenal problem seemed also to handle the cortisol—and the anxiety.
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_007.jpg	IN A NUTSHELL Although meditation was not originally intended to treat psychological problems, in
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_008.jpg	modern times it has shown promise in the treatment of some, particularly depression and anxiety
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_009.jpg	disorders. In a meta-analysis of forty-seven studies on the application of meditation methods to treat
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_010.jpg	patients with mental health problems, the findings show that meditation can lead to decreases in
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_011.jpg	depression (particularly severe depression), anxiety, and pain—about as much as medications but
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_012.jpg	with no side effects.
test/images/synth_doc_00114_line_013.jpg	Meditation also can, to a lesser degree, reduce the toll of psychological stress. Loving-kindness
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_000.jpg	Altering Traits 14. A Healthy Mind FURTHER RESOURCES ACKNOWLEDGMENTS NOTES INDEX ABOUT
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_001.jpg	THE AUTHORS1 The Deep Path and the Wide O ne bright fall morning, Steve Z, a lieutenant colonel
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_002.jpg	working in the Pentagon, heard a “crazy, loud noise,” and instantly was covered in debris as the
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_003.jpg	ceiling caved in, knocking him to the floor, unconscious.
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_004.jpg	It was September 11, 2001, and a passenger jet had smashed into the huge building, very near to
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_005.jpg	Steve’s office. The debris that buried Steve saved his life as the plane’s fuselage exploded, a fireball of
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_006.jpg	flames scouring the open office. Despite a concussion, Steve returned to work four days later, laboring
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_007.jpg	through feverish nights, 6:00 p.m. to 6:00 a.m., because those were daytime hours in Afghanistan.
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_008.jpg	Soon after, he volunteered for a year in Iraq. “I mainly went to Iraq because I couldn’t walk around the
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_009.jpg	Mall without being hypervigilant, wary of how people looked at me, totally on guard,” Steve recalls. “I
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_010.jpg	couldn’t get on an elevator, I felt trapped in my car in traffic.” His symptoms were classic
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_011.jpg	post-traumatic stress disorder. Then came the day he realized he couldn’t handle this on his own.
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_012.jpg	Steve ended up with a psychotherapist he still sees. She led him, very gently, to try mindfulness.
test/images/synth_doc_00116_line_013.jpg	Mindfulness, he recalls, “gave me something I could do to help feel more calm, less stressed, not be so
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_000.jpg	Mary was squatting next to me, and when I finally looked up into her face, I saw she had turned into
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_001.jpg	María Sabina, the Mexican curandera who had given psilocybin to R. Gordon Wasson in that dirt
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_002.jpg	basement in Huautla de Jiménez sixty years ago. Her hair was black, her face, stretched taut over its
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_003.jpg	high cheekbones, was anciently weathered, and she was wearing a simple white peasant dress. I took
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_004.jpg	the dried mushroom from the woman’s wrinkled brown hand and looked away as I chewed. I didn’t
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_005.jpg	think I should tell Mary what had happened to her.
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_006.jpg	(Later, when I did, she was flattered: María Sabina was her hero.) • • • BUT THERE WAS SOMETHING I
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_007.jpg	needed to do before putting my eyeshades back on and going back under, a little experiment I had
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_008.jpg	told Mary I wanted to perform on myself during my trip. I wasn’t sure if in mycondition I could pull it
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_009.jpg	off, but I’d found that even in the middle of the journey it was possible to summon oneself to a
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_010.jpg	semblance of normality for a few moments at a time. Loaded on my laptop was a brief video of a
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_011.jpg	rotating face mask, used in a psychological test called the binocular depth inversion illusion. As the
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_012.jpg	mask rotates in space, its convex side turning to reveal its concave back, something remarkable
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_013.jpg	happens: the hollow mask appears to pop out to become convex again. This is a trick performed by
test/images/synth_doc_00118_line_014.jpg	the mind, which assumes all faces to be convex, and so automatically corrects for the seeming
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_000.jpg	Look at where we are: at the edge of the continent, the edge of an ecosystem, the edge of civilization,
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_001.jpg	and of course these mushrooms bring us to the edge of consciousness.” At this point, Stamets, who
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_002.jpg	when it comes to mushrooms is one serious dude, made the first joke I had ever heard him make:
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_003.jpg	“You know one of the best indicator species for Psilocybe azurescens are Winnebagos.” We’re
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_004.jpg	obviously not the first people to hunt for azzies in this park, and anyone who picks a mushroom trails
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_005.jpg	an invisible cloud of its spore behind him; this, he believes, is the origin of the idea of fairy dust. At the
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_006.jpg	end of many of those trails is apt to be a campsite, a car, or a Winnebago.
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_007.jpg	We found seven azzies that afternoon, though by we I mean Stamets; I only found one, and even then I
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_008.jpg	wasn’t at all certain it was a Psilocybe until Stamets gave me a smile and a thumbs-up. I could swear it
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_009.jpg	looked exactly like half a dozen other species I was finding. Stamets patiently tutored me in
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_010.jpg	mushroom morphology, and by the following day my luck had improved, and I found four little
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_011.jpg	caramel beauties on my own.
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_012.jpg	Not much of a haul, but then Stamets had said that even just one of these mushrooms could
test/images/synth_doc_00120_line_013.jpg	underwrite a major psychic expedition. That evening, we carefully laid out our seven mushrooms on a
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_000.jpg	The same lessened connectivity compared to nonmeditators was found by brain researchers in Israel
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_001.jpg	studying long-term mindfulness meditators, who had on average around 9,000 hours of practice
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_002.jpg	under their belts.9 Further indirect evidence for this change in long-term meditators comes from a
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_003.jpg	study at Emory University of seasoned Zen meditators (three years–plus practice, but lifetime hours
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_004.jpg	unknown) who, compared to controls, seemed to show less activity in parts of the default area while
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_005.jpg	focusing on their breath during brain scans. The bigger this effect, the better they did on a test of
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_006.jpg	sustained attention outside the scanner, suggesting a lasting drop in mind- wandering.10 Finally, a
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_007.jpg	small but suggestive study of Zen meditators at the University of Montreal found lessened default area
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_008.jpg	connectivity while just resting among Zen meditators (with an average 1,700 hours of practice)
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_009.jpg	compared to a group of volunteers trained in zazen for just one week.11 There’s a theory that what
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_010.jpg	captures our attention signifies an attachment, and the more attached we are, the more often we’ll be
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_011.jpg	so captivated.
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_012.jpg	In an experiment testing this premise, a group of volunteers and one of seasoned meditators (4,200
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_013.jpg	hours) were told they would get money whenever they recognized certain geometric shapes within an
test/images/synth_doc_00115_line_014.jpg	array.12 That was, in a sense, thecreation of a mini-attachment. Then, in a later phase, when they
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_000.jpg	From evidence like this, it seems likely that the states we practice in meditation gradually spill over into daily life to mold our traits—at
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_001.jpg	least when it comes to handling stress. A DEVILISH ORDEAL Imagine you are describing your qualifications for a job while two
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_002.jpg	interviewers glare at you, unsmiling. Their faces reveal no empathy, not even an encouraging nod. That’s the situation in the Trier Social
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_003.jpg	Stress Test (TSST), one of the most reliable ways known to science to trigger the brain’s stress circuits and its cascade of stress hormones.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_004.jpg	Now imagine, after that dispiriting job interview, doing some pressured mental arithmetic: you have to subtract 13s in rapid-fire succession
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_005.jpg	from a number like 1,232.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_006.jpg	That’s the second part of the Trier test, and those same impassive interviewers push you to do the math faster and faster—and whenever
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_007.jpg	you make a mistake, they tell you to start all over at 1,232. That devilish test delivers a huge dose of social stress, the awful feelings we get
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_008.jpg	when other people evaluate, reject, or exclude us. Alan Wallace and Paul Ekman created a renewal program for schoolteachers that
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_009.jpg	combined psychological training with meditation.19 Whereas Dan had used the shop accident film to bring stress into the lab, here the
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_010.jpg	stressor was the Trier test’s simulated job interview followed by that formidable math challenge. The more hours those teachers had
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_011.jpg	practiced meditation, the quicker their blood pressure recovered from a high point during the TSST.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_012.jpg	This was true five months after the program ended, suggesting at least a mild trait effect (five years afterward would be still stronger
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_013.jpg	evidence of a trait). Richie’s lab used the Trier with seasoned (lifetime average = 9,000 hours) vipassana meditators who did an eight-hour
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_014.jpg	day of meditation and the next day underwent the test.20 The meditators and their age-and gender-matched comparison group all went
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_015.jpg	through the TSST (as well as a test for inflammation —more on those results in chapter nine, “Mind, Body, and Genome”). Result: the
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_016.jpg	meditators had a smaller rise in cortisol during the stress.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_017.jpg	Just as important, the meditators perceived that dreaded Trier test as less stressful thandid the nonmeditators. This cooled-out, more
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_018.jpg	balanced way of viewing that stressor among the seasoned meditators was not tapped while they were practicing but while they were at
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_019.jpg	rest—our “before.” Their ease during both the stressful interview and the formidable mental math challenge seems a genuine trait effect.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_020.jpg	Further evidence for this comes from research with these same advanced meditators.21 The meditators’ brains were scanned while they
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_021.jpg	saw disturbing images of people suffering, like burn victims.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_022.jpg	The seasoned practitioners’ brains revealed a lowered level of reactivity in the amygdala; they were more immune to emotional hijacking.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_023.jpg	The reason: their brains had stronger operative connectivity between the prefrontal cortex, which manages reactivity, and the amygdala,
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_024.jpg	which triggers such reactions. As neuroscientists know, the stronger this particular link in the brain, the less a person will be hijacked by
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_025.jpg	emotional downs and ups of all sorts. This connectivity modulates a person’s level of emotional reactivity: the stronger the link, the less
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_026.jpg	reactive. Indeed, that relationship is so strong that a person’s reactivity level can be predicted by the connectivity.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_027.jpg	So, when these high-lifetime-hour meditators saw an image of a gruesome-looking burn victim, they had little amygdala reactivity.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_028.jpg	Age-matched volunteers did not show either the heightened connectivity or the equanimity on viewing the disturbing images. But when
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_029.jpg	Richie’s group repeated this study with people taking the MBSR training (a total of just under thirty hours) plus a bit of daily at-home
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_030.jpg	practice, they failed to find any strengthening of connection between the prefrontal region and the amygdala during the challenge of
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_031.jpg	upsetting images.
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_032.jpg	Nor was there any when the MBSR group simply rested. While MBSR training did reduce the reactivity of the amygdala, the long- term
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_033.jpg	meditator group showed both this reduced reactivity in the amygdala plus strengthening of the connection between the prefrontal cortex
test/images/synth_doc_00123_line_034.jpg	and amygdala.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_000.jpg	But I do not want to overstate the similarities between scientific discovery and biological evolution, for there are important differences too.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_001.jpg	One difference is that in biology variations (mutations) are random, blind and purposeless, while in human problem-solving the creation of
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_002.jpg	new conjectures is itself a complex, knowledge-laden process driven by the intentions of the people concerned. Perhaps an even more
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_003.jpg	important difference is that there is no biological equivalent of argument.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_004.jpg	All conjectures have to be tested experimentally, which is one reason why biological evolution is slower and less efficient byan
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_005.jpg	astronomically large factor. Nevertheless, the link between the two sorts of process is far more than mere analogy: they are two of my four
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_006.jpg	intimately related ‘main strands’ of explanation of the fabric of reality. Both in science and in biological evolution, evolutionary success
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_007.jpg	depends on the creation and survival of objective knowledge, which in biology is called adaptation. That is, the ability of a theory or gene
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_008.jpg	to survive in a niche is not a haphazard function of its structure but depends on whether enough true and useful information about the
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_009.jpg	niche is implicitly or explicitly encoded there. I shall say more about this in Chapter 8.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_010.jpg	We can now begin to see what justifies the inferences that we draw from observations. We never draw inferences from observations alone,
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_011.jpg	but observations can become significant in the course of an argument when they reveal deficiencies in some of the contending explanations.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_012.jpg	We choose a scientific theory because arguments, only a few of which depend on observations, have satisfied us (for the moment) that the
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_013.jpg	explanations offered by all known rival theories are less true, less broad or less deep. Take a moment to compare Figures 3.1 and 3.3. Look
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_014.jpg	how different these two conceptions of the scientific process are.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_015.jpg	Inductivism is observation- and prediction-based, whereas in reality science is problem- and explanation- based. Inductivism supposes that
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_016.jpg	theories are somehow extracted or distilled from observations, or are justified by them, whereas in fact theories begin as unjustified
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_017.jpg	conjectures in someone’s mind, which typically precede the observations that rule out rival theories.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_018.jpg	Inductivism seeks to justify predictions as likely to hold in the future. Problem-solving justifies an explanation as being better than other
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_019.jpg	explanations available in the present. Inductivism is a dangerous and recurring source of many sorts of error, because it is superficially so
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_020.jpg	plausible.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_021.jpg	But it is not true. When we succeed in solving a problem, scientific or otherwise, we end up with a set of theories which, though they are
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_022.jpg	not problem-free, we find preferable to the theories we started with.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_023.jpg	What new attributes the new theories will have therefore depends on what we saw as the deficiencies in our original theories — that is, on
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_024.jpg	what the problem was. Science is characterized by its problems as well as by its method. Astrologers who solve the problem of how to cast
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_025.jpg	more intriguing horoscopes without risking being proved wrong are unlikely to have created much that deserves to be called scientific
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_026.jpg	knowledge, even if they have used genuine scientific methods (such as market research) and are themselves quite satisfied with the
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_027.jpg	solution.
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_028.jpg	The problem in genuine science is always to understand some aspect of the fabric of reality, by finding explanations that are as broad and
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_029.jpg	deep, and as true and specific, as possible. When we think that we have solved a problem, we naturally adopt our new set of theories in
test/images/synth_doc_00124_line_030.jpg	preference to the old set.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_000.jpg	So we offer a clear-eyed view based on hard science, sifting out results that are not nearly as compelling as the claims made for them. Even
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_001.jpg	well-meaning proponents have little guidance in distinguishing between what’s sound and what’s questionable—or just sheer nonsense.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_002.jpg	Given the rising tide of enthusiasm, our more sober-minded take comes not a moment too soon. A note to readers. The first three chapters
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_003.jpg	cover our initial forays into meditation, and the scientific hunch that motivated our quest.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_004.jpg	Chapters four through twelve narrate the scientific journey, with each chapter devoted to a particular topic like attention or compassion;
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_005.jpg	each of these has an “In a Nutshell” summary at the end for those who are more interested in what we found than how we got there. In
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_006.jpg	chapters eleven and twelve we arrive at our long-sought destination, sharing the remarkable findings on the most advanced meditators
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_007.jpg	ever studied. In chapter thirteen, “Altering Traits,” we lay out the benefits of meditation at three levels: beginner, long-term, and
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_008.jpg	“Olympic.” In our final chapter we speculate on what the future might bring, and how these findings might be of greater benefit not just to
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_009.jpg	each of us individually but to society.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_010.jpg	THE ACCELERATION As early as the 1830s, Thoreau and Emerson, along with their fellow American Transcendentalists, flirted with
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_011.jpg	these Eastern inner arts. They were spurred bythe first English-language translations of ancient spiritual texts from Asia—but had no
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_012.jpg	instruction in the practices that supported those texts.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_013.jpg	Almost a century later, Sigmund Freud advised psychoanalysts to adopt an “even-hovering attention” while listening to their clients—but
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_014.jpg	again, offered no method. The West’s more serious engagement took hold mere decades ago, as teachers from the East arrived, and as a
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_015.jpg	generation of Westerners traveled to study meditation in Asia, some returning as teachers. These forays paved the way for the current
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_016.jpg	acceleration of the wide path, along with fresh possibilities for those few who choose to pursue the deep way.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_017.jpg	Publication Count for Scientific Studies on Meditation or Mindfulness, 1970–2016 In the 1970s, when we began publishing our research on
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_018.jpg	meditation, there were just a handful of scientific articles on the topic. At last count there numbered 6,838 such articles, with a notable
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_019.jpg	acceleration of late.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_020.jpg	For 2014 the annual number was 925, in 2015 the total was 1,098, and in 2016 there were 1,113 such publications in the English language
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_021.jpg	scientific literature.5 PRIMING THE FIELD It was April 2001, on the top floor of the Fluno Center on the campus of the University of
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_022.jpg	Wisconsin–Madison, and we were convening with the Dalai Lama for an afternoon of scientific dialogue on meditation research findings.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_023.jpg	Missing from the room was Francisco Varela, a Chilean-born neuroscientist and head offrom the room was Francisco Varela, a
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_024.jpg	Chilean-born neuroscientist and head of a cognitive neuroscience laboratory at the French National Center for Scientific Research in Paris.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_025.jpg	His remarkable career included cofounding the Mind and Life Institute, which had organized this very gathering. As a serious meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_026.jpg	practitioner, Francisco could see the promise for a full collaboration between seasoned meditators and the scientists studying them. That
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_027.jpg	model became standard practice in Richie’s lab, as well as others. Francisco had been scheduled to participate, but he was fighting liver
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_028.jpg	cancer and a severe downturn meant he could not travel.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_029.jpg	He was in his bed at home in Paris, close to dying. This was in the days before Skype and videoconferencing, but Richie’s group managed a
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_030.jpg	two-way video hookup between our meeting room and Francisco’s bedroom in his Paris apartment. The Dalai Lama addressed him very
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_031.jpg	directly, looking closely into the camera. They both knew that this would be the very last time they would see each other in this lifetime.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_032.jpg	The Dalai Lama thanked Francisco for all he had done for science and for the greater good, told him to be strong, and said that they would
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_033.jpg	remain connected forever. Richie and many others in the room had tears streaming down, appreciating the momentous import of the
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_034.jpg	moment.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_035.jpg	Just days after the meeting, Francisco passed away. Three years later, in 2004, an event occurred that made real a dream Francisco had often
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_036.jpg	talked about. At the Garrison Institute, an hour up the Hudson River from New York City, one hundred scientists, graduate students, and
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_037.jpg	postdocs had gathered for the first in what has become a yearly series of events, the Summer Research Institute (SRI), a gathering devoted
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_038.jpg	to furthering the rigorous study of meditation. The meetings are organized by the Mind and Life Institute, itself formed in 1987 by the Dalai
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_039.jpg	Lama, Francisco, and Adam Engle, a lawyer turned businessman. We were founding board members.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_040.jpg	The mission of Mind and Life is “to alleviate suffering and promote flourishing by integrating science with contemplative practice.” Mind
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_041.jpg	and Life’s summer institute, we felt, could offer a more welcoming reality for those who, like us in our grad school days, wanted to do
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_042.jpg	research on meditation. While we had been isolated pioneers, we wanted to knit together a community of like-minded scholars and
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_043.jpg	scientists who shared this quest.
test/images/synth_doc_00126_line_044.jpg	They could be supportive of each other’s work at a distance, even if they were alone in their interests at their own institution.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_000.jpg	The word never crossed my lips again. By the end of the call, Stamets had invited me up to his place in Washington State, on the Little
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_001.jpg	Skookum Inlet at the base of the Olympic Peninsula. I asked him, gingerly, if I could come at a time when the Psilocybes were fruiting.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_002.jpg	“Most of them have already come and gone,” he said. “But if you come right after Thanksgiving, and the weather’s right, I can take you to
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_003.jpg	the only place in the world where Psilocybe azurescens has been consistently found, at the mouth of the Columbia River.” He mentioned
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_004.jpg	the name of the park where he had found them in the past and told me to book a yurt there, adding, “Probably best not to use my name.” •
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_005.jpg	• • IN THE WEEKS BEFORE my trip to Washington State, I pored over Stamets’s field guide, hoping to prepare myself for the hunt. It
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_006.jpg	seems there are more than two hundred species of Psilocybe, distributed all over the world; it’s not clear whether that’s always been the
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_007.jpg	case, or if the mushrooms have followed in the footsteps of the animals who have taken such a keen interest in them. (Humans have been
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_008.jpg	using psilocybin mushrooms sacramentally for at least seven thousand years, according to Stamets.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_009.jpg	But animals sometimes ingest them too, for reasons that remain obscure. Psilocybes are saprophytes, living off dead plant matter and dung.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_010.jpg	They are denizens of disturbed land, popping up most often in the habitats created by ecological catastrophe, such as landslides, floods,
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_011.jpg	storms, and volcanoes. They also prosper in the ecological catastrophes caused by our species: clear-cut forests, road cuts, the wakes of
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_012.jpg	bulldozers, and agriculture.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_013.jpg	(Several species live in and fruit from the manure of ruminants. Curiously, or perhaps not so curiously, the most potent species occur less
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_014.jpg	often in the wild than in cities and towns; their predilection for habitats disturbed by us has allowed them to travel widely, “following
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_015.jpg	streams of debris,” including our own. In recent years,the practice of mulching with wood chips has vastly expanded the range of a handful
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_016.jpg	of potent Psilocybes once confined to the Pacific Northwest. They now thrive in all those places we humans now “landscape”: suburban
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_017.jpg	gardens, nurseries, city parks, churchyards, highway rest stops, prisons, college campuses, even, as Stamets likes to point out, on the
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_018.jpg	grounds of courthouses and police stations. “Psilocybe mushrooms and civilization continue to co-evolve,” Stamets writes. So you would
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_019.jpg	think these mushrooms would be fairly easy to find.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_020.jpg	In fact after I published an article about psilocybin research, I was informed by a student that after the December rains Psilocybes can be
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_021.jpg	found on the Berkeley campus, where I teach. “Look in the wood chips,” he advised. Yet as soon as I began studying the photographs in
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_022.jpg	Stamets’s field guide, I began to despair of ever identifying any mushroom as a member of the genus, much less learning how to
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_023.jpg	distinguish one species of Psilocybe from another.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_024.jpg	To judge from the pictures, the genus is just a big bunch of little brown mushrooms, most of them utterly nondescript. By comparison, the
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_025.jpg	edible species with which I was familiar were as distinct as tulips are from roses, poodles from Great Danes. Yes, all the Psilocybes have
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_026.jpg	gills, but that isn’t much help, because thousands of other mushrooms have gills, too.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_027.jpg	After that, you’re trying to sort out a bewildering array of characteristics, not all of which are shared by the class. Some Psilocybes have a
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_028.jpg	little nipple-like knob or protrusion on top—it’s called an umbo, I learned; others don’t. Some were “viscid”—slippery or slimy when wet,
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_029.jpg	giving them a shiny appearance.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_030.jpg	Others were dull and matte gray; some, like azurescens, were a milky caramel color. Many but not all Psilocybes sport a “pellicle”—a
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_031.jpg	condom-like layer of gelatinous material covering the cap that can be peeled off. My fungal vocabulary might be expanding, but my
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_032.jpg	confidence was rapidly collapsing, much like the mushroom that, in the course of a single day, decomposes into an inky puddle. By the
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_033.jpg	time I got to chapter four, “The Dangers of Mistaken Identification,” I was ready to throw in the towel. “Mistakes in mushroom
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_034.jpg	identification can be lethal,” Stamets begins, before displaying a photograph in which a Psilocybe stuntzii is seen growing cheek by jowl
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_035.jpg	with a trio of indistinguishable Galerina autumnalis, an unremarkable little mushroom that, when eaten, “can result in an agonizing
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_036.jpg	death.”But while Stamets urges extreme circumspection in amateurs hoping to identify Psilocybes, he also equips the mushroom hunter
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_037.jpg	who hasn’t been completely discouraged with something he calls “The Stametsian Rule”: a three-pronged test that, he (sort of) assures us,
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_038.jpg	can head off death and disaster. “How do I know if a mushroom is a psilocybin producing species or not?” “If a gilled mushroom has
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_039.jpg	purplish brown to black spores, and the flesh bruises bluish, the mushroom in question is very likely a psilocybin- producing species.” This
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_040.jpg	is definitely a big help, though I wouldn’t mind something more categorical than “very likely.” He then offers a sobering caveat. “I know of
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_041.jpg	no exceptions to this rule,” he adds, “but that does not mean there are none!” After committing to memory the Stametsian Rule, I began
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_042.jpg	picking promising-looking gilled LBMs—in my neighbors’ yards, on my walk to work, in the parking lot of the bank—and then roughing
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_043.jpg	them up a bit to see if they would turn black and blue. The blue pigment is in fact evidence of oxidized psilocin, one of the two main
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_044.jpg	psychoactive compounds in a Psilocybe.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_045.jpg	(The other is psilocybin, which breaks down into psilocin in the body. To determine if the mushroom in question had purplish-brown or
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_046.jpg	black spores, I began making spore prints. This involves cutting the cap off a mushroom and placing it, gill side down, on a piece of white
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_047.jpg	paper.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_048.jpg	(Or black paper if you have reason to believe the mushroom has white spores. Within hours, the mushroom cap releases its microscopic
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_049.jpg	spores, which will form a pretty, shadowy pattern on the paper (reminiscent of a lipstick kiss) that you can then try to decide is purplish
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_050.jpg	brown or black—or rust colored, in which case you might have a deadly Galerina on your hands. Certain things are perhaps best learned in
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_051.jpg	person, rather than from a book. I decided I should probably wait before making any irreversible decisions until I had spent some time in
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_052.jpg	the company of my mycological Virgil. • • •AT THE TIME OF MY VISIT, Paul Stamets lived with his partner, Dusty Yao, and their two
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_053.jpg	big dogs, Plato and Sophie, in a sprawling new house on the Little Skookum Inlet that is constructed inside and out of a small forest’s
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_054.jpg	worth of the most gorgeous clear Douglas fir and cedar.
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_055.jpg	Like many species of fungi, Stamets has a passionate attachment to trees and wood. I arrived on a Friday; our reservation at the campsite
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_056.jpg	wasn’t until Sunday night, so we had the better part of the weekend to talk Psilocybes, eat (other kinds of) mushrooms, tour the Fungi
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_057.jpg	Perfecti facilities, and ramble the surrounding woods and shoreline with the dogs before driving south to the Oregon border Sunday
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_058.jpg	morning to hunt azzies. This was the house that mushrooms built, Stamets explained, launching into its story before I had a chance to
test/images/synth_doc_00121_line_059.jpg	unpack my bag.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_000.jpg	Out there in the woods in the middle of the Olympic Peninsula? Andrei mentioned that an aspiring guide he was training had “once asked
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_001.jpg	me, ‘What do you do if someone dies?’” I don’t know what I expected him to say, but Andrei’s reply, delivered with one of his most
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_002.jpg	matter-of-fact shrugs, was not it. “You bury him with all the other dead people.” I told Andrei I would be in touch.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_003.jpg	The psychedelic underground was populated with a great many such vivid characters, I soon discovered, but not necessarily the kinds of
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_004.jpg	characters to whom I felt I could entrust my mind—or for that matter any part of me. Immediately after my session with Andrei, I had a
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_005.jpg	meetingwith a second prospective guide, a brilliant psychologist in his eighties who had been a student of Timothy Leary’s at Harvard. His
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_006.jpg	knowledge of psychedelics was deep; his credentials impressive; he had been highly recommended by people I respected. Yet when over
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_007.jpg	lunch at a Tibetan restaurant near his office he removed his bolo tie and suspended it over the menu, I began to lose confidence that this
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_008.jpg	was my man.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_009.jpg	He explained that he relied on the energies released by the pendulum swing of the silver clasp to choose the entrée most likely to agree
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_010.jpg	with his temperamental digestion. I forget what his tie ordered for lunch, but even before he began dilating on the evidence that 9/11 was
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_011.jpg	an inside job, I knew my search for a guide was not over quite yet. • • • ONE NOTABLE DIFFERENCE about doing psychedelics at sixty,
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_012.jpg	as opposed to when you’re eighteen or twenty, is that at sixty you’re more likely to have a cardiologist you might want to consult in
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_013.jpg	advance of your trip.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_014.jpg	That was me. A year before I had decided to embark on this adventure, my heart, the reliable operations of which I had taken completely
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_015.jpg	for granted to that point, had suddenly made its presence felt and, for the first time in my life, demanded my attention.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_016.jpg	While sitting at my computer one afternoon, I was suddenly made aware of a pronounced and crazily syncopated new rhythm in my chest.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_017.jpg	“Atrial fibrillation” was the name the doctor gave the abnormal squiggles that appeared on my EKG. The danger of AFib is not a heart
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_018.jpg	attack, he said to my (short-lived) relief, but a heightened risk of stroke. “My cardiologist”—the unfortunate phrase had suddenly joined
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_019.jpg	my vocabulary, probably for the duration—put me on a couple of meds to calm the heart rhythms and lower the blood pressure, plus a
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_020.jpg	daily baby aspirin to thin my blood. And then he told me not to worry about it.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_021.jpg	I followed all of his advice except the last bit. Now I couldn’t help but think about my heart constantly. All of its operations that had
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_022.jpg	previously taken place completely outside my conscious awareness suddenly became salient: something I could hear and feel whenever I
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_023.jpg	thought to check in, which now was incessantly.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_024.jpg	Months later, the AFib had not recurred, but my surveillance of my poor heart had gotten out of control. I checked myblood pressure daily
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_025.jpg	and listened for signs of ventricular eccentricity every time I got into bed. It took months of not having a stroke before I could once again
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_026.jpg	trust my heart to go about its business without my supervision. Gradually, thankfully, it retreated once again to the background of my
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_027.jpg	attention.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_028.jpg	I tell you all this by way of explaining why I felt I should talk to my cardiologist before embarking on a psychedelic journey. My
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_029.jpg	cardiologist was my age, so not likely to be shocked by the word “psilocybin” or “LSD” or “MDMA.” I told him what I had in mind and
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_030.jpg	asked if any of the drugs in question were contraindicated, given my coronary issues, or if there was any risk of an interaction with the
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_031.jpg	meds he had prescribed. He was not overly concerned about the psychedelics—most of them concentrate their effects in the mind with
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_032.jpg	remarkably little impact on the cardiovascular system—but one of the drugs I mentioned he advised I avoid. This was MDMA, also known
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_033.jpg	as Ecstasy or Molly, which has been on schedule 1 since the mid-1980s, when it emerged as a popular rave drug.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_034.jpg	The drug 3,4-methylenedioxymethamphetamine is not a classical psychedelic (it works on different brain receptors and doesn’t have strong
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_035.jpg	visual effects), yet several of the guides I was interviewing had told me it was part of their regimen. Sometimes called an empathogen,
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_036.jpg	MDMA lowers psychological defenses and helps to swiftly build a bond between patient and therapist. (Leo Zeff was one of the first
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_037.jpg	therapists to use MDMA in the 1970s, after the compound was popularized by his friend the legendary Bay Area chemist Sasha Shulgin and
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_038.jpg	his wife, the therapist Ann Shulgin. Guides told me MDMA was a good way to “break the ice” and establish trust before the psychedelic
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_039.jpg	journey.
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_040.jpg	(One said, “It condenses years of psychotherapy into an afternoon.”) But as its scientific name indicates, MDMA is an amphetamine, and so,
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_041.jpg	chemically, it implicates the heart in a way psychedelics don’t. I was disappointed my cardiologist had taken MDMA off the table but
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_042.jpg	pleased that he had more or less given me a green light on the rest of my travel plans. Trip One: LSDAt least on paper, nothing about the
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_043.jpg	first guide I chose to work with sounds auspicious. The man lived and worked so far off the grid, in the mountains of the American West,
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_044.jpg	that he had no phone service, generated his own electricity, pumped his own water, grew his own food, and had only the spottiest satellite
test/images/synth_doc_00128_line_045.jpg	Internet.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_000.jpg	Because I had never much enjoyed video games, this seemed cruel, an expulsion from the garden: no plants, no people, no sunlight. Not
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_001.jpg	that the computer world wasn’t an interesting place to explore.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_002.jpg	I watched in awe as, one by one, musical notes turned into palpable forms before my eyes. Annoying music was the presiding deity of the
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_003.jpg	place, the generative force. Even the most spa-appropriate New Age composition had the power to spawn fractal patterns in space that
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_004.jpg	grew and branched and multiplied to infinity. Weirdly, everything in my visual field was black, but in so many different shades that it was
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_005.jpg	easy to see. I was traversing a world generated by mathematical algorithms, and this gave it a certain alienated, lifeless beauty.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_006.jpg	But whose world was it? Not mine, and I began to wonder, whose brain am I in?
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_007.jpg	(Please, not Thierry David’s!) “This could easily take a terrifying turn,” it occurred to me, and with that a dim tide of anxiety began to
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_008.jpg	build. Recalling the flight instructions, I told myself there was nothing to do but let go and surrender to the experience. Relax and float
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_009.jpg	downstream.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_010.jpg	This was not at all like previous trips, which had left me more or less the captain of my attention, able to direct it this way or that and
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_011.jpg	change the mental channel at will. No, this was more like being strapped into the front car of a cosmic roller coaster, its heedless headlong
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_012.jpg	trajectory determining moment by moment what would appear in my field of consciousness. Actually, this is not completely accurate: all I
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_013.jpg	had to do was to remove my eyeshades and reality, or at least something loosely based on it, wouldreconstitute itself. This is what I now
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_014.jpg	did, partly to satisfy myself that the world was still existing but mostly because I badly had to pee.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_015.jpg	Sunlight and color flooded my eyes, and I drank it in greedily, surveying the room for the welcome signifiers of non-digital reality: walls,
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_016.jpg	windows, plants. But all of it appeared in a new aspect: jeweled with light. I realized I should probably put on my glasses, which partly
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_017.jpg	domesticated the scene, but only partly: objects continued to send their sparkles of light my way. I got up carefully from the mattress, first
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_018.jpg	onto one knee, then, unsteadily, onto my feet. Mary took me by the elbow, geriatrically, and together we made the journey across the room.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_019.jpg	I avoided looking at her, uncertain what I might see in her face or betray in mine. At the bathroom door she let go of my elbow.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_020.jpg	Inside, the bathroom was a riot of sparkling light. The arc of water I sent forth was truly the most beautiful thing I had ever seen, a waterfall
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_021.jpg	of diamonds cascading into a pool, breaking its surface into a billion clattering fractals of light. This went on for a pleasant eternity.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_022.jpg	When I was out of diamonds, I went to the sink and splashed my face with water, making sure not to catch sight of myself in the mirror,
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_023.jpg	which seemed like a psychologically risky thing to do. I made my unsteady way back to the mattress and lay down. Speaking softly, Mary
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_024.jpg	asked if I wanted a booster.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_025.jpg	I did and sat up to receive it. Mary was squatting next to me, and when I finally looked up into her face, I saw she had turned into María
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_026.jpg	Sabina, the Mexican curandera who had given psilocybin to R. Gordon Wasson in that dirt basement in Huautla de Jiménez sixty years ago.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_027.jpg	Her hair was black, her face, stretched taut over its high cheekbones, was anciently weathered, and she was wearing a simple white peasant
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_028.jpg	dress. I took the dried mushroom from the woman’s wrinkled brown hand and looked away as I chewed. I didn’t think I should tell Mary
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_029.jpg	what had happened to her.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_030.jpg	(Later, when I did, she was flattered: María Sabina was her hero.) • • • BUT THERE WAS SOMETHING I needed to do before putting my
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_031.jpg	eyeshades back on and going back under, a little experiment I had told Mary I wanted to perform on myself during my trip. I wasn’t sure if
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_032.jpg	in mycondition I could pull it off, but I’d found that even in the middle of the journey it was possible to summon oneself to a semblance of
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_033.jpg	normality for a few moments at a time.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_034.jpg	Loaded on my laptop was a brief video of a rotating face mask, used in a psychological test called the binocular depth inversion illusion. As
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_035.jpg	the mask rotates in space, its convex side turning to reveal its concave back, something remarkable happens: the hollow mask appears to
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_036.jpg	pop out to become convex again. This is a trick performed by the mind, which assumes all faces to be convex, and so automatically corrects
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_037.jpg	for the seeming error—unless, as a neuroscientist had told me, one was under the influence of a psychedelic.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_038.jpg	This auto-correct feature is a hallmark of our perception, which in the sane, adult mind is based as much on educated guesswork as the raw
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_039.jpg	data of the senses. By adulthood, the mind has gotten very good at observing and testing reality and developing confident predictions
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_040.jpg	about it that optimize our investments of energy (mental and otherwise) and therefore our survival. So rather than starting from scratch to
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_041.jpg	build a new perception from every batch of raw data delivered by the senses, the mind jumps to the most sensible conclusion based on past
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_042.jpg	experience combined with a tiny sample of that data. Our brains are prediction machines optimized by experience, and when it comes to
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_043.jpg	faces, they have boatloads of experience: faces are always convex, so this hollow mask must be a prediction error to be corrected.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_044.jpg	These so-called Bayesian inferences (named for Thomas Bayes, the eighteenth-century English philosopher who developed the mathematics
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_045.jpg	of probability, on which these mental predictions are based) serve us well most of the time, speeding perception while saving effort and
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_046.jpg	energy, but they can also trap us in literally preconceived images of reality that are simply false, as in the case of the rotating mask. Yet it
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_047.jpg	turns out that Bayesian inference breaks down in some people: schizophrenics and, according to some neuroscientists, people on high
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_048.jpg	doses of psychedelics drugs, neither of whom “see” in this predictive or conventionalized manner. (Nor do young children, who have yet
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_049.jpg	to build the sort of database necessary for confident predictions.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_050.jpg	This raises an interesting question: Is it possible that the perceptions of schizophrenics, people tripping on psychedelics, and young
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_051.jpg	children are, at least incertain instances, more accurate—less influenced by expectation and therefore more faithful to reality—than those of
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_052.jpg	sane and sober adults? Before we started, I had cued up the video on my laptop, and now I clicked to run it. The mask on the screen, gray
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_053.jpg	against a black ground, was clearly the product of computer animation and was uncannily consistent with the visual style of the world I’d
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_054.jpg	been in. (During my integration session with Mary the next day, she suggested that it might have been this image on my laptop that had
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_055.jpg	conjured the computer world and trapped me in it.
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_056.jpg	Could there be a better demonstration of the power of set and setting? As the convex face rotated to reveal its concave back, the mask
test/images/synth_doc_00127_line_057.jpg	popped back out, only a bit more slowly than it did before I ate the mushroom.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_000.jpg	This surprised me, because I have never thought of myself as a particularly spiritual, much less mystical, person. This is partly a function of
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_001.jpg	worldview, I suppose, and partly of neglect: I’ve never devoted much time to exploring spiritualpaths and did not have a religious
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_002.jpg	upbringing. My default perspective is that of the philosophical materialist, who believes that matter is the fundamental substance of the
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_003.jpg	world and the physical laws it obeys should be able to explain everything that happens.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_004.jpg	I start from the assumption that nature is all that there is and gravitate toward scientific explanations of phenomena. That said, I’m also
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_005.jpg	sensitive to the limitations of the scientific-materialist perspective and believe that nature (including the human mind) still holds deep
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_006.jpg	mysteries toward which science can sometimes seem arrogant and unjustifiably dismissive. Was it possible that a single psychedelic
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_007.jpg	experience—something that turned on nothing more than the ingestion of a pill or square of blotter paper—could put a big dent in such a
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_008.jpg	worldview? Shift how one thought about mortality? Actually change one’s mind in enduring ways?
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_009.jpg	The idea took hold of me. It was a little like being shown a door in a familiar room—the room of your own mind—that you had somehow
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_010.jpg	never noticed before and being told by people you trusted (scientists!) that a whole other way of thinking—of being!—lay waiting on the
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_011.jpg	other side. All you had to do was turn the knob and enter. Who wouldn’t be curious?
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_012.jpg	I might not have been looking to change my life, but the idea of learning something new about it, and of shining a fresh light on this old
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_013.jpg	world, began to occupy my thoughts. Maybe there was something missing from my life, something I just hadn’t named.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_014.jpg	Now, I already knew something about such doors, having written about psychoactive plants earlier in my career. In The Botany of Desire, I
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_015.jpg	explored at some length what I had been surprised to discover is a universal human desire to change consciousness. There is not a culture
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_016.jpg	on earth (well, one*) that doesn’t make use of certain plants to change the contents of the mind, whether as a matter of healing, habit, or
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_017.jpg	spiritual practice. That such a curious and seemingly maladaptive desire should exist alongside our desires for nourishment and beauty
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_018.jpg	and sex—all of which make much more obvious evolutionary sense—cried out for an explanation. The simplest was that these substances
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_019.jpg	help relieve pain and boredom.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_020.jpg	Yet the powerful feelings and elaborate taboos and rituals that surround many of these psychoactive species suggest there must be
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_021.jpg	something more to it. For our species, I learned, plants and fungi with the power to radically alter consciousness have long and widely been
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_022.jpg	used as tools for healingthe mind, for facilitating rites of passage, and for serving as a medium for communicating with supernatural
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_023.jpg	realms, or spirit worlds. These uses were ancient and venerable in a great many cultures, but I ventured one other application: to enrich the
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_024.jpg	collective imagination—the culture—with the novel ideas and visions that a select few people bring back from wherever it is they go. • • •
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_025.jpg	NOW THAT I HAD DEVELOPED an intellectual appreciation for the potential value of these psychoactive substances, you might think I
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_026.jpg	would have been more eager to try them.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_027.jpg	I’m not sure what I was waiting for: courage, maybe, or the right opportunity, which a busy life lived mainly on the right side of the law
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_028.jpg	never quite seemed to afford. But when I began to weigh the potential benefits I was hearing about against the risks, I was surprised to
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_029.jpg	learn that psychedelics are far more frightening to people than they are dangerous.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_030.jpg	Many of the most notorious perils are either exaggerated or mythical. It is virtually impossible to die from an overdose of LSD or
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_031.jpg	psilocybin, for example, and neither drug is addictive. After trying them once, animals will not seek a second dose, and repeated use by
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_032.jpg	people robs the drugs of their effect.* It is true that the terrifying experiences some people have on psychedelics can risk flipping those at
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_033.jpg	risk into psychosis, so no one with a family history or predisposition to mental illness should ever take them. But emergency room
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_034.jpg	admissions involving psychedelics are exceedingly rare, and many of the cases doctors diagnose as psychotic breaks turn out to be merely
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_035.jpg	short-lived panic attacks.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_036.jpg	It is also the case that people on psychedelics are liable to do stupid and dangerous things: walk out into traffic, fall from high places, and,
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_037.jpg	on rare occasions, kill themselves. “Bad trips” are very real and can be one of “the most challenging experiences of [a] lifetime,” according
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_038.jpg	to a large survey of psychedelic users asked about their experiences.* But it’s important to distinguish what can happen when these drugs
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_039.jpg	are used in uncontrolled situations, without attention to set and setting, from what happens under clinical conditions, after careful
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_040.jpg	screening and under supervision. Since the revival of sanctioned psychedelic researchbeginning in the 1990s, nearly a thousand volunteers
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_041.jpg	have been dosed, and not a single serious adverse event has been reported. • • • IT WAS AT THIS POINT that the idea of “shaking the
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_042.jpg	snow globe,” as one neuroscientist described the psychedelic experience, came to seem more attractive to me than frightening, though it
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_043.jpg	was still that too. After more than half a century of its more or less constant companionship, one’s self—this ever-present voice in the head,
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_044.jpg	this ceaselessly commenting, interpreting, labeling, defending I—becomes perhaps a little too familiar.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_045.jpg	I’m not talking about anything as deep as self-knowledge here. No, just about how, over time, we tend to optimize and conventionalize our
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_046.jpg	responses to whatever life brings. Each of us develops our shorthand ways of slotting and processing everyday experiences and solving
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_047.jpg	problems, and while this is no doubt adaptive—it helps us get the job done with a minimum of fuss—eventually it becomes rote. It dulls us.
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_048.jpg	The muscles of attention atrophy. Habits are undeniably useful tools, relieving us of the need to run a complex mental operation every time
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_049.jpg	we’re confronted with a new task or situation. Yet they also relieve us of the need to stay awake to the world: to attend, feel, think, and then
test/images/synth_doc_00129_line_050.jpg	act in a deliberate manner.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_000.jpg	It was staggering.” It would probably be too strong to describe this far-flung and disparate group as a community, much less an
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_001.jpg	organization, yet my interviews with more than a dozen of them suggest they are professionals who share an outlook, a set of practices,
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_002.jpg	and even a code of conduct. Soon after the meeting in San Jose, a “wiki” appeared on the Internet—a collaborative website where
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_003.jpg	individuals can share documents and together create new content. (Fadiman included the URL in his 2011 book, The Psychedelic Explorer’s
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_004.jpg	Guide.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_005.jpg	Here, I found two items of particular interest, as well as several sub-wikis—documents under development—that hadn’t had a new entry
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_006.jpg	for several years; it could be that public disclosure of the site in Fadiman’s book had led the creators to abandon it or move elsewhere
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_007.jpg	online. The first item was a draft charter: “to support a category of profound, prized experiences becoming more available to more people.”
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_008.jpg	These experiences are described as “unitive consciousness” and “non-dual consciousness,” among other terms, and several
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_009.jpg	non-pharmacological modalities for achieving these states are mentioned, including meditation, breathwork, and fasting. “A principal tool
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_010.jpg	of the Guides is the judicious use of a class of psychoactive substances” known to be “potent spiritual catalysts.” The website offers
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_011.jpg	would-be guides links to printable forms for legal releases, ethical agreements, and medical questionnaires.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_012.jpg	(“We don’t have very good insurance,” one guide told me, with a sardonic smile. “So we’re very careful.”) There’s also a link to a
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_013.jpg	thoughtful “Code of Ethics for Spiritual Guides,” which acknowledges the psychological and physical risks of journeying and emphasizes
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_014.jpg	the guide’s ultimate responsibility for the well-being of the client. Recognizing that during “primary religious practices” “participants may
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_015.jpg	be especially open to suggestion, manipulation, and exploitation,” the code states that it is incumbent upon the guide to disclose all risks,
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_016.jpg	obtain consent, guarantee confidentiality,protect the safety and health of participants at all times, “safeguard against . . . ambition” and
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_017.jpg	self-promotion, and accommodate clients “without regard to their ability to pay.” Perhaps the most useful document on the website is the
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_018.jpg	“Guidelines for Voyagers and Guides.”* The guidelines represent a compendium of half a century’s accumulated knowledge and wisdom
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_019.jpg	about how best to approach the psychedelic journey, whether as a participant or as a guide. It covers the basics of set and setting; mental
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_020.jpg	and physical preparation for the session; potential drug interactions; the value of formulating an intention; what to expect during the
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_021.jpg	experience, both good and bad; the stages of the journey; what can go wrong and how to deal with frightening material; the supreme
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_022.jpg	importance of post-session “integration”; and so on.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_023.jpg	For me, standing on the threshold of such an experience, it was reassuring to learn that the underground community of psychedelic guides,
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_024.jpg	which I had assumed consisted of a bunch of individuals all doing pretty much their own thing, operated like professionals, working from
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_025.jpg	a body of accumulated knowledge and experience and in a set of traditions that had been handed down from psychedelic pioneers such as
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_026.jpg	Al Hubbard, Timothy Leary, Myron Stolaroff, Stan Grof, and Leo Zeff. They had rules and codes and agreements, and many elements of the
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_027.jpg	work had been more or less institutionalized.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_028.jpg	Stumbling upon the website also made me appreciate just how far the culture of psychedelics has evolved since the 1950s and 1960s.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_029.jpg	Implicit in these documents, it seemed to me, was the recognition that these powerful, anarchic medicines can and have been misused and
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_030.jpg	that if they are to do more good than harm, they require a cultural vessel of some kind: protocols, rules, and rituals that together form a
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_031.jpg	kind of Apollonian counterweight to contain and channel their sheer Dionysian force. Modern medicine, with its controlled trials and
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_032.jpg	white-coated clinicians and DSM diagnoses, offers one such container; the underground guides offer another. • • •YET THE FIRST
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_033.jpg	COUPLE of guides I interviewed did not fill me with confidence.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_034.jpg	Maybe it was because I was so new to the territory, and nervous about the contemplated journey, but I kept hearing things in their spiels
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_035.jpg	that set off alarm bells and made me want to run in the opposite direction. Andrei, the first guide I interviewed, was a gruff Romanian-born
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_036.jpg	psychologist in his late sixties with decades of experience; he had worked with a friend of a friend of a friend. We met at his office in a
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_037.jpg	modest neighborhood of small bungalows and neat lawns in a city in the Pacific Northwest.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_038.jpg	A hand-lettered sign on the door instructed visitors to remove their shoes and come upstairs to the dimly lit waiting room. A kilim rug had
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_039.jpg	been pinned to the wall. Instead of a table piled with old copies of People or Consumer Reports, I found a small shrine populated with
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_040.jpg	spiritual artifacts from a bewildering variety of traditions: a Buddha, a crystal, a crow’s wing, a brass bowl for burning incense, a branch of
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_041.jpg	sage. At the back of the shrine stood two framed photographs, one of a Hindu guru I didn’t recognize and the other of a Mexican curandera
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_042.jpg	I did: María Sabina.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_043.jpg	This was not the last time I would encounter such a confusing tableau. In fact every guide I met maintained some such shrine in the room
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_044.jpg	where he or she worked, and clients were often asked to contribute an item of personal significance before embarking on their journeys.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_045.jpg	What I was tempted to dismiss as a smorgasbord of equal-opportunity New Age tchotchkes, I would eventually come to regard more
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_046.jpg	sympathetically, as the material expression of the syncretism prevalent in the psychedelic community.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_047.jpg	Members of this community tend to be more spiritual than religious in any formal sense, focused on the common core of mysticism or
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_048.jpg	“cosmic consciousness” that they believe lies behind all the different religious traditions. So what appeared to me as a bunch of conflicting
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_049.jpg	symbols of divinity are in fact different means of expressing or interpreting the same underlying spiritual reality, “the perennial
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_050.jpg	philosophy” that Aldous Huxley held to undergird all religions and to which psychedelics supposedly can offer direct access. After a few
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_051.jpg	minutes, Andrei bounded into the room, and when I stood to offer my hand, he surprised me with a bear hug. A big man with a full head of
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_052.jpg	hastily combed gray hair, Andrei was wearing a blue-checked button-down over a yellow T-shirt that struggled to encompass the globeof
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_053.jpg	his belly. Speaking with a thick accent, he managed to seem both amiable and disconcertingly blunt.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_054.jpg	Andrei had his first experience with LSD at twenty-one, soon after he came out of the army; a friend had sent it from America, and the
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_055.jpg	experience transformed him. “It made me realize we live a very limited version of what life is.” That realization propelled him on a journey
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_056.jpg	through Eastern religion and Western psychology that eventually culminated in a doctorate in psychology. When military service
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_057.jpg	threatened to interrupt his psycho-spiritual journey, he “decided I have to make my own choices” and deserted.
test/images/synth_doc_00125_line_058.jpg	Andrei eventually left Bucharest for San Francisco, bound for what he had heard was “the first New Age graduate school”—the California
