test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_000.jpg	He gave her awhen he was recognized by a Taiwanese nun at a retreat cave. He gave her a letter (telling her to send it
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_001.jpg	after he had moved on) that said not to worry, he was fine—and exhorting his students to practice.
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_002.jpg	A photo that surfaced when a monk, a longtime friend, managed to join Mingyur shows a radiant face with a wispy beard
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_003.jpg	and long hair, his expression one of ebullient rapture. Then, suddenly, in November 2015, after almost four and a half years
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_004.jpg	as a wanderer in radio silence, Mingyur reappeared at his monastery in Bodh Gaya. On hearing that news, Richie arranged
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_005.jpg	to see him during a visit to India that December. Months later, Mingyur stopped in Madison while on an American teaching
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_006.jpg	tour, and stayed at Richie’s house.
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_007.jpg	Within minutes of his arrival at the house Mingyur agreed to go back into the scanner. Only a few months after returning
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_008.jpg	from his hardscrabble life he seemed right at home in this up-to-the-minute lab. As Mingyur entered the MRI suite, the lab
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_009.jpg	technician gave him a friendly welcome, saying, “I was the tech the last time you were in the scanner.” Mingyur beamed his
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_010.jpg	electric smile in return. While he waited for the machine to be readied, Mingyur joked with another member of Richie’s
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_011.jpg	team, an Indian scientist from Hyderabad.
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_012.jpg	Given the go-ahead, Mingyur left his sandals at the bottom of the two-step ladder that boosted him to the MRI table and lay
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_013.jpg	down so the tech could strap his head into a cradle tight enough that it allows no more than 2 millimeters of movement—all
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_014.jpg	the better to obtain sharp images of his brain. His calves, thickened by years of trekking the steep slopes of the Himalayas,
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_015.jpg	protruded from his monk’s robes and then disappeared as the table slipped into the maw of the MRI. The technology had
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_016.jpg	improved since his last visit; the monitors reveal a crisper image of his brain’s folds and tucks. It would take months to
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_017.jpg	compare these data with those collected years before, and to track the changes in his brain during that time against the
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_018.jpg	normal alterations seen in the brains of men his age. Although he was barraged with requests, following his return from this
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_019.jpg	last retreat, to have his brain scanned by many labs all over the world, Mingyur turned most all of them down for fear of
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_020.jpg	becoming a perpetual subject.
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_021.jpg	He had consented to have his brain rescanned by Richie and his team because he knew they had longitudinal data from
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_022.jpg	previous scans and could analyze ways his brain might be showing atypical changes. The first scan Richie’s lab had of
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_023.jpg	Mingyur’s brain was obtained in 2002; there was another in 2010 and now the most recent, in 2016.
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_024.jpg	These three scans provided the lab team with an opportunity to examine age-related declines ingray matter density, the site
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_025.jpg	of the brain’s molecular machinery. Each of us has a decrease in the density of gray matter as we age, and as we saw in
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_026.jpg	chapter nine, “Mind, Body, and Genome,” a given brain can be compared with a large database of the brains of other
test/images/synth_doc_00178_line_027.jpg	people the same age.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_000.jpg	To do this one would have to postulate even more complex manoeuvrings in space, governed by laws of physics very
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_001.jpg	different from those that operate on our supposedly stationary Earth. But they would be different in precisely such a way as
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_002.jpg	to remain observationally consistent with the Earth being in motion and the laws being the same out there as they are here.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_003.jpg	Many such theories are possible. Indeed, if making the right predictions were our only constraint, we could invent theories
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_004.jpg	which say that anything we please is going on in space.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_005.jpg	For example, observations alone can never rule out the theory that the Earth is enclosed in a giant planetarium showing us
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_006.jpg	a simulation of a heliocentric solar system; and that outside the planetarium there is anything you like, or nothing at all.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_007.jpg	Admittedly, to account for present-day observations the planetarium would also have to redirect our radar and laser pulses,
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_008.jpg	capture our space probes, and indeed astronauts, send back fakemessages from them and return them with appropriate
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_009.jpg	moonrock samples, altered memories, and so on. It may be an absurd theory, but the point is that it cannot be ruled out by
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_010.jpg	experiment. Nor is it valid to rule out any theory solely on the grounds that it is ‘absurd’: the Inquisition, together with most
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_011.jpg	of the human race in Galileo’s time, thought it the epitome of absurdity to claim that the Earth is moving.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_012.jpg	After all, we cannot feel it moving, can we? When it does move, as in an earthquake, we feel that unmistakably. It is said
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_013.jpg	that Galileo delayed publicly advocating the heliocentric theory for some years, not for fear of the Inquisition but simply for
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_014.jpg	fear of ridicule. To us, the Inquisition’s theory looks hopelessly contrived.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_015.jpg	Why should we accept such a complicated and ad hoc account of why the sky looks as it does, when the unadorned
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_016.jpg	heliocentric cosmology does the same job with less fuss? We may cite the principle of Occam’s razor: ‘do not multiply
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_017.jpg	entities beyond necessity’ — or, as I prefer to put it, ‘do not complicate explanations beyond necessity’, because if you do,
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_018.jpg	the unnecessary complications themselves remain unexplained.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_019.jpg	However, whether an explanation is or is not ‘contrived’ or ‘unnecessarily complicated’ depends on all the other ideas and
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_020.jpg	explanations that make up one’s world-view. The Inquisition would have argued that the idea of the Earth moving is an
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_021.jpg	unnecessary complication. It contradicts common sense; it contradicts Scripture; and (they would have said) there is a
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_022.jpg	perfectly good explanation that does without it. But is there?
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_023.jpg	Does the Inquisition’s theory really provide alternative explanations without having to introduce the counter-intuitive
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_024.jpg	‘complication’ of the heliocentric system? Let us take a closer look at how the Inquisition’s theory explains things. It explains
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_025.jpg	the apparent stationarity of the Earth by saying that it is stationary.
test/images/synth_doc_00181_line_026.jpg	So far, so good. On the face of it that explanation is better than Galileo’s, for he had to work very hard, and contradict some
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_000.jpg	GENOMICS “It’s just naive,” a grant reviewer bluntly told Richie, to think that one will see changes in how genes are
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_001.jpg	expressed during just one day of meditation. Richie had just received the same negative opinion via a review from the
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_002.jpg	National Institutes of Health rejecting his proposal for that exact study. Some background.
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_003.jpg	After genetic scientists mapped the entire human genome, they realized it wasn’t enough to just know if we had a given
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_004.jpg	gene or not. The real questions: Is that gene expressed? Is it manufacturing the protein for which it is designed?
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_005.jpg	And how much? Where is the “volume control” on the gene set? This meant there was another important step: finding what
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_006.jpg	turns our genes on or off. If we’ve inherited a gene that gives us a susceptibility to a disease like diabetes, we may never
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_007.jpg	develop the malady if, for example, we have a lifelong habit of getting regular exercise and not eating sugar. Sugar turns on
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_008.jpg	the genes for diabetes; exercise turns them off.
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_009.jpg	Sugar and exercise are “epigenetic” influencers, among the many, many factors that control whether or not a gene
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_010.jpg	expresses itself. Epigenetics has become a frontier of genomic studies. And Richie thought meditation just might have
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_011.jpg	epigenetic impacts, “down-regulating” the genes responsible for the inflammatory response. As we’ve seen, meditation
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_012.jpg	seems to do this—but the genetic mechanism for the effect was a complete mystery. Undeterred by the skeptics, his lab
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_013.jpg	went ahead, assaying changes in the expression of key genes before and after a day of meditation in a group of long- term
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_014.jpg	vipassana practitioners (average of about 6,000 lifetime hours).14 They followed a fixed eight-hour schedule of practice
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_015.jpg	sessions throughout the day, and listened to tapes of some inspiring talks and guided practices by Joseph Goldstein.
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_016.jpg	After the day of practice the meditators had a marked “down-regulation” of inflammatory genes—something that had never
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_017.jpg	been seen before in response toinflammatory genes—something that had never been seen before in response to a purely
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_018.jpg	mental practice. Such a drop, if sustained over a lifetime, might help combat diseases with onsets marked by chronic
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_019.jpg	low-grade inflammation. As we’ve said, these include many of the world’s major health problems, ranging from
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_020.jpg	cardiovascular disorders, arthritis, and diabetes to cancer.
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_021.jpg	And this epigenetic impact, remember, was a “naive” idea that countered the then prevailing wisdom in genetic science.
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_022.jpg	Despite assumptions to the contrary, Richie’s group had shown that a mental exercise, meditation, could be a driver of
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_023.jpg	benefits at the level of genes. Genetic science would have to change its assumptions about how the mind can help manage
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_024.jpg	the body. A handful of other studies find that meditation seems to have salutary epigenetic effects.
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_025.jpg	Loneliness, for instance, spurs higher levels of pro- inflammatory genes; MBSR can not only lower those levels—but also
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_026.jpg	lessen the feeling of being lonely.15 Though these were pilot studies, an epigenetic boost was found in research with two
test/images/synth_doc_00179_line_027.jpg	other meditation methods. One is Herb Benson’s “relaxation response,” which has a person silently repeat a chosen word
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_000.jpg	In other words, it is the reason why human beings exist. The ecological niche that human beings occupy depends on virtual
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_001.jpg	reality as directly and as absolutely as the ecological niche that koala bears occupy depends on eucalyptus leaves.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_002.jpg	TERMINOLOGY image generator A device that can generate specifiable sensations for a user. universal image generator An
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_003.jpg	image generator that can be programmed to generate any sensation that the user is capable of experiencing. external
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_004.jpg	experience An experience of something outside one’s own mind. Internal experience An experience of something within
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_005.jpg	one’s own mind. physically possible Not forbidden by the laws of physics. An environment is physically possible if and only if
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_006.jpg	it exists somewhere in the multiverse (on the assumption that the initial conditions and all other supplementary data of the
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_007.jpg	multiverse are determined by some as yet unknown laws of physics). logically possible Self-consistent. virtual reality Any
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_008.jpg	situation in which the user is given the experience of being in a specified environment. repertoire The repertoire of a
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_009.jpg	virtual-reality generator is the set of environments that the generator can be programmed to give the user the experience
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_010.jpg	of. image Something that gives rise to sensations.accuracy An image is accurate in so far as the sensations it generates are
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_011.jpg	close to the intended sensations.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_012.jpg	A rendered environment is accurate in so far as it would respond in the intended way to every possible action of the user.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_013.jpg	perfect accuracy Accuracy so great that the user cannot distinguish the image or rendered environment from the intended
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_014.jpg	one. SUMMARY Virtual reality is not just a technology in which computers simulate the behaviour of physical environments.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_015.jpg	The fact that virtual reality is possible is an important fact about the fabric of reality. It is the basis not only of computation,
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_016.jpg	but of human imagination and external experience, science and mathematics, art and fiction.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_017.jpg	What are the ultimate limits — the full scope — of virtual reality (and hence of computation, science, imagination and the
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_018.jpg	rest)? In the next chapter we shall see that in one respect the scope of virtual reality is unlimited, while in another it is
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_019.jpg	drastically circumscribed.6 Universality and the Limits of Computation The heart of a virtual-reality generator is its computer,
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_020.jpg	and the question of what environments can be rendered in virtual reality must eventually come down to the question of
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_021.jpg	what computations can be performed.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_022.jpg	Even today, the repertoire of virtual-reality generators is limited as much by their computers as by their image generators.
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_023.jpg	Whenever a new, faster computer, with more memory and better image-processing hardware, is incorporated into a
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_024.jpg	virtual-reality generator, the repertoire is enlarged. But will this always be so, or will we eventually encounter full
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_025.jpg	universality, as I have argued we should expect to in the case of image generators?
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_026.jpg	In other words, is there a single virtual-reality generator, buildable once and for all, that could be programmed to render
test/images/synth_doc_00182_line_027.jpg	any environment that the human mind is capable of experiencing? Just as with image generators, we do not mean by this
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_000.jpg	And, fMRI scans showed, the greater their increase in connectivity between the prefrontal region and the default areas that
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_001.jpg	generate our inner stream of chat, the greater the reductions in the cytokine. Presumably, putting the brakes on destructive
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_002.jpg	self-talk that floods us with thoughts of hopelessness and depression —understandable in the unemployed—also lowered
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_003.jpg	cytokine levels. How we relate to our gloomy self-talk has a direct impact on our health.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_004.jpg	HYPERTENSION? RELAX. The moment you woke up today, were you breathing in or breathing out? That hard-to-answer
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_005.jpg	question was put to a retreatant by the late Burmese monk and meditation master Sayadaw U Pandita. It bespeaks the
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_006.jpg	extremely conscientious and precise version of mindfulness he was renowned for teaching.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_007.jpg	The sayadaw was the direct lineage holder of the great Burmese teacher Mahasi Sayadaw, as well as spiritual guide to Aung
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_008.jpg	San Suu Kyi during her years-long house arrest before she became Burma’s head of government. On his occasional trips to
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_009.jpg	the West, Mahasi Sayadaw had instructed many of the best- known teachers in the vipassana world. Dan had traveled
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_010.jpg	off-season to a rented kids’ summer camp in the high desert of Arizona to spend a few weeks under U Pandita’s guidance.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_011.jpg	As Dan later wrote in the New York Times Magazine, “The consuming task of my day was to build a precise attention to my
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_012.jpg	breath, noticing every nuance of eachinhalation and exhalation: its speed, lightness, coarseness, warmth.”11 The point for
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_013.jpg	Dan: clear the mind, and so, calm the body. While this retreat was one of a series Dan tried to fit into his yearly calendar in
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_014.jpg	the decades after returning from his graduate school sojourns in Asia, it wasn’t just meditation progress he hoped for. Over
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_015.jpg	the fifteen years or so since his last long stay in India, his blood pressure had gotten too high, and Dan hoped this retreat
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_016.jpg	would lower it, at least for a while. His physician had been troubled by readings over 140/90, the lower border of
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_017.jpg	hypertension.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_018.jpg	And when Dan returned home from retreat, he was pleased to find a reading far below that borderline. The notion that
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_019.jpg	people could lower blood pressure through meditation largely originated with Dr.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_020.jpg	Herbert Benson, a Harvard Medical School cardiologist. When we were at Harvard, Dr. Benson had just published one of the
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_021.jpg	first studies on the topic showing meditation seemed to help lower blood pressure.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_022.jpg	Herb, as we know him, served on Dan’s dissertation committee, and was one of the few faculty members anywhere at
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_023.jpg	Harvard sympathetic to meditation studies. As later research on meditation and blood pressure have shown, he was on the
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_024.jpg	right track.
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_025.jpg	Take, for example, a well-designed study of African American men, who are at particularly high risk for hypertension,
test/images/synth_doc_00183_line_026.jpg	cardiac and kidney disease. Just fourteen minutes of mindfulness practice in a group who already suffered from kidney
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_000.jpg	As these young scientists entered academic posts, they swelled the numbers of researchers doing such studies. They have
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_001.jpg	driven in no small part the ever- growing numbers of scientific studies on meditation. At the same time, more established
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_002.jpg	scientists have shifted their focus toward this area as results showed valuable yield.
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_003.jpg	The findings rolling out of Richie’s brain lab at the University of Wisconsin—and labs of other scientists, from the medical
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_004.jpg	schools of Stanford and Emory, Yale and Harvard, and far beyond— routinely make headlines. Given meditation’s booming
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_005.jpg	popularity, we feel a need for a hard-nosed look. The neural and biological benefits best documented by sound science are
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_006.jpg	not necessarily the ones we hear about in the press, on Facebook, or from email marketing blasts. And some of those
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_007.jpg	trumpeted far and wide have little scientific merit.
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_008.jpg	Many reports boil down to the ways a short daily dose of meditation alters our biology and emotional life for the better. This
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_009.jpg	news, gone viral, has drawn millions worldwide to find a slot in their daily routine for meditation.
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_010.jpg	But there are far greater possibilities—and some perils. The moment has come to tell the bigger tale the headlines are
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_011.jpg	missing. There are several threads in the tapestry we weave here.
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_012.jpg	One can be seen in the story of our decades-long friendship and our shared sense of a greater purpose, at first a distant
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_013.jpg	and unlikely goal but one in which we persisted despite obstacles. Another traces the emergence of neuroscience’s evidence
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_014.jpg	that our experiences shape our brains, a platform supporting our theory that as meditation trains the mind, it reshapes the
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_015.jpg	brain. Then there’s the flood of data we’ve mined to show the gradient of this change.At the outset, mere minutes a day of
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_016.jpg	practice have surprising benefits (though not all those that are claimed). Beyond such payoffs at the beginning, we can now
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_017.jpg	show that the more hours you practice, the greater the benefits you reap. And at the highest levels of practice we find true
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_018.jpg	altered traits—changes in the brain that science has never observed before, but which we proposed decades ago.2 Ancient
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_019.jpg	Clues O ur story starts one early November morning in 1970, when the spire of the stupa in Bodh Gaya was lost to view,
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_020.jpg	enveloped in the ethereal mist rising from the Niranjan River nearby.
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_021.jpg	Next to the stupa stood a descendant of the very Bodhi Tree under which, legend has it, Buddha sat in meditation as he
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_022.jpg	became enlightened. Through the mist that morning, Dan glimpsed an elderly Tibetan monk amble by as he made his
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_023.jpg	postdawn rounds, circumambulating the holy site. With short-cropped gray hair and eyeglasses as thick as the bottoms of
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_024.jpg	Coke bottles, he fingered his mala beads while mumbling softly a mantra praising the Buddha as a sage, or muni in
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_025.jpg	Sanskrit: “Muni, muni, mahamuni, mahamuniya swaha!” A few days later, friends happened to bring Dan to visit that very
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_026.jpg	monk, Khunu Lama.
test/images/synth_doc_00186_line_027.jpg	He inhabited a sparse, unheated cell, its concrete walls radiating the late-fall chill. A wooden-plank tucket served as both
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_000.jpg	This argument is trying to show that solipsism is literally indefensible, because by accepting such a defence one is implicitly
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_001.jpg	contradicting it. But our solipsistic professor could try to evade that argument by saying something like this: ‘I can and do
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_002.jpg	consistently defend solipsism. Not against other people, for there are no other people, but against opposing arguments.
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_003.jpg	These arguments come to my attention through dream-people, who behave as if they were thinking beings whose ideas
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_004.jpg	often oppose mine.
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_005.jpg	My lecture and the arguments it contains were not intended to persuade these dream- people, but to persuade myself — to
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_006.jpg	help me to clarify my ideas.’ However, if there are sources of ideas that behave as if they were independent of oneself, then
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_007.jpg	they necessarily are independent of oneself. For if I define ‘myself as the conscious entity that has the thoughts and feelings
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_008.jpg	I am aware of having, then the ‘dream-people’ I seem to interact with are by definition something other than that narrowly
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_009.jpg	defined self, and so I must concede that something other than myself exists. My only other option, if I were a committed
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_010.jpg	solipsist, would be to regard the dream-peopleas creations of my unconscious mind, and therefore as part of ‘myself in a
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_011.jpg	looser sense. But then I should be forced to concede that ‘myself had a very rich structure, most of which is independent of
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_012.jpg	my conscious self. Within that structure are entities — dream-people — who, despite being mere constituents of the mind of
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_013.jpg	a supposed solipsist, behave exactly as if they were committed anti-solipsists.
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_014.jpg	So I could not call myself wholly a solipsist, for only my narrowly defined self would take that view. Many, apparently most,
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_015.jpg	of the opinions held within my mind as a whole would oppose solipsism. I could study the ‘outer’ region of myself and find
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_016.jpg	that it seems to obey certain laws, the same laws as the dream-textbooks say apply to what they call the physical universe.
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_017.jpg	I would find that there is far more of the outer region than the inner region.
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_018.jpg	Aside from containing more ideas, it is also more complex, more varied, and has more measurable variables, by a literally
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_019.jpg	astronomical factor, than the inner region. Moreover, this outer region is amenable to scientific study, using the methods of
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_020.jpg	Galileo. Because I have now been forced to define that region as part of myself, solipsism no longer has any argument
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_021.jpg	against the validity of such study, which is now defined as no more than a form of introspection. Solipsism allows, indeed
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_022.jpg	assumes, that knowledge of oneself can be obtained through introspection. It cannot declare the entities and processes
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_023.jpg	being studied to be unreal, since the reality of the self is its basic postulate.
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_024.jpg	Thus we see that if we take solipsism seriously — if we assume that it is true and that all valid explanations must
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_025.jpg	scrupulously conform to it — it self- destructs. How exactly does solipsism, taken seriously, differ from its common-sense
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_026.jpg	rival, realism?
test/images/synth_doc_00185_line_027.jpg	The difference is based on no more than a renaming scheme. Solipsism insists on referring to objectively different things
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_000.jpg	Dr Johnson’s criterion (My formulation) If it can kick back, it exists. A more elaborate version is: If, according to the simplest
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_001.jpg	explanation, an entity is complex and autonomous, then that entity is real.self-similarity Some parts of physical reality (such
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_002.jpg	as symbols, pictures or human thoughts) resemble other parts. The resemblance may be concrete, as when the images in a
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_003.jpg	planetarium resemble the night sky; more importantly, it may be abstract, as when a statement in quantum theory printed
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_004.jpg	in a book correctly explains an aspect of the structure of the multiverse. (Some readers may be familiar with the geometry
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_005.jpg	of fractals; the notion of self-similarity defined here is much broader than the one used in that field.) complexity theory The
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_006.jpg	branch of computer science concerned with what resources (such as time, memory capacity or energy) are required to
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_007.jpg	perform given classes of computations. SUMMARY Although solipsism and related doctrines are logically self-consistent, they
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_008.jpg	can be comprehensively refuted simply by taking them seriously as explanations.
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_009.jpg	Although they all claim to be simplified world-views, such an analysis shows them to be indefensible over-elaborations of
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_010.jpg	realism. Real entities behave in a complex and autonomous way, which can be taken as the criterion for reality: if something
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_011.jpg	‘kicks back’, it exists. Scientific reasoning, which uses observation not as a basis for extrapolation but to distinguish between
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_012.jpg	otherwise equally good explanations, can give us genuine knowledge about reality. Thus science and other forms of
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_013.jpg	knowledge are made possible by a special self-similarity property of the physical world.
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_014.jpg	Yet it was not physicists who first recognized and studied this property: it was mathematicians and computer theorists, and
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_015.jpg	they called it the universality of computation. The theory of computation is our third strand.5 Virtual Reality The theory of
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_016.jpg	computation has traditionally been studied almost entirely in the abstract, as a topic in pure mathematics. This is to miss the
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_017.jpg	point of it.
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_018.jpg	Computers are physical objects, and computations are physical processes. What computers can or cannot compute is
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_019.jpg	determined by the laws of physics alone, and not by pure mathematics. One of the most important concepts of the theory of
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_020.jpg	computation is universality. A universal computer is usually defined as an abstract machine that can mimic the computations
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_021.jpg	of any other abstract machine in a certain well-defined class.
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_022.jpg	However, the significance of universality lies in the fact that universal computers, or at least good approximations to them,
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_023.jpg	can actually be built, and can be used to compute not just each other’s behaviour but the behaviour of interesting physical
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_024.jpg	and abstract entities. The fact that this is possible is part of the self- similarity of physical reality that I mentioned in the
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_025.jpg	previous chapter. The best-known physical manifestation of universality is an area of technology that has been mooted for
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_026.jpg	decades but is only now beginning to take off, namely virtual reality.
test/images/synth_doc_00184_line_027.jpg	The term refers to any situation in which a person is artificially given the experience of being in a specified environment. For

test/images/synth_doc_00187_line_001.jpg	NREM Sleep,” PLoS One 8:8 (2013): e73417; doi:10.1371/journal.pone.0073417.

test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_000.jpg	A vision lets you see things in a new light, as he says, one “not to be found in the facts, methods, and results of the
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_001.jpg	preexisting state of the science.”8 Sure, we had a vision in this sense—but we had paltry methods or data available for
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_002.jpg	exploring this positive range of altered traits, and no idea of the brain mechanism that would allow such a profound shift.
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_003.jpg	We were determined to make the argument, but were years too soon for the crucial scientific piece in this puzzle.
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_004.jpg	Our dissertation data were feebly—very feebly—supportive of the idea that the more you practice how to generate a
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_005.jpg	meditative state, the more that practice shows lasting influences beyond the session itself. Still, as brain science has evolved
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_006.jpg	over the decades, we saw mounting rationales for our ideas.
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_007.jpg	Richie attended his first meeting of the Society for Neuroscience in 1975 in New York City, along with about 2,500 other
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_008.jpg	scientists, all exhilarated that they were seeing the birth of a new field (and none dreaming that these days those meetings
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_009.jpg	would draw more than 30,000 neuroscientists).9 In the mid-1980s one of the early presidents of the society, Bruce McEwen
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_010.jpg	of Rockefeller University, gave us scientific ammunition. McEwen put a dominant tree shrew in the same cage for
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_011.jpg	twenty-eight days with one lower in the pecking order—the rodent version of being trapped at work with a nightmare boss
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_012.jpg	24/7 for a month. The big shock from McEwen’s study was that in the brain of the dominated rodent, dendrites shrank in
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_013.jpg	the hippocampus, a node crucial for memory.
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_014.jpg	These branching projections of the body’s cells allow them to reach out to and act on other cells; shrinking dendritesbody’s
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_015.jpg	cells allow them to reach out to and act on other cells; shrinking dendrites mean faulty memory. McEwen’s results ripped
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_016.jpg	through the brain and behavioral sciences like a small tsunami, opening minds to the possibility that a given experience
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_017.jpg	could leave an imprint on the brain. McEwen was zeroing in on a holy grail for psychology: how stressful events produce
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_018.jpg	lingering neural scars. That an experience of any kind could leave its mark on the brain had, until then, been unthinkable.
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_019.jpg	To be sure, stress was par for the course for a laboratory rat—McEwen just upped the intensity.
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_020.jpg	The standard setup for lab rat living quarters was the rodent equivalent of solitary confinement: weeks or months on end in
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_021.jpg	a small wire cage and, if the rat was lucky, a running wheel for exercise. Contrast that life in perpetual boredom and social
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_022.jpg	isolation to something like a rodent health resort, with lots of toys, things to climb on, colorful walls, playmates, and
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_023.jpg	interesting spaces to explore. That’s the stimulating habitat Marion Diamond at the University of California at Berkeley built
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_024.jpg	for her lab rats. Working about the same time as McEwen, Diamond found the rats’ brains benefited, with thicker dendritic
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_025.jpg	branches connecting neurons and growth in brain areas, such as the prefrontal cortex, that are crucial in attention and self-
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_026.jpg	regulation.10 While McEwen’s work showed how adverse events can shrink parts of the brain, Diamond’s emphasized the
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_027.jpg	positive in her studies. Yet her work was largely met with a shrug in neuroscience, perhaps because it posed a direct
test/images/synth_doc_00188_line_028.jpg	challenge to pervasive beliefs in the field.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_000.jpg	DAVID: It was that the actual outcomes refuted all the rival theories, and corroborated the theory that now prevails.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_001.jpg	CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: Good. Now listen carefully, because you have just said something which is not only provably untrue,
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_002.jpg	but which you yourself conceded was untrue only moments ago. You say that the outcomes of experiments ‘refuted all the
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_003.jpg	rival theories’. But you know very well that no set of outcomes of experiments can refute all possible rivals to a general
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_004.jpg	theory.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_005.jpg	You said yourself that any set of past outcomes is (I quote) ‘consistent with an infinity of theories, including theories
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_006.jpg	predicting every logically possible outcome of my jumping over the railing’. It follows inexorably that the prediction you
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_007.jpg	favour was not justified by the experimental outcomes, because there are infinitely many other rivals to your theory, also
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_008.jpg	unrefuted as yet, which make the opposite prediction.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_009.jpg	DAVID: I’m glad I listened carefully, as you asked, for now I see that at least part of the difference between us has been
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_010.jpg	caused by a misunderstanding over terminology. When Popper speaks of ‘rival theories’ to a given theory, he does not mean
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_011.jpg	the set of all logically possible rivals: he means only the actual rivals, those proposed in the course of a rational controversy.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_012.jpg	(That includes theories ‘proposed’ purely mentally, by one person, in the course of a ‘controversy’ within one mind.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_013.jpg	CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: I see.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_014.jpg	Well, I’ll accept your terminology. But incidentally (I don’t think it matters, for present purposes, but I’m curious), isn’t it a
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_015.jpg	strange assertion you are attributing to Popper, that the reliability of a theory depends on the accident of what other
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_016.jpg	theories — false theories — people have proposed in the past, rather than just on the content of the theory in question, and
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_017.jpg	on the experimental evidence? DAVID: Not really. Even you inductivists speak of…
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_018.jpg	CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: I am not an inductivist! DAVID: Yes you are. CRYPTO-INDUCTIVIST: Hmph! Once again, I shall
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_019.jpg	accept your terminology if you insist.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_020.jpg	But you may as well call me a porcupine. It really is perverse to call a person an ‘inductivist’ if that person’s whole thesis is
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_021.jpg	that the invalidity of inductive reasoning presents us with an unsolved philosophical problem. DAVID: I don’t think so. I think
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_022.jpg	that that thesis is what defines, and always has defined, an inductivist.
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_023.jpg	But I see that Popper has at least achieved one thing: ‘inductivist’ has become a term of abuse! Anyway, I was explaining
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_024.jpg	why it’s not so strange that the reliability of a theory should depend on what false theories people have proposed in the
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_025.jpg	past. Even inductivists speak of a theory being reliable or not, given certain ‘evidence’. Well, Popperians might speak of a
test/images/synth_doc_00190_line_026.jpg	theory being the best available for use in practice, given a certain problem-situation.
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_000.jpg	People generally think of me as a fairly even-keeled and psychologically sturdy person, and I’ve played that role for so long
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_001.jpg	now— in my family as a child, in my family as an adult, with my friends, and with my colleagues—that it’s probably an
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_002.jpg	accurate enough characterization. But every so often, perhaps in the wee-hour throes of insomnia or under the influence of
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_003.jpg	cannabis, I have found myself tossed in a psychic storm of existential dread so dark and violent that the keel comes off the
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_004.jpg	boat, capsizing this trusty identity. At such times, I begin seriously to entertain the possibility that somewhere deep beneath
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_005.jpg	the equable presence I present, there exists a shadow me made up of forces roiling, anarchic, and potentially mad.
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_006.jpg	Just how thin is the skin of my sanity? There are times when I wonder. Perhaps we all do. But did I really want to find out?
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_008.jpg	D. Laing once said there are three things humanbeings are afraid of: death, other people, and their own minds. Put me
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_009.jpg	down as two for three. But there are moments when curiosity gets the better of fear. I guess for me such a moment had
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_010.jpg	arrived. • • • BY “PSYCHEDELIC UNDERGROUND,” I don’t mean the shadowy world of people making, selling, and using
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_011.jpg	psychedelic drugs illegally.
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_012.jpg	I have in mind a specific subset of that world, populated by perhaps a couple hundred “guides,” or therapists, working with
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_013.jpg	a variety of psychedelic substances in a carefully prescribed manner, with the intention of healing the ill or bettering the well
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_014.jpg	by helping them fulfill their spiritual, creative, or emotional potential. Many of these guides are credentialed therapists, so by
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_015.jpg	doing this work they are risking not only their freedom but also their professional licenses. I met one who was a physician
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_016.jpg	and heard about another.
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_017.jpg	Some are religious professionals—rabbis and ministers of various denominations; a few call themselves shamans; one
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_018.jpg	described himself as a druid. The rest are therapists trained in dizzying combinations of alternative schools: I met Jungians
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_019.jpg	and Reichians, Gestalt therapists and “transpersonal” psychologists; energy healers; practitioners of aura work, breathwork,
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_020.jpg	and bodywork; EST, past-life, and family constellation therapists, vision questers, astrologers, and meditation teachers of
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_021.jpg	every stripe—a shaggy reunion of that whole 1970s class of alternative “modalities” that usually get lumped together under
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_022.jpg	the rubric of the “human potential movement” and that has as its world headquarters Esalen. The New Age terminology can
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_023.jpg	be a little off-putting; there were times when I felt I was listening to people whose language and vocabulary had stopped
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_024.jpg	evolving sometime in the early 1970s, at the very moment when psychedelic therapy was forced underground, freezing a
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_025.jpg	subculture in time. I tracked down several of these people in the Bay Area, which probably has the largest concentration of
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_026.jpg	underground guides in the country, without much difficulty. Asking around, I soon discovered that a friend had a friend who
test/images/synth_doc_00191_line_027.jpg	worked with a guide down in Santa Cruz, doing an annual psilocybin journey on the occasion of his birthday.
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_000.jpg	There are only about 10 80 atoms in the entire visible universe, an utterly miniscule number compared with 10 500 . So if
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_001.jpg	the visible universe were the extent of physical reality, physical reality would not even remotely contain the resources
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_002.jpg	required to factorize such a large number. Who did factorize it, then? How, and where, was the computation performed?I
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_003.jpg	have been discussing traditional types of mathematical task that quantum computers would be able to perform more quickly
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_004.jpg	than existing machines.
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_005.jpg	But there is an additional class of new tasks open to quantum computers that no classical computer could perform at all. By
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_006.jpg	a strange coincidence, one of the first of these tasks to be discovered also concerns public-key cryptography. This time it is
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_007.jpg	not a matter of breaking an existing system, but of implementing a new, absolutely secure system of quantum
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_008.jpg	cryptography. In 1989, at IBM Research, Yorktown Heights, New York, in the office of the theoretician Charles Bennett, the
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_009.jpg	first working quantum computer was built.
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_010.jpg	It was a special-purpose quantum computer consisting of a pair of quantum cryptographic devices designed by Bennett and
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_011.jpg	Gilles Brassard of the University of Montreal. It became the first machine ever to perform non-trivial computations that no
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_012.jpg	Turing machine could perform. In Bennett and Brassard’s quantum cryptosystem, messages are encoded in the states of
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_013.jpg	individual photons emitted by a laser. Although many photons are needed to transmit a message (one photon per bit, plus
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_014.jpg	many more photons wasted in various inefficiencies), the machines can be built with existing technology because they need
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_015.jpg	to perform their quantum computations on only one photon at a time.
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_016.jpg	The system’s security is based not on intractability, either classical or quantum, but directly on the properties of quantum
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_017.jpg	interference: that is what gives it its classically unobtainable absolute security. No amount of future computation by any sort
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_018.jpg	of computer, whether for millions or trillions of years, would be of any help to an eavesdropper on quantum-encrypted
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_019.jpg	messages: for if one communicates through a medium exhibiting interference, one can detect eavesdroppers.
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_020.jpg	According to classical physics, there is nothing that can prevent an eavesdropper who has physical access to a
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_021.jpg	communication medium, such as a telephone line, from installing a passive listening device. But, as I have explained, if one
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_022.jpg	makes any measurement on a quantum system one alters its subsequent interference properties. The communication
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_023.jpg	protocol relies on this effect. The communicating parties effectively set up repeated interference experiments, co-ordinating
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_024.jpg	them over a public communication channel.
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_025.jpg	Only if the interference passes the test for there having been no eavesdropper do they pass on to the next stage of the
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_026.jpg	protocol, which is to use some of the transmitted information as a cryptographic key. At worst, persistent eavesdropper
test/images/synth_doc_00192_line_027.jpg	might prevent any communication from taking place at all (though of course that is more easily achieved just by cutting the
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_000.jpg	So whether copying takes place or not is exquisitely sensitive to the physical form of the insulin gene. The presence of the
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_001.jpg	gene in us proper form and location makes a difference to whether copying takes place, which makes it a replicator, though
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_002.jpg	there are countless other causes contributing to its replication as well.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_003.jpg	Along with genes, random sequences of A, C, G and T, sometimes called junk DNA sequences, are present in the DNA of
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_004.jpg	most organisms. They arealso copied and passed on to the organisms’ offspring. However, if such a sequence is replaced by
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_005.jpg	almost any other sequence of similar length, it is still copied.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_006.jpg	So we can infer that the copying of such sequences does not depend on their specific physical form. Unlike genes, junk DNA
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_007.jpg	sequences are not programs. If they have a function (and it is not known whether they do), it cannot be to carry
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_008.jpg	information of any kind. Although they are copied, they do not contribute causally to their own copying, and are therefore
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_009.jpg	not replicators.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_010.jpg	Actually, that is an exaggeration. Anything that is copied must have made at least some causal contribution to that copying.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_011.jpg	Junk DNA sequences, for instance, are made of DNA, which allows the cellular computer to copy them. It cannot copy
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_012.jpg	molecules other than DNA. It is not usually illuminating to consider something as a replicator if its causal contribution to its
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_013.jpg	own replication is small, though strictly speaking being a replicator is a matter of degree.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_014.jpg	I shall define the degree of adaptation of a replicator to a given environment as the degree to which the replicator
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_015.jpg	contributes causally to its own replication in that environment. If a replicator is well adapted to most environments of a
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_016.jpg	niche, we may call it well adapted to the niche. We have just seen that the insulin gene is highly adapted to its niche.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_017.jpg	Junk D N A sequences have a negligible degree of adaptation by comparison with the insulin gene, or any other bona fide
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_018.jpg	gene, but they are far more adapted to that niche than most molecules are. Notice that to quantify degrees of adaptation,
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_019.jpg	we have to consider not only the replicator in question but also a range of variants of it. The more sensitive the copying in a
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_020.jpg	given environment is to the replicator’s exact physical structure, the more adapted the replicator is to that environment. For
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_021.jpg	highly adapted replicators (which are the only ones worth calling replicators) we need consider only fairly small variations,
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_022.jpg	because under most large variations they would no longer be replicators. So we are contemplating replacing the replicator
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_023.jpg	by broadly similar objects.
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_024.jpg	To quantify the degree of adaptation to a niche, we have to consider the replicator’s degree of adaptation to each
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_025.jpg	environment of the niche. We must therefore consider variants of the environment as well as of the replicator. If most
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_026.jpg	variants of the replicator fail to cause most environments of its niche to copy them, then it would follow that our replicator’s
test/images/synth_doc_00193_line_027.jpg	form is a significant cause of its own copying in that niche, which is what we mean by saying that it is highly adapted to the
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_000.jpg	TM research has had a somewhat checkered history in part because most of it has been done by staff at Maharishi
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_001.jpg	University of Management (formerly Maharishi International University), which is a part of the organization that promotes
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_002.jpg	TM. This raises the concern of a conflict of interest, even when the research has been well done. For this reason, Richie’s
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_003.jpg	lab intentionally employs several scientists who are skeptical of meditation’s effects, and who raise a healthy number of
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_004.jpg	issues and questions that “true believers” in the practice might overlook or sweep under the rug.
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_005.jpg	One result: Richie’s lab has published several nonfindings, studies that test a specific hypothesis about the effect of
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_006.jpg	meditation and fail to observe the expected effect. The lab also publishes failures to replicate—studies that do not get the
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_007.jpg	same results when duplicating the method of previously published papers that found meditation has some beneficial effect.
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_008.jpg	Such failures to replicate earlier findings call them into question. Bringing in skeptics is but one of many ways to minimize
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_009.jpg	experimenter bias.
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_010.jpg	Another would be to study a group that is told about meditation practices and their benefits but gets no instruction. Better:
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_011.jpg	an “active control,” where one group engages in an activity unlike meditation, one that they believe will benefit them, such
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_012.jpg	as exercise. A further dilemma in our Harvard research, also still pervasive in psychology, was that the undergrads available
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_013.jpg	for study in our lab were nottypical of humanity as a whole. Our experiments were done with subjects known in the field as
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_014.jpg	WEIRD: Western, educated, industrialized, rich, and from democratic cultures.10 And using Harvard students, an outlier
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_015.jpg	group even among the WEIRD, makes the data less valuable in searching for universals in human nature. THE VARIETIES
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_016.jpg	OF THE MEDITATIVE EXPERIENCE Richie in his dissertation research was among the first neuroscientists to ask if we can
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_017.jpg	identify a neural signature of attention skill.
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_018.jpg	That basic question was, in those days, quite respectable. But Richie’s PhD research was in the spirit of that concealed
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_019.jpg	excursion into the mind in his undergraduate work. The agenda embedded, sub rosa, in the study: exploring if signs of skill
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_020.jpg	in attention differed in meditators and nonmeditators. Did meditators get better at focusing?
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_021.jpg	In those days, that was not a respectable question. Richie measured the brain electrical signals from the scalp of meditators
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_022.jpg	as they heard tones or saw flashing LED lights, while he instructed them to focus on the sounds and ignore the lights, or
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_023.jpg	vice versa. Richie analyzed the electrical signals for “event-related potential” (ERP), indicated by specific blips in response to
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_024.jpg	a light and/or tone. The ERP, embedded in a chorus of noise, is a signal so minuscule it is measured in
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_025.jpg	microvolts—millionths of a volt.
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_026.jpg	These tiny signals offer a window on how we allocate our attention. Richie found that the size of these tiny signals was
test/images/synth_doc_00194_line_027.jpg	diminished in response to the tone when meditators focused on the light, while the signals triggered by the light were
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_000.jpg	Not the wife, not the child. So you can really let go—and go.” This, I realized, was another reason I was eager to work with
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_001.jpg	a guide. When Judith and I had our magic mushroom day the previous summer, the simmer of worry about her welfare
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_002.jpg	kept intruding on my journey, forcing me to stay close to the surface.
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_003.jpg	Much as I hated the psychobabble-y locution, I loved the idea of someone “holding space” for me. “That night I’ll ask you to
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_004.jpg	make some notes before you go to sleep. On your last morning, we’ll compare notes and try to integrate and make sense of
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_005.jpg	your experience. Then I’ll cook you a big breakfast to get you ready to face the interstate!” We scheduled a time for me to
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_006.jpg	come back. • • •THE FIRST THING I learned about myself that first afternoon, working with Fritz in the yurt, is that I am
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_007.jpg	“easy to put under”—susceptible to trance, a mental space completely new to me and accessible by nothing more than a
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_008.jpg	shift in the pattern of one’s breathing.
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_009.jpg	It was the damnedest thing. Fritz’s instructions were straightforward: Breathe deeply and rapidly while exhaling as strongly
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_010.jpg	as you can. “At first it will feel unnatural and you’ll have to concentrate to maintain the rhythm, but after a few minutes your
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_011.jpg	body will take over and do it automatically.” I stretched out on the mattress and donned a pair of eyeshades while he put
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_012.jpg	on some music, something generically tribal and rhythmic, dominated by the pounding of a drum. He placed a plastic bucket
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_013.jpg	at my side, explaining that occasionally people throw up. It was hard work at first, to breathe in such an exaggerated and
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_014.jpg	unnatural way, even with Fritz’s enthusiastic coaching, but then all at once my body took over, and I found that no thought
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_015.jpg	was required to maintain the driving pace and rhythm. It was as if I had broken free from gravity and settled into an orbit:
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_016.jpg	the big deep breaths just came, automatically.
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_017.jpg	Now I felt an uncontrollable urge to move my legs and arms in sync with the pounding of the drums, which resonated in my
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_018.jpg	rib cage like a powerful new heartbeat. I felt possessed, both my body and my mind. I can’t remember many thoughts
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_019.jpg	except “Hey, this is working, whatever it is!” I was flat on my back yet dancing wildly, my arms and legs moving with a will
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_020.jpg	of their own. All control of my body I had surrendered to the music.
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_021.jpg	It felt a little like speaking in tongues, or what I imagine that to be, with some external force taking over the mind and body
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_022.jpg	for its own obscure purpose. There wasn’t much visual imagery, just the naked sensation of exhilaration, until I began to
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_023.jpg	picture myself on the back of a big black horse, galloping headlong down a path through a forest. I was perched up high on
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_024.jpg	its shoulders, like a jockey, holding on tight as the beast scissored its great muscles forward and back with each long stride.
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_025.jpg	As my rhythm synced with that of the horse, I could feel myself absorbing the animal’s power. It felt fantastic to so fully
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_026.jpg	inhabit my body, as if for the first time. And yet because I am not a very confident rider (or dancer!), it also felt precarious,
test/images/synth_doc_00196_line_027.jpg	as if were I to miss a breath or beat I might tumble off.I had no idea how long the trance lasted, time was utterly lost on
test/images/synth_doc_00195_line_000.jpg	To be sure, the changes in the meditators were not as strong nor as long-lasting as the structural brain patterns unique to
